O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, dear sons, I have completed this book for you which contains the principles and the fullness of the medical sciences, and have ended it with explanations and clarifications.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is, "surgery."
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the practice of surgery is forbidden in our region and is banned everywhere, the science has perished and been cut off, and nothing remains of it except for small descriptions in books by ancient authors which have been handled by hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And because of this, errors and falsehoods have arisen, and understanding has been closed off and the science has been driven away.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I wish to compile together the organization of this treatise following the order of exposition and explanation and abbreviation; and I will compile together the forms of the fire-making tools for cautery, as well as the other instruments of the craft with the addition of explanation and preparation as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no skilled craftsmen of the hands are found in our time, the art of medicine has declined.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for one who practices (medicine) to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen said, so that they know precisely about the members, their forms and connections and separations, and have knowledge of the bones and nerves and veins and the number of arteries, and their movement and repose, and where they originate.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And so Hippocrates said that the name is much with the name, and little with the work; and it is the same in the art of hands. (Meaning that the reputation or name of a surgeon or physician may be great, but their actual skills and abilities are what truly matter)
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book, that whoever is not knowledgeable about the previously mentioned things, should be careful not to fall into error and not to kill men; as I have seen many times with those who meddle in this science and abandon themselves without knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish surgeon who lanced an abscess of scrofula on a woman's neck and cut the arteries of the neck, so that so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in her hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another surgeon who treated a stone in a man's bladder, and the stone was large, and he removed a piece of the bladder along with it, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to see him (the patient) and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and I knew well that if he operated on him, he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And see one other doctor who took in charge a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break, there was a wound; and the ignorant doctor tightly binds the break over the wound with splints, and did not leave any bandage at the wound, and he left it like this for a while; and he ordered him not to loosen it; and it remained so until the leg became swollen and the foot became gangrenous.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and unbind his leg; and when I had undone it, he was calm and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But in any case, the corruption had already set in the limb, and I could not heal it; and the corruption continued to spread through the limb until it was completely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see one other doctor who ruptured an enlarged abscess, and then inflamed it further through the malice of his treatment.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	Because when a chancre is pure of melancholic humor, it should not be touched with iron unless it is in such a place that all corrupt matter can be completely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And so, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: that is, work where there is danger in many dispositions; and I will point out in every part of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	 For which reason it is necessary that you take caution, so that foolish doctors cannot speak ill of you; Take up your arms in haste, and approach your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best method so that through the grace of God, you come to safety and are praised; and leave behind terrifying diseases with great care; and remove your weapons from those who make you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	 Galen says in one of his admonitions: "Do not take on the care of a serious illness, lest you be called a foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	 I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about cauteries of fire and medical caustics, and this chapter is arranged from head to toe; and the forms of instruments, and the iron tools for cauterization, and all that is necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cupping glasses and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter is arranged and includes the forms of instruments.[](https://french.stackexchange.com/)
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and sprains, and similar conditions, and it covers the entire body from head to toe, as well as the forms of instruments. This passage indicates that the chapter provides instructions for treating injuries such as dislocated joints and twisted limbs using surgical tools.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	So that we may remember the work, it is necessary for me to describe the qualities of care and the harmfulness of each temperament. This passage suggests that the text will discuss how different bodily temperaments (e.g., sanguine, phlegmatic) respond to medical treatment and the potential risks associated with treating patients of certain temperaments.[2](https://french.stackexchange.com/a/50136)
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of help, and harm, are the longest in word and the most subtle in science and hidden knowledge; and of this, many sages spoke and agreed to it; and I am not satisfied with their words, because I fear their length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the cautery helps universally for all complexions where there is matter, except for two complexions: namely, the hot complexion without matter, and the dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the hot and dry complexion together with matter, some have divided and said that the cautery is of great help there; and others have said the opposite: that the cautery is not worth anything for the illness that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to cure a disease caused by heat and dryness; and those who say the opposite claim that the cautery provides great help for a hot and dry illness that arises in the body of humans.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the human body and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body to be cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And yet, it should not be meddled with by anyone other than the one who has experienced it and is knowledgeable about the chapter of cauteries, as well as the diversity of human complexions, dispositions, and causes of their illnesses, and their outcomes and the season; we are not afraid of other complexions, even those that are cold and moist.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians gathered together and agreed on the use of the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that a fire cautery is also one of the surgical instruments of treatments, and of greater virtue than a caustic medical cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple and does not spread beyond the member that is burned, and does not harm any other member unless it happens to do so.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	 Hot medicines come from one member to another while spreading, and they bring illnesses to the affected limb that are difficult to cure; and perhaps fever, due to its intensity and the quality of its substance, does not cause this, unless there is an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found through experience and the length of time spent in service and studying the art, and it is based on the truth of things; and therefore I excuse myself for the length of my speech, for it does not please me to take away from you the secret that is hidden within fire, and its quality of work, how it drives out illnesses from bodies, as philosophers have said in their demonstrations. Now receive this in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on what time cauteries should be performed, and chose priests.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that a cautery is appropriate in all cases, because harmful effects arising from it are minimized by the use of the cautery; and similarly, even if cauterization causes pain, it is necessary to perform quickly without delay, before greater harm comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear son, as foolish people do; for a disease healed by cauterization does not return, and they say so; but it is not what they think, because a cautery is not merely a medicine that changes the complexion, but rather it dries up the humors that cause pain, and works more quickly than other medicines due to its power and authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	It is possible that a disease may come at times according to the complexion of the patient and the location and nature of the disease; and excessive fluids accumulate in him due to the consumption of foods and similar things, unless cauteries are administered where there is little excess fluid and moisture, such as cauterization with hot irons for pain, and similar things. In this case, the pain does not return, but it happens infrequently.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cautery is called the "last resort" of medicine, but this is indeed the case; however, they do not believe that cautery can be effective after other treatments, but their belief is false. The reason cautery is called the "last resort" of medicine is because when we administer methods of cure for a disease and they are not effective, we then administer cauterization, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it becomes clear that cautery is the "last resort" of medicine, and not in the way foolish doctors think.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cautery with an instrument of gold is more gentle than iron, and they only said this because of the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance. They also said that the place of cauterization does not cause gangrene, but this is not true as I have experienced. However, they were correct in saying that gold cautery is more effective than iron, just as they claimed.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet, when heating an instrument of gold, you cannot be sure when it is hot enough because the color of gold does not change much, and it can quickly cool down again. Additionally, if it is heated too much, it may become brittle and break in the fire. Thus, there are many difficulties with using a gold cautery instrument.[/] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And so we make use of the fire cautery, which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	I have arranged this chapter on wounds from head to toe, so that the way may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	olive cautery (referring to a type of cauterization)
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moistness and coldness in the brain, and there are two types that are made for a disease called "soda" (possibly epilepsy) and for many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, and for an abundance of dreams, pain in the teeth and throat, and also for all illnesses that come from coldness, such as paralysis and numbness and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient must be purged with a cleansing medicine, clearing the head for three or four nights, depending on what the virtues (strength), water and habits of the patient can bear; and then heat up the patient's head.[Source](https://www.perseus.tufts.edu/hopper/text?doc=Perseus%3Atext%3A2007.04.0059%3Asid%3D186)
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on something heavy; then place the base of your palm on the base of his nose between his two eyes; and where your middle fingers come, bleed a little and then heat the cautery called "olivare," which looks like this:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the mark made with ink, and make a small wound while pulling downward and outward with your hand; then quickly remove your hand and look at the mark to see if you see a hole as small as a pin; and if you do not see it, reapply the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; then take a little bit of salt and put it in warm water and soft cotton, and place it on the mark and leave it for three days; then apply a wet cloth soaked in butter and leave it on until the heat is gone; then treat the wound with the "tetrafarmaçon" ointment until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said that the longer a wound remains open, the more it purges; and because of this, movement helps.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of them said that one should let the cautery burn long enough that a part of the bone is burnt, and then remove what has been burnt from the bone and have it treated.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say that one should leave the cautery for a while, and apply it strongly enough that it makes a hole as large as a buckle that women put in their shoes so that the humors may come out; and one should leave the wound open for a long time; after that, one should clean and close it.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem good to me at all, except in certain men where there is a cause for fear; and it seems to me that I should leave them; for the head is weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we have witnessed in other members; and even when the head of the patient is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is more healing and powerful for me, and I use this one to bring about a cure.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When there is chronic pain coming all over the head, and it lasts for a long time, then the patient should use ear irrigation and pills which are called "cochie", and purgatives for the head and eyes and plasters; and if one applies the cautery that we have previously mentioned, but it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's head( chin?) is strongly tilted, and that it is not too cold; then cauterize beneath it a little as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After that, make a cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and make a mark or sign on the spot called "vasselz"; it is a spot where cups are placed; and keep your hand light so you don't touch the bone; the patient will feel more pain in this cautery than in others, and I will talk about that later; and the cauteries on the horns should be thinner than those used to cauterize the middle of the head, and that is the method.
dou cautere dou chief	of the head cautery.
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When there is sudden pain in a part of the head and it extends to the eye, and the area around the eye has been purged with cleansing medicines, and other cures have been applied as I mentioned in the classification of illnesses, but they are of no help; then two methods of cautery should be used, namely medicinal cauterization and surgical cauterization.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The medical cautery of medicine is as follows: take a piece of elder, remove the bark and soak it in a little wine for two days, then make an incision where the pain is, in such a way that you can place the piece of elder under the skin; and when it is placed, bind and tighten it well and leave it for twelve hours; then unbind and take out the piece of garlic, and leave the wound like this for two or three days; then put a compress soaked in butter on it until it heals.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish, use some of the burning medicines that I have written about in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	 The fire cautery is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 Heat the cautery until it reaches the shape described here:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the tip of the cautery is shaped like a bell with one curve and a small point in the middle; place it on the painful area and hold your hand and turn the cautery slightly for a short time, until half of the thickness of the skin is burnt; then lift your hand so that the artery below, which is behind, does not burn, causing an abundant flow of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Afterward, put cotton in the wound covered with silk, and keep it there for three days; then put wet cotton smeared with butter, and then cure the wound with ointment until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this pimple with the cautery called "cultellare," at its entire tip, and be careful not to cover the artery in this pimple which is not old.
de emigraine	of a pimple/swelling. The word "emigraine" here likely refers to a small growth or swelling on the skin.
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat a pimple/swelling as we have previously said in the divisions of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cautery of fire does not suffice, then you must heat the "cultellare" cautery until it is white; and similarly pass it over the painful place once, and remove your hand, and press so that you do not cover the artery and reach the bone; and watch out for the mandible which moves when one chews, and the nerve does not move and spasms do not come to the patient, and be careful of bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or if they have great fear and even the same for those who are not knowledgeable and experienced; and leave the work half-done; but I will tell you how one stops blood flow when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it fits in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauteries do not suffice for the disease and the patient is tolerant, then cauterize it in the head as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery which has two blades; and this cautery is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ears from part coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes to the ear from coldness, and medical liquids and other cures as we have mentioned in the division have been tried but the pain persists, then heat this "pointed" cautery, of which the form is as follows:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After, point all around the affected ear, or around both if the pain persists in both, and move back a bit from the root of the ear after making your mark; and have ten points around each ear; then heal the area until it is healed.[WATU type="translation" format="plaitixt">
de la torture de la bouche	of the affliction/torture of the mouth.
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Afflictions of the mouth that should be treated with cautery are only those that involve an excess of fluid, as we have mentioned in the divisions of diseases; and do not apply cautery to similar afflictions that come from dryness or nerve spasms.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this type of torture which moves with fluid from purging of the head and gargling, and if that is of no use, then you should cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the base of the ear, another a little behind the temple, and the third on the joint of the two lips; and place the cautery on the part which appears healthy, and cauterize next to the head of the ear a little above and below the ear horn, and another on the temple as long as a thumb; and leave the cautery in place until half of the heart is burned; and this is the form of the cautery.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And this is the appearance of the cutting instrument that we have mentioned before, but it is slightly more subtle and requires that the knife be a little larger; after curing the wound as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and there is no improvement and the patient has no fever, then perform four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one at the top of the head, and one in the place called "vasselz" as we have mentioned before, and the last cautery at the mouth of the stomach; and treat it as we have said before.
de litargie	The term "litargie" is a variant spelling of "litharge," which was a type of medicine made from lead oxide that was used in the Middle Ages to treat various conditions such as skin diseases, ulcers, and eye inflammations. It could be applied topically or taken internally. The exact recipe for making litharge varied, but it typically involved heating lead ore or lead metal with vinegar or another acid to create a powder or paste. Litharge was also known by other names such as "ceruse" and "lead white." However, the use of litharge in medicine declined over time due to concerns about its toxicity, particularly its potential to cause lead poisoning. Modern medical treatments no longer include litharge.
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this ailment, give the patient large quantities of purifying pills for the brain; then thoroughly comb the patient's hair and apply on the back of the head the plaster of sinapis (mustard seed) that is written in the treatise on plasters; this is the method of fire cautery: perform as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is healed in this way, it is good; and if not, perform three cauteries along the top of the head down to the neck, with a space of two fingers between each cautery; and treat it as you would other wounds, and if you see fit to adjust, and the patient is tolerant, perform one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, two others on the two temples, and continue treatment until healed; and let the cautery used be called "olivare", as I have previously mentioned.
de la froidor dou chief	of the chilliness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	The head must be purified with pills and the things previously mentioned; then thoroughly comb the patient's hair, then perform cautery on the top of the head and on each temple, and one at the back and three along the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is tolerant, and the illness is severe, if necessary, perform four cauteries along the spine of the back; and let it heal until the deepest part of the burn has dried up, then remove your hand; then treat it until healed, and use the type of cautery called "olivare" that I previously mentioned.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and first, the brain must be cleaned of mucus and other cures that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is large and able to take medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot tolerate it, have them perform gargling and chewing to clean the brain frequently with good meats; then apply a poultice to the head, and make one cautery as we have said before, and one on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the patient is strong and able to tolerate it, make cauteries as I have said for those with paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be made of olive oil in the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, make one subtle cautery in this way:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When, due to melancholy, superfluities or corrupt moisture cause thick phlegm, then use such cautery as we have said for someone who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if, due to melancholy, the superfluities tend towards melancholy and the body of the patient is moist, then give him to drink something that purifies the brain, according to what has been previously divided (explained).
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, wash the patient's head; then make a well-made linen compress, like a circle, and place it on the head; and have the patient lie crossways, and keep it tightly in place from all sides; then apply the liniment, warmed with old bean butter; and heat it over moderate fire, so that the patient can bear it; then empty the circle inside the head, and let it cool down; and do this to the patient once a week with other good treatment until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	 Or if you want to cauterize by making multiple points with the entire cautery.[Comment: Here, "poins" means "marks made by burning." The text is suggesting that multiple burn marks can be made over the affected area for treatment.]
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	 This method of cautery moistens the brain a lot; and then put a cotton soaked in butter and chicken fat on top.[Comment: Here, "amoistit le cerveil" may refer to the fact that cauterization was believed to draw out blood and moisture from the affected area. The text suggests using butter and chicken fat as an ointment for the wound after cauterization.][Note: I am a language model and my translations should be used as a guide and not as definitive or professional medical advice.
