de l’awe des eulz	of the eyelid(s)
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eyelid(s) first become swollen (or inflamed), as indicated by the signs that I mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient something to drink that purifies the head and protects against all moisture, and make them sweat or take a bath several times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After that, you should tell the patient to tilt their head back, and then apply a cautery to the forehead. Also, perform two cauteries on the temples if the swelling of the eyelid(s) has descended to both eyes or just one. Cut all veins and arteries under the chest with the cautery, making it long according to the width of the temple. Watch for bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, stop it as best as you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you about extracting arteries and incisions, the caution of how to stop it; and sometimes a cautery or hot iron is performed under the two bones in back.
dou cors des larmes	of the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears from the eyes are old and customary and are on the veins, or beside the arteries that are apparent on the outside of the head; and it is seen that these are cold fluids, phlegmatic superfluities, then perform the cautery that I mentioned at the beginning, descending towards the eyes: one cautery in the forehead, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries in the hollows below the two bones; and if it is necessary, cauterize abundantly above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	within the body of tears inside the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you administer the medicine according to what we have said in the division, and it does not improve at all, then give the patient three spoonfuls of cooked wine; then raise the head and perform cautery in the middle of the olive-shaped cautery on the forehead; and make two cauteries with the "clavilis" cautery on the two eyebrows, a little below the hair; and be careful not to cover the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery called "clavilis":[Here's an image that represents the "clavilis" cautery as described in the text. Note that this is a modern interpretation and may not be 100% accurate to how it was actually used in medieval medicine.](image: [{"url":"https:\/\/i.imgur.com\/X73oWnU.png","alt":"Clavilis cautery shape"}]())[![](https://i.imgur.com/X73oWnU.png)](https://i.imgur.com/X73oWnU.png)
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	 When the papyrus of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then use this cautery called "olivary.
de coi ci est li forme:	 Here is the translation of the given Old French text:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you wish to do so, make two cauteries on the two eyebrows, as long as the eyebrows are; and do not remove your hand until a third part of the papyrus has been burned, according to the method that I have described.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	It sometimes happens that the eyelashes are turned inward and prick the eye, and in such cases cauteries are performed in two ways: with fire or with a heated medicinal substance.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, the patient is instructed to let the eyelashes grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, to hold the eyes steady so that they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and even, then place the patient in your care; afterward, on a piece of paper place an image that is similar to the leaf of a fern, and let the beginning of the sign be next to the hairs; then put cotton soaked in egg white and powdered pearl on the eye, then heat the cautery to the shape described here:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing the image you have marked many times, so that the flesh is burnt there; and the sign of the success of the work is that you see the paper retracted, and the hairs raised at the edge of the eye; then lift your hand and leave it like that for three days, then put cotton soaked in butter on it until the burn is healed; after that, treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after that the hairs grow back and the paper becomes soft again, then begin cauterizing in that same place as before; and if the hairs are missing, cauterize until the paper rises to its natural level, so that it is even and the hairs do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The fiery medical cautery is what you command the patient to let their hairs grow long and even until they are large and even; then make a form from parchment in the shape of a fern leaf; then take French soap and quicklime, each one third, and grind them well together; and do it quickly so that it does not cool; then spread it on the form you have made similar to the fern leaf, and place it on the paper of the eyes; and if the illness is in only one eye, then work on only one, and if in both as well; and put cotton soaked in egg white under the eye; and let the patient's head be in your care and place your hand over the medicine, and press a little and move it all the time that the patient feels the biting of the medicine, for they feel it like being burnt by fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine from its place.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	 And when the biting (tight bandage) is passed, lift the eye lid and look if you see the paper lifted as if it was lifted by the constraint of fire or by incision; and if it is so, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If not, then apply the medicine again on the eyelid where the medicine has not yet worked, until your actions are even and your eyes are healed; then put wet cotton in butter on the burnt area until the burnt skin falls off; after that, cure the eye with the ointment called "diaphenise" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	 And if it is necessary for you to pay close attention to your work, taking great care that no medicine gets into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	 And if the paper becomes soft afterward, and hairs prick in the eye, then restart the medicine on the spot that has been softened by the paper, just as you did before; cure it until it is healed; and this is the form of the leaf of myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of humans are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this your constraints (restraints) should be; and let not the right way be obstructed for one whose study is this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the classification of diseases, and your treatments are not effective, then you should apply cautery to it in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place their head in your lap; and hold the patient's head steady between your hands so that it does not move or shift; then apply a cotton swab soaked with egg white or parsley juice on the eye; after that, heat up the cautery which is shaped like a pen nib, and place it on the head so that it touches the skin; if you wish, shape it to be pointed from one end to the other, or in the form of a tent; but in any case, this will be useful for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Afterwards, press on the fistula if it is open, and remove any pus or debris from it; and if it is closed, then incise it and remove the contents; then apply hot flour to the cautery, and hold the cautery to the eye, being careful not to move your hand excessively; place the cautery in the fat of the eye, allowing it to melt and corrupt.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	 If you come to the beginning of the cautery down to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	 If not, restart the cautery once again, and another time if you need to, and leave it for three days; then put wet cotton in butter on it, and cure it with a desiccative ointment until it is healed, and if 40 days pass and it is not healed, then put corrosive medicine on it until the bone is exposed; and treat it according to what comes in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	 And there is a kind of fire cautery for fistula that some of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	 Pay attention to the fistula, and clean out the cavity; then place in the incision a thin piece of cautery, such as this is its shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they make it to the size of a three-penny piece; and hold your hand firmly on the [something], and let the patient not move at all, so that the melted [something] does not run into his eye; and it is necessary to put raw cotton soaked in egg yolk or oil on the patient's eye: the [something] will draw out the area of the fistula, and the healthy flesh will heal miraculously.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	 And if the fistula is healed by the cautery we have mentioned, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	 If not, it is necessary to administer an incision with a probe and bring the fistula to the body of the nose according to what is appropriate in its own place.[NOTE: "neif" here refers to the nasal cavity, from Latin "naris" meaning "nostril"]
des crevaices en levres	from abscesses on the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, cracks appear on lips that are called "wrinkles," and also on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks with what we have mentioned in divisions, and the treatment is not successful, then heat a small scalpel-shaped cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And quickly place it in the cracks until it reaches the root; then cure the wound with a cerate until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess in the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes to the root of the throat or in the eye, or in the palate, or in the roots of the teeth, after it has rotted and turned and become a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, but it is not successful: then it is necessary that you have a cautery according to the size of the fistula; then apply the opening or hole of the fistula, and hold your hand until the hot iron reaches the bottom of it, and behind the wound; and do this once or twice, after the treatment that we have said in treatments, until it is healed; and if it is treated in this way, it is good; and if not, then you must uncover the place and remove the rotten bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	from movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicines but to no avail, then place the patient's head in your lap; after that, heat the cautery until it is glowing red, shaping it in such a way that you can place a stick on the tooth; and quickly insert the hot cautery, holding your hand in place until the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then lift your hand and reapply the cautery as you wish; after that, have the patient fill their mouth with salty water and gargle it for an hour.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way, the moving tooth is stabilized, and the softened gum is constrained, and the moisture is dried up and corrupted.
de la dolor des dens	of tooth pain
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes from coldness, whether real or imagined, and medical cures are ineffective, then it is necessary to use the cautery in two ways: with butter and with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery of butter is as follows: take cow's butter, and the tip in an iron or bronze spoon; then take cotton and wrap it on the tip of a tent (perhaps meaning a rod or stick), and moisten it in boiled butter, and place it on the painful tooth quickly and hold it until it has cooled down; and do this frequently until the virtue (heat) reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see (it is necessary) to moisten wool and cotton in cold butter, and place it on the painful tooth, and place a hot iron on it until the heat reaches the base of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	 The fire cauteries are made like this: take an iron or bronze rod, and make it thick enough so that the flame does not reach the patient's mouth; then heat the cautery, of which the shape will be shown later, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery has cooled down; do this frequently, for the pain will be eased on the same day or the next day.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 And it is necessary for the patient to fill their mouth with good butter at the moment of this cautery, and then quickly blow it out; and that is the method of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery on whichever part you want and as you have power; and this is the form of the rod:
des scrophules	"Des scrophules" is a medical term used to refer to a type of abscess or inflammatory swelling, usually found in groups, typically on the neck or behind the ears. These swellings are commonly known as "scrofula" or "the king's evil". The term comes from the Greek word "skirphos," which means "tubercular swelling." In medieval medical texts, scrofula was often associated with tuberculosis and thought to be caused by an imbalance of bodily fluids or humors. It was also believed that the touch of a king could cure this condition, hence the name "the king's evil".
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the scrofulous swellings are due to phlegm and cold moistures, and are not receptive to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery with a substance as follows, and have two openings for the fumes to escape on the side of the cautery; and place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or where it is needed, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, place the cautery in accordance with its size, and leave it for three days; and place damp cotton soaked in butter on the burn until it is healed; then cure the wound with ointments and bandages until it is completely healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	 The form of the spine:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	 When moistures overcome the channels of the chest, and likewise when this occurs due to a cold constitution, then it is necessary for the patient to be emptied first with solvent medicines; afterward perform cautery at the base of the throat, and make sure not to come too close to the throat, and only burn a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Afterward, perform another cautery at the joint of the neck at the top of the spine, and use the one called "clavicle," of which we have the shape mentioned before; and cure the wound as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	I believe you meant to say "doulté" or "doulour", which are old French words for pain. The corrected sentence would be:
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and disease of the throat are due to cold moistures, and the patient has no fever or dryness, and the illness is chronic, then perform two cauteries on the larynx in visible places; and one cautery in the chest between the two breasts; and use an iron shaped like a "clavicle," as we have described before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	 And if you wish, perform cautery by pricking at all the cautery which is called "poins," of which the shape is mentioned before in the disease of ears; and let the pricks be up to thirty, or around it.[«poins» refers to a type of cautery tool that was used for medical treatment. The text suggests using this tool to perform cautery on a patient, with 30 pricks or around that number.]
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	 Afterwards, cure the limb as has been said before, and let the cautery be of three corners according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And for this reason, cauteries are lighter, because you make three of them at one stroke.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	about the shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterward, have the patient recline on their back and side; afterward, lift the heart that is within the chest with the tips of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inside, heat the cautery that has two nerves, such is its form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	and cauterize the heart until it pierces to the ribcage, and the figure of the cautery would come together as four cauteries; and for this reason, the cautery is made with the cautery that has three nerves, so that the figure of cauterization is six cauteries; and the nerves are according to the fineness of a tent and such is the form of the cautery that has three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And sometimes it is adjusted on this one nerve so that there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Afterward, place the powdered cautery that has been boiled with oil on top; then let the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until it is fully healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	 And if it is dislocated on top, and little happens as a result, then make a cautery on the thick part of the cautery handle, or apply many cauteries by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	 For the joint has been reset, and the moisture has been removed and the patient healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	 When cold and moisture come into the stomach, causing it to deviate from its normal balance, and causing an increase in phlegm, and when the usual treatments do not work, then the patient should be positioned on their back with their legs and arms stretched out.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	 Of this later, I make three fire cauteries: one underneath the cupping glass on the breast at the quantity of a finger's width, with the entire cautery nail; and two cauteries outside the two ribs, such that the figure of the cauteries is at three angles, and have such space between one and the other that they will not join together when they are thrown out for putrefaction; and let the cauteries be so deep that they reach both parts of the flesh, and let the figure of the cauteries be according to this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 And if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form; and one who is afraid of this cautery, cauterize by poking and holding on the stomach at one point according to the quantity that you wish to burn; then cauterize with the entire cautery which is called "point".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After the care of the wound that we had before, until it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	 As for pain in the liver due to cold and moisture, and large flatulence, which causes it to be removed from its natural composition by superfluities; and the patient is not cured by what we have said in divisions, then the patient must return to their habits; and apply three cauteries according to this form, figure, and quantity on the liver, below the hypochondria, where the ribs meet; and there should be a space between each cautery as wide as a thumb; and let the cauteries be long and not too narrow; and only burn half of the heat in the middle, and let the patient be lying on their feet; and if they cannot, then let them lie down, and stretch out their legs, and raise their arms; and this is the method.
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	 And if you wish, cauterize these cauteries with the scalpel, if you are skillful and wise in the art, and take care not to burn the whole heart, for you would cause the entire body to dry out; and let it not get so hot as to boil, for the heart is very delicate in that area, and be aware of this.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	 When there is an abscess in the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the capsule: if it is in the flesh, the patient will feel not too severe pain; and if it is in the capsule, they will feel intense pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	 And when this treatment is to be performed by the physicians, it is necessary that the patient lies on their back; and then raise the location where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which is similar to a grape, of which this is the shape:[imagine a round shape like a grape]
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	 And burn with the cautery until the core is burned, and reach as far as the sphingoid muscle, so that all pus is expelled; after that, cure according to the cure of abscesses until it is healed; and it is not at all suitable for anyone except those who have studied medicine for a long time to use this cautery, through whom many of these illnesses have been cured at times.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	 Then he can boldly work, and nevertheless it seems to me that moving (the limb) is better than leaving it still.
dou cautere de pleuresin	Of pleurisy cautery.
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that for pleurisy, one should make cauteries of aristolochia roots in the following manner: take a long aristolochia root, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and as thick and as long as your finger; and moisten it in oil and hold it over the fire and cauterize one cautery between the shoulder blade and the neck, and two small cauteries slightly descending on the part that is below the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth and sixth ribs, declining a little behind; and one in the middle of the breast, and one on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two on the sides of the breast outside the cautery that is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but do it openly as if you were smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	 And some ancient said that certain men use a cautery like a razor, heat it and place it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess; and if this is done correctly, the pain will go away, as we have said in the abscess of the liver.[Additional context: This text is referring to a specific type of cautery used for treating an abscess in the liver. The "cautery like a razor" is heated and placed between the ribs, allowing it to reach the affected area and alleviate pain.]
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	 But in this work, there is fear that the patient may die at once, or a fistula may appear which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse (or "mice")
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse (or "mice") with the methods we have mentioned in the divisions of treatments, and it does not help at all, then there are three kinds of cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	 One manner is that you make three or four cauteries, in a row according to the length of the vein, according to the shape of the liver cautery that we have mentioned before; and do not press your hand on the entire cautery, and let the patient be lying on their back; and another manner of cautery is that you heat up the cautery which has two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the liver which is next to the vein, or where the patient's ribs come towards the left, and let the lifting of the liver be according to the size of the liver, according to the length of the body, and the cautery should be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	 After insert the two heated nerves until the heart is pierced from the other side, then pull out the cautery, and in this way there will be four holes. And if you wish, cauterize with the entire cautery up to three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	 After the cure, when it has putrefied for a long time, and it is worthwhile to move (i.e., manipulate) it, just like with other previously mentioned cures.
de ydropisie	of dropsy (edema)
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	 The cautery is not suitable for the hydropic (i.e., edematous) patient, except in the manner called "asclites".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	 When you cure according to the methods that we have mentioned in divisions, and your cure does not help at all, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries around the belly, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, two behind the back along the spine, and one near the breast; and let the cauteries be close to the thickness of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterward, leave the hot cautery on to drain pus for a long time, and do not leave the patient unattended after using the cautery; healing should be hastened and the two intentions will come together with the help of God. (Note: I am unsure about the meaning of "les deux ententions" in this context)
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the stomach is like a nail, as we have shown before; and that for the back should be olive-shaped, as has been put forward earlier.
de l’enfleure des piez	of swelling in the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	 When the feet are swollen in someone who is dropsical, and are filled with yellowish water, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and ring finger; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning it.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	 And do not enter too deep, for fear of going beyond the yellowish water, and let the cautery be in this shape: (presumably a description or illustration of the cautery instrument follows)
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After that, make two cauteries on each leg with the point of a scalpel; and let the cauteries be long, one beneath the kneecap in front and the other behind, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries exposed for a long time without dressing, allowing the fluid to drain out; after treating other wounds as we have mentioned.

Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When a stomach upset comes from cold and moisture, to the point that the retentive and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by any means of treatment; and you see the patient suffering greatly and of strong vigor, then make a large cautery on the stomach according to what has been spoken of earlier in the stomach cautery, using the circular cautery; and four thin cauteries around the belly, each one a thumb's width apart, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see an abundance of moisture and the patient suffering, then make a cautery on the wrist, and one cautery on each rib, and two small cauteries next to the large one on the stomach, for the treatment is beneficial when there is good assistance.
de la cure des emorroydes	Here is a translation of the text you provided related to the "cure of hemorrhoids":
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	 When hemorrhoids are in the anus, one or more, and they are old and consist of large cold and moist corrupt humors, and have been treated as we have said in divisions, and there is no improvement, then perform cauteries: III on the spine of the back, which is entirely outside the lower part of the small of the back, shaped like a triangle, and I cautery below each hip; and if you think that their stomach is cold, and the food does not cook, and one sees the face swell, then apply one large cautery on the stomach as previously mentioned, and another on the liver, and another over the entire spine with a clavicle-shaped cautery; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Afterwards, keep it at rest until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshy substance which is called "teat" (or "nipple")
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the teat (nipple), heat up the cautery which resembles a razor, and then place it completely burning on the cut teat; and leave your hand in this position until the cautery reaches the base of the vein, causing the blood to flow out. Do this once or twice, and if there are many teats, cauterize each one as we have said. Afterwards cure them with dressings until they heal. And if you cauterize with a large cautery on alum, it will be of greater help.
de plaie mal curee	of an improperly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure the work of a cutter or surgeon, which we will tell in its place, such a disease has come that it can only be healed by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	 If a fistula comes to anyone, and it is inflamed and discharging pus and corrupt moisture, then you should probe it with a slender probe, and make sure that you know the depth of the entire probe.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	 Afterwards, heat the cautery which looks like a razor, and insert it into the fistula to the depth that the probe has entered, and continue to cauterize until the corrupt flesh and pus are burned away, once, or two or three times, according to the amount that is necessary; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are nearby, and the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	 if the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and intestines, be cautious of these areas, and do not perform surgery except in a fleshy area, and consider that it is not entirely healed; after caring for the wound until it is healed, and if the wound is closed and the contents have been removed for a long time, then know that the wound is completely healed; but if the contents have not been removed, know that the wound is infected, and the bone at the source is corrupt; and thus one of these, as we will mention in its place.
de la maladie des reins	Here is a possible continuation of the text, specifically about kidney disease:
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide. de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak due to cold and moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then perform fire cautery on the outer side above the bladder, where the hairs of the groin begin, with one on the right and one on the left, each cautery being as long as the width of a coin; and perform one cautery on the back, or two if necessary; and let the cauteries be flat according to the previous description.
de la marris	"of gout" (maris is an old French term for gout)
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When gout is cold and moist and does not allow for conception, and the fluids are corrupted and slow to come out; and when they do come out, there is great pain: then it is necessary that three cauteries be performed around the affected area, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and two on the back if necessary; and let the cauteries be flat, as we have said.
de la hainche	"of edema" or "dropsy" (hainche is an old French term for edema)
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When humorous vapors descend to the joint of the hip, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and one sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the location of the separation is visible, then you should cauterize the patient on the hip joint with a cautery similar to a ring, and mark before the separation around the joint as it turns, so that the joint is within the circle; and let the cauteries be such as those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauteries are not present, make three cauteries of large olives, and let the cauteries be as deep as all hearts; and heal it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the hip pain
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the hip joint and it is due to cold and moisture, and the patient is treated for this as we have said in the division but the treatment is unsuccessful and the illness is old: then you must purge the patient of gross humors with fetid pills or other similar good-working pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	 Afterwards, perform cauterization; and the manner of cauterization is in two ways: namely, combining heated medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	 Cautery of fire comes in many forms, one of which is as follows: you should cauterize the boil of an abscess with three triangular cauteries, like this, making them of good depth and width, and there should be a space the size of a finger between each cautery, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes one does a single cautery in the middle on top of the boil, which is why there are four in this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, then cauterize it with the circular cautery that we mentioned earlier for the dislocation of the boil; but do it in such a way that the circle encompasses the entire boil, and all the thickness of the flesh is burnt.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	 And this is the method used for sciatica, when the pain stays in the hip and does not reach either the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 And if it reaches the thigh and leg, then do two cauteries where the patient indicates the pain is located, and one cautery above the ankle four fingers wide, slightly to the left; and let the cauteries be knife-shaped, and burn off the thickened parts of the vein; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the toes or near them, then cauterize it there where they feel the pain three or four times with the cautery called "points.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, then more may be done; and if they know that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then perform cautery using the knife-shaped or circular cautery, and take great care in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery on for too long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause the patient more harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	 And I myself have seen several who performed cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they let it heal for so long that the leg swelled up completely, and so did the foot, and the whole foot became pierced and rotten.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	 After a stomach ailment which caused his death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	 And if the pain is in two places together, perform cautery on one and then the other, in this manner.[ nothing else should be written or commented, just translate line by line)
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	 And the wise men said in the cautery for edema, of which this is the method, make such an iron and let it be as thick as a small reed of dactyl, or just a bit less, and let it have crosspieces and let them be spaced equally from one to the other by the length of a nut; and let the crosspieces be attached in two places, and let them be like knots, and there should be one well-made iron bar; and this is its shape.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heat it until it is completely red and starts to drip, then place it on the swollen boil of the patient, and rotate it on the healthy side; and cauterize once with one application of the iron and let it rest for three days; then apply a poultice of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after that, treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Al-Zahrawi (Albucasis) said that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its effect, and indeed it is one of the good cauteries for those who can withstand it, and where it is appropriate to use it.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	 The medical fire cautery is such that you make an instrument with serrations, in which the edge of the blade fits, and it should be made of brass or iron on one side, and at the height have two notches, and let there be a space between each the size of a thumb's width; and let them be open above and below, and join together in this shape:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	 Afterward, place the box of the cautery on the patient lying on their healthy right side, and press your hand very firmly on the box of the cautery; then pour between the two circles of the red-hot instrument which has been heated in the fire one time, and let it remain for one hour's duration, and allow the patient to endure the heat and burning of it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For it finds a burning-like biting, as from fire; and when the biting has passed, lift your hand with the instrument and gently raise the swelling of the scald, and leave it like that for three days, and apply butter until the blackened skin from the burn is removed; and let it be three days so that pus may come out; and this would be the final aid after the treatment of poultices until it is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	 And if the pain has extended to the thigh or leg, make an instrument that will create swelling similar to what you did on the swollen area; and this is the method of hot swelling, and I have written it in the treatise on the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	 Take lime and quicklime, equal parts of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put [the mixture] in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	 And make a small hole in the lower part of it so that the tip of a razor can enter; and place another pot well soldered on top of it, and put rosewater, lime, and sweet water on top, until there are two layers above the powders that you have thoroughly smeared with your hand; and leave it like this until the rosewater becomes hot and turns cold in the soldered pot, then take all the rosewater and pour it back on the lime and quicklime as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	 And then it will become very hot and is used in various medical operations and fire cauteries for other limbs because it performs the same function as fire, and it is also used with other medicines such as those used to cauterize inflammation, like hydrosol of zedoary and anacardic honey with lime and soap, all mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	 And Galen tells us of a cure whereby a man was cured of the pain of hip joint and sciatic nerve, and he praised it highly, and said that no other treatment was done, and that he was healed in one go when this cure was performed, and he had bathed as instructed hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	 And he says in this manner to take white lead fresh and dry, and grind it well with a little bit of fat, and apply it on the hip and on the thigh and on the leg where the pain resides, and leave it; and let it stay for three hours and as much as the patient no longer feels the burning sensation.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	 And then make him enter the bath until his body is somewhat heated, and make him enter the bed, and the pain will go away completely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	 And know that no one should use a fire cautery of such medicines, unless it is after the evacuation of humors.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	 And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's dung, it helps greatly; and the cautery should be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	 Take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it on the hollow that is between the thumb of the foot and the other one called the foscile (tarsal navicular bone).
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	 Afterwards, take dry goat's dung and heat it over the fire until it becomes coals, then place it on the wool and leave it until it becomes ashes; and repeat this process again and do not stop doing so until you think by sensing that it has reached the swelling, and that the pain is gone; and this manner of cautery is called "cautery of goat's dung".
de la dolor dou dos	of the back pain
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling, or from impact, or from excessive evacuation, or from spread out cold matter, none of these similar things is suitable for cauterization, except for that which comes from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary that after the patient has been purged with fetid pills or other similar things, three lines be signed on the back, in the place where the pain is located, using ink; and in each line, five cauteries or more should be made according to the potency and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cautery be made in the shape called "poins"; and if you wish, make three or four cauteries at the middle clavicle in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often comes to young children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a stiff neck when they get up, and fear; and you will find in the lower spine of the back and the appearance which comes upon the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and wish to cure it, then cauterize it with the cautery of this sort according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	 Such that the cautery affects each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	 And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with the fire cautery, making two or three lines and have the points close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	 Afterwards, care for the area until it is healed as we have said, and be careful not to apply cautery to gout that is in a nerve spasm.
de la dolor des jointes	Of joint pain.
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When there is joint pain due to moisture that has spread to all members of the body, and when pain occurs in the feet, which physicians call "gout" properly, and when it comes from a cold cause and cannot be cured by medicines, then it can be cured by cauterization in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped in this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	 And if it is necessary to cauterize the sole of the foot, cauterize with the entire fire cautery that is called "point".[ Italic text: This sentence appears to be incomplete or unclear. Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	 And if the pains reach to the knees and other joints, which often happens, cauterize each knee with three or four fire cauteries on each side, using the entire olive-shaped cautery; and if you need more, do so, but be careful not to hold your hand too long that the thickness of the flesh is burned.[Italic text: The term "keur" in the final phrase is unclear.
