Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	 And if the pains descend down to the knee and the back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	 And if the pains are in the arms, make incisions around the wrist two lines deep; and if there is no more pain, make incisions on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the wrists or shoulders, cauterize each part, and provide good care for the patient and give them medicine.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	 For if you take good care of them and purge phlegm, they will heal with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the opening (incision) of the syphilis sore
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When an abscess comes to a head and the intestines descend to the hips and it is recent, then when you see it needs to be cured, they must not eat that day; and they should use things that lighten the belly so that the feces come out of their stomach. Afterwards make them sit on their back between your hands and command them to hold their breath until the abscess has been retracted, and massage it with your fingers, and apply pressure underneath the opening above the bone of the wrist, and in a straight line that is half the size of a circle above the body. Then heat up the cautery iron until it is red hot, which looks like this: [The text includes a symbol for fire or the cautery iron.]
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	 until it is white and produces pus.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	 Then return the bowels to their place; and the assistant places his hand so that they do not return backward; and work well the thighs of the patient, and place a cushion and a servant beneath the thighs, and another on the stomach who holds the hands; then place the cautery on the sign with your entire hand, and hold it directly and firmly until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again until you reach the bone; and be careful that the bowels do not protrude when you use the cautery; so that you do not burn him; and so that through this, the patient does not die, or suffer other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	 And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	 And it is necessary that the cautery for children be fine, according to the size of an egg, and for adults also as large according to their measure; after three days cure the wound of the cautery with butter until the burn is removed; after curing other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his bandages be left on long enough, so that the boils do not come out when he moves to get up.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	 And after forty days, when he wants to get up, have a well-made belt ready for him and let him wear it for another forty days; and have good rest, that he does not exert himself much and guards against excessive consumption of drink and food, and high voices; and when he follows this instruction, he will be fully healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	 And I will tell hereafter the cure of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of abdominal surgery
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	 When ruptures come in other bellies and are recognized, and you see that they do not grow anymore, perform the fire cautery with the reusable cautery according to its quantity, and let one third of the belly be burnt; then cure according to what we have said; and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a three-pointed cautery in this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	 but first mark the place of the rupture and make a line along its width above it, and another below it, and hold your hand in the middle of the entire cauterizing area.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	 But the first fire cautery is lighter and sharper.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in some limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	 When pain comes to any limb, either from falling or injury, and this pain lasts for a long time, and medical care is of no use, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the "poins" cautery, and let the cautery be according to the length of the member and its smallness and weakness and its virtue and its location of twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	 If it is healed from the first cautery, that is good; if not, begin another cautery on top of it, for it is often the case that it must change to the member that is near it, therefore you must make the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of leprosy.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	 The measles are sometimes helped by cautery with great benefit, and likewise the diseases that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	 If you wish to cauterize the wound, be vigilant and check if the illness is at its beginning, and if it can be cured following what has been said in the division (treatment plan). And may it not descend or remain (fester), and should you doubt that corruption (infection) might spread throughout the patient's body, then perform two cauteries on the head: one near the forehead at the hairline, and the other at the back of the head; and two at the temples, and one in the middle of the skull; and leave your hand steady so that the cauterizing iron may reach the bone, and so that any blistered skin may come off, allowing the vapors of the bodily humors to escape; and cauterize the wound as it appears.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the sickness is spread everywhere and it is clearly lost, then you should cauterize it with the cauteries that we have mentioned in the head, and one cautery on the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the haunch and another next to it, and two on the shoulders; and two on the ribs, and two on the groins of the chest, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are at the back of the heels; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the wrist, and one on the bone of the stomach, and one on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	 And know that the more I do with fire cautery, the more help I provide, and movement increases its benefit; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as a healthy person would, because the body is already completely corrupt.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	 And the cautery should be large or small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you find in the ways of iron instruments.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	 Afterwards, apply to it a mixture of bran flour and honey, along with other remedies, until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When swelling comes to any limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, but is not healed, then cauterize the limb according to its size; and let the cauterization be a little into the thickness of the flesh; then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	 And sometimes, cautery is done on the hand and foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the member, and in this way, swelling is removed; yet no one should meddle with it if they are not knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the nerves moving the body.

Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" has woken up and the means of medicine are worth nothing, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deep, according to the amount of flesh, until the whiteness is removed and the color changed; then cure it with bran of vetch and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of dove and almond, each one part; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and expose it to air until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of chancre (a type of skin ulcer) with cautery involves using a hot iron or other heated instrument to burn and destroy the infected tissue. This was a common medical practice in the Middle Ages as it was believed to remove the corrupt humors and promote healing. After cauterization, the wound would be cleaned and dressed with various medicinal substances such as herbs, oils, and powders to help prevent infection and promote healing. The specific method of cautery used for chancre may have varied depending on the severity of the ulcer and the practitioner's preference.
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	 When a chancre first appears and you wish to stop it, cauterize it with a cautery that forms a circle, all around the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	 And yet the doctors say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the chancre; but this does not seem good to me, for I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen this happen before; and a more appropriate thing is that it be cauterized around, with a "circular" cautery, as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot spread
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	 When someone has an illness called "adubelati", and it delays in killing or due to the excess it creates, or due to the water of the sick person when they are infirm (that is, too old) and have little blood, or due to time; and you wish to hasten its death: then cauterize around with many small cauteries by pricking; leave it like that after.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	 because it will hurry up and die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you wish to pierce it with the entire cautery, heat the cautery like this: [shape of the cautery is not provided in the text].
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	 And place your hand in the middle of that illness called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the core, and make such cauteries that the patient feels them outside in such a way that the course of the gangrene is alleviated.[note] It's unclear what exactly the text means by "allegis" here. I translated it as "alleviated," but it could also mean something like "shortened" or "reduced".[/
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 After the care until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the healing by fire using iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	 Another kind of illness exists which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing but a wasting of the limb, for it consumes the limbs just as fire consumes dry logs.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	 If you see this illness in a place that can tolerate cautery with fire, then heat the cautery pin very lightly and strongly, according to where the illness is; after that, cauterize all around until you reach all of the corruption, and let nothing of it remain, so that everything corrupt be removed.[`learn more about old french to english translation`](https://www.the-north-way.com/old-french-to-english-translation/)
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	 And then let it (the wound) be for three days, and place soft bandages with oil on the cauterized areas until the burns from the fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	 After treating (the wound) with ointments causing the flesh to grow.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	 And if after three days you see that healthy flesh is not growing, that's good; and if not, then repeat the cautery on the areas that remain corrupt.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	 And this condition has sometimes been cured with medication instead of fire cautery; however, fire cautery is of greater help. I have already mentioned the cure for the ailment using medication in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of fungi that come between the toes
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	 Much of the time, at the feet arises a disease called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large swollen thing that hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	 And the cauteries for this disease are of two kinds.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	 That is to say, cautery of fire, and cautery of hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	 Cautery of fire is: heat a cauterizing iron as if it were a pen of rooster, and make sure it is made of good iron, of the size that can touch the nail from all sides, and it should have thin edges; then place it very hot on the nail, and turn your hand around the nail until you reach the base of the nail; leave it like this for three days until it begins to rot; then make a plaster with crushed mallows with oil, and leave the plaster on all night, and the nail will fall off and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then cure the wound with a hot compress until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	 And if they are turned inward by the body, which often happens in hands and feet, then you should apply hot water cautery. Here's how: take an iron or copper rod, or a chicken wing bone, and place it on the nail and apply althea (an herb) and garlic cloves. Place the rod so that it surrounds completely, then add some hot water and hold your hand tightly, pressing down while turning the rod until the edge of the rod reaches the base of the nail and the hot water can penetrate deeply to the root. Have the patient endure the bite of the hot water for an hour; then leave it as is and it will come out by itself with all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	 Do one after the other, until you have bled all those in the body, then cure the inflammations that cause flesh to grow.
li cure dou trembler	The treatment for trembling.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone is trembling from cold nerves or quartan fever or any other cause, then you should apply four or five cauteries to them on the spine at the base of the neck, one cautery between each vertebra; and one cautery on the affected area (pez) and one on the stomach using an olive-shaped cautery. This will stop the trembling and speed up recovery from the cold disease.[br]
des pustules puans	of stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	 Sometimes it happens that the body appears with hollows or foul-smelling pustules, which come from large amounts of corrupted matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	 When they first appear, it is necessary to apply a hot cautery to each pustule: using a thin rod of myrtle wood, with the tip heated in fire, or with a root of aristolochia, or with a round-shaped cautery.[br] Note: A cautery is a surgical tool used to burn the skin and tissue to stop bleeding or destroy diseased tissue. The text recommends using a thin rod made from myrtle wood or aristolochia root, both of which have been historically used for medicinal purposes. A lenticular cautery refers to a small, round-shaped cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	 And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow any further, but the excesses from which they come are broken off, and they are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when an artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	It often happens that there is a large loss of blood from the artery that is cut in an injury or incision of an abscess, or in the cauterization of a limb, and similar things; and it is very difficult to stop the bleeding.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, when this happens to someone, you must quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein and press very hard until the bleeding stops under your finger and no more blood comes out; then heat various sized olive-shaped cauters over the fire until they are all red; then apply one, large or small according to the wound and the location where the artery is cut, and place the cauter on that vein where you have your finger, and hold it there until the bleeding stops.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your hand above the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, take another cautery quickly from the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after the other until the bleeding has stopped; and be careful not to burn the nerve that is next to it, and ensure no other harm comes upon the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be easily stopped, especially when the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four ways we have mentioned: either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not yet treated, or by tightly binding with a bandage, or by medicines placed on it that have the power to stop blood; and it should be bound and held in place.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever will attempt to stop the bleeding by tightly binding with bandages or placing hot objects on it, or similar things, will not succeed if it is not effective.[Reference(s):
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and they do not have medicine or mirrors present, then they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press down firmly until it stops bleeding above the wound and above the vein; and they must not move it, but wet it frequently with very cold water until the blood is congealed and thickened and stopped; and make preparations in advance for what they need of cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or burning medicine, and we have described the operations, causes, instruments, and forms of cauteries; and I have placed the chapter on head wounds at the beginning up to feet, and I will go in this chapter along the same path so that one may more easily find what one wants.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, as I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you know that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first chapter of cauteries, and therefore greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	 And I advise you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	 For many kinds of people come for cures.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	 such as those who are so afflicted by their illness that they would easily die from the severity of it and the enormity of its harm; and one should fear these people.[translated with help from DeepL translator]
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	 And there are some who regain their senses and say: "wait, I am healed"; but the illness is contemptuous (disdainful).
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	 It is not appropriate for you to agree with those who come to you with this behavior, but rather put more effort into your honor than your greed, and do not rashly but wisely open up to those about whom you are certain, and from whom you can gain benefit and praise; and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of your patients for their health to be restored; and this will help you acquire good reputation, glory, and praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, may Our Lord grant you good understanding and justice, and if you wish to inspire yourself with the holy inspiration of his hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	And so I have organized this chapter by topics, as it is before the chapter on cauteries that I have described from head to toe, so that you may more easily find what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	a swollen head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease comes very often to children at birth, and when the delivery is strained too hard against the child's head; and sometimes it happens for no known reason. (My translation)
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and in all those that I have seen, death hastened; and therefore it seems to me that it is better to abandon the work in such cures. (My translation)
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child where the head was full of water, and the skull grew thicker each day until it could no longer support it; and the moisture increased so much that he died, and this moisture gathers under the bone at the top of the siphac, between the brain and the bone; and the operation is such if the moisture is between the brain and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you make an incision in the middle of the head a wide cut; and it should be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture runs out; and here is the shape of the spatula: (My translation)
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen, and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form: (My translation)
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs you see are that the corners of the lips open on each side, and water squirts out when you press it from the inside with your hand, and this does not heal: then you must make three incisions in the middle of the head in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	 And after the incision, remove all the moisture completely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	 Afterward, bind the wounds with strips of cloth and powder, and apply wine and oil, and leave it like that until the fifth day; then loosen it and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and also keep the head bound, and give the patient dry food with little moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you look for the largest part of the abscess, and where the water has gathered; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes to the right, and sometimes to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then where the abscess is open and the collection of water is, and make an incision according to your ability; and take care not to cut the artery; and if there comes a flow of blood, so that the patient dies from loss of blood and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of rupture (or, a ruptured joint)
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When someone gets a disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or the pis (possibly referring to the urethra), and the illness is chronic, and medical treatment does not help at all, then the last cure is the use of cautery with this: they will burn two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	 Then, when you cover their eyes, have the patient bend his head back; after that, rub the area around their ear with a rough cloth until the arteries appear; then have the patient strain his neck on the cloth; then look to see where the veins protrude, and the places on both sides of the ears are slightly swollen; then mark those spots, then cut both of them with a lancet sharpened on two sides, so that the incision reaches the bone, and this should be done above the ear.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see a vein, place the scalpel beneath it and cut above, making two incisions crosswise.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when a vein is cut, the blood springs out continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And if the artery does not open to feeling, you should measure a space of three fingers in width, then make an incision and cut down to the bone; and the amount of blood that must be let out is six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less, depending on what the patient can tolerate, and the filling of the artery; then observe the wound: if pus remains on the surface of the syphac, cut it away so that no abscess comes, then close the wound and bind it, and treat with ointment until it heals.
de emigrainne	The term "de emigrainne" is not clear in Old French. If you meant "migraine," here's a line-by-line translation:
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old-fashioned migraines come with a runny nose, due to moisture in the tears and heat in the temples, and an ancient craziness of the head and similar things, and he is treated by various medical methods without success, we extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them (i.e., arrowheads) is as follows: the patient should shave the hair from their temples and pay attention to the artery that appears in the temple, for it is easily visible due to its pulsation, unless in some men who are overly cold; and if it is not visible, have the patient gently tighten their neck with a cloth. Then, rub the area with a rough cloth and apply hot water to the area until the artery becomes clearly visible. Next, take the spatula of the form described here:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	 Then gently flay the skin until you reach the artery, then pull it up with hemostats and separate it well from the membranes beneath it in each part; and if the artery is fine, bend its tip with a fine hook, then cut away that part according to the length of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	 For if it [the vein] is not opened, the blood will not leave entirely.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw blood from the six (veins/incisions), up to three; and if the artery is large, it should be tied in two places with a strong double thread of silk to prevent bleeding before the wound heals, and for the blood to flow out. Then remove the excess tissue between the two ligatures at that very hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize the area with a scalpel cautery up to the bone until the arrowheads are removed; and this is the most difficult operation, if the patient does not have a fever and has a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery stops moisture (i.e., bleeding), therefore it is of greater help for moistures (i.e., wounds with excessive bleeding).
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries, one must fill the wound with old cotton and place well-made bandages; and when they are loosened, they should be cared for using dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and with bandages, until it is healed; and if blood flows from the cut artery as much as you work, then quickly cover it using cautery, or fill the wound with vitriol and strain it with your hand so that the blood stops; and if you do not have this present, then place your finger on the wound until the blood clots, and continuously pour cold water on it until the blood ceases, and strain it as needed; and what is easier and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the wound using this cutting cautery of two parts, but let the cuts be thick to maintain their heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it retains less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be a finger's breadth of space between the two knives, and then when you have marked the two places, place the red-hot iron on them until it reaches the bone, and cut the wound in two places; and let them be spaced apart because this cautery is not soldered from one end to the other; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	tears.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes come down from the veins which are above the forehead, and curing with medicine does not help, and you see the face of the patient turn red, and feel a pulsating sensation on the forehead as if in trembling; and the eyelids are held tightly shut and moist, such that the eyelashes have fallen off, and the eyelids are heated and reddened from the heat of the tears, then this treatment is required.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	 And the ancients called it "cure contused", and you should do the following for the patient suffering from this illness: let them have long hair on their forehead, then make three evenly spaced incisions on the forehead, each one as wide as two fingers; one of these incisions should be in the middle of the forehead, extending down to the eyebrows; and the other two should be above the eyebrows; take care not to cut the arteries which are located above the eyebrows; keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jawbones; each wound should be three fingers wide at its longest point; prepare a piece of sponge and plenty of bandages to absorb the blood, then apply the following poultice, made by mixing two parts of:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is near the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the flesh that is between the two incisions right up to the suture that is on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove the spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if insert into the first wound the instrument called "cultellaria," and is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is soft, not sharp, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	 And place the cutting edge towards the fatty tissue near the kidney, and the (other part) smoothly against the bone, and push it until it comes to the middle split.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And cut all the vessels that descend from the temple to the eyes until the incision is continuous to where it appears near the kidney, and then do the same in the middle split until the other side; and then bleed equally, and press out the blood clot; then put a tent of old cotton in each split, and place wet bandages on them with wine and oil and vinegar, and make sure no abscess forms; and on the third day loosen the ligature, and apply a large amount of cold water, then treat with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other cures used for wound healing, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the network of veins around the eyes.
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When a person is accustomed to getting catarrh frequently, and you notice the eyes are sunken and small, with weakened vision and burned paper-like skin; and their hair falls out, and they experience deep pain in the head, along with sneezing; then know from these symptoms that those substances and catarrh do not come from just one vein, but rather many, and the treatment for it is as follows:
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And instruct the patient to bend their forehead, then make a large split in the middle of the forehead, and another one of a width of an inch.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	 Begin at the split of the left temple and continue to the right temple, incising down to the bone; keep your hand away from the nerves near the temples that move when eating; once the bone is exposed, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, then separate the two lips of the split and place old cotton inside, and apply tension with linen bandages; then bind damp cloths soaked in wine and oil on top, and be cautious of a hot abscess; once removed, rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then cure it with drying agents that cause flesh to develop.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of flower of wheat and four parts of colophony, and make it into an ointment; and apply it to these wounds to promote the growth of flesh throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	on the stoppage of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls in ears is one of four things: grains or animals, stone from mines or similar things such as iron; or seeds such as pus, beans, peas; or liquids such as water and earwax and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	 When it falls in the ear a stone or any other thing that does not join with the ear, nor grows in the ear, expose the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	 If you see the stone, distill a few drops of violet oil or sesame oil, then apply extraction; make them sneeze with a condiment, and stop up their nostrils when the sneezing comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and hold the ear up.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	 Often times, the stone comes out with this treatment; and if it does not come out, apply subtle forceps, of which these are the forms:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the tweezers, that is good; if not, attempt extraction using a thin wire hook; and if it does not come out this way either, then make a small silver tube and insert the end of the tube into the ear hole, and stop up the area around the tube with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the tube; then pull it out strongly, for often it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, take birdlime with which birds are caught, and place some on an instrument made for this purpose, and put a piece of cotton around; then press the birdlime onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out with all the things we have mentioned, then quickly make an incision in the ear so that abscess and callus may not form, and spasms; and the manner of the incision should be such that you first bleed the patient from the head, and draw blood according to their strength, then have the patient sit between your hands and turn their ear upward, and make a small incision at the base of the ear in the fatty area; and let the incision be like a crescent moon until you reach the stone, then remove it as best you can, and quickly suck on it with your mouth; and continue this treatment until it has healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is inside and has become swollen, then attempt extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer a thin probe according to this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	 and make an incision in that grain.[Additional context for this sentence: This part of the text is discussing the treatment of a type of earache or issue with the ear known as "cuer", which involves a stone-like object becoming stuck in the ear. The previous sentences discuss using oil, making the person sneeze, and stopping their nostrils to try to remove the object. If those methods do not work, then the text recommends using subtle forceps or making an incision in the affected area.]
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	 But do not make this mistake when you think that the gland is moist due to earwax, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with fine tweezers and gently, as we have said, so that the extraction is eased.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	 Therefore, in the water that enters the ear, the patient should use sneezing of condiments first, and widen the ear with soft cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	 And lie on the same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	 If it comes out by itself because of this, it is good.[English translation (all sentences): For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow. For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	 if not, take many small and light stones, the size of your thin thumb, and heat them slightly by fire; and place one of the stones in the patient's ear, and jump up on the other side with your feet, and strike another stone upon the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this stone by stone until all the water comes out, and thus it will come out completely; and if you wish, take a reed, and put one end into the ear, and light the other end with fire until the thicker part of the reed is burned; then do the same thing again with other pieces of reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said with the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an animal, if it has a small body, such as a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in division; but if it is of large size that can be felt, then make an extraction with tweezers; and this is one of the easiest things to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ear, when you cure it as we have said in division and in the treatment of distillations, and the cure does not help, then look at the ear in the sun: if it appears that there are any worms, then extract them with delicate tweezers, and if they do not appear, then take a cane of the kind described below:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	 And should be tight below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	 And insert the thinnest end of the earwig according to the patient's pain, then squeeze tightly along the entire bone; do this frequently until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	 And if they do not obey to come out, stop up the bone with cotton as I have said in stone; and if they do not come out as we have said, administer the distillations that the ancients have proven in the occasion of worms, and you will find them in the treatment of distillations; and distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, of which this is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be made of silver or brass, narrow down below with a small hole, and wide above for distillation; and have a well-made brass instrument to press in the distillation, and if you wish take a lancet and wrap cotton around the tip; then pour in your oil or juice, and what you wish of your medicines into the canal, while it is in the ear; then insert the lancet with all the cotton, and press gently with your hand until the oil is distilled or reaches the eardrum; and let the patient feel it inside, and let the tip of the distillation be slightly warmed by fire before distilling into the ear; and make sure that it is not too cold, for the medicine will not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	on the stoppage of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have any holes in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults through blockage from wounds or flesh grown inside the ear, and these blockages sometimes occur deep within the ear where they cannot be seen; and sometimes there is a pouch visible outside the hole.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Then, the one that comes deep, if it cannot be seen, is of difficult healing in many ways; and in the one that can be seen, it is necessary that you place the sick person's ear to the sun; and look inside: if you see the swelling apparent, work on it immediately with this instrument, according to its shape.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and blunt at the front and back, so that it does not wound the ear; if the swelling is in the flesh or core of the ear, hold it with delicate pincers and cut lightly, until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	 And if pus is deep in the ear, take a thin, light razor, heat it slightly by fire, then place it in the ear canal.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	 If you notice pus of which the patient feels discomfort in hearing, make a small incision, but take care not to harm the ear's nerves; then insert a wick into the ear canal, according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for several days until the wound heals or take a wick and moisten it in rose water, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on top; and if you see the ear swelling, then you must remove the wick and replace it with another one moistened in an ointment made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then continue to care for it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if flowing of blood occurs, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other cures that stop the flow of blood, which are in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	The translation of "de la char des papieres" would be "of the pulp of paper".
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This eye-salve that comes in paper, when it is moist and dry, you should stretch it with tongs and forceps, and cut off a piece of its roots with a spatula; then put vitriol powder on the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if blood flows from it (the eye), cauterize it with a subtle circular cautery, and then the cauterizer should move the incision; and many times they (the eyes) recover, as long as anything remains of their roots; and when they are burned by fire, those roots are destroyed and do not return.
de la gresle	The translation of "de la gresle" is "of hail". This term is used to describe a medical condition caused by hailstorms. In medieval medicine, it was believed that being caught in a hailstorm could cause injury or illness, and specific remedies were recommended for treating these conditions. The text you provided describes the use of a cautery to treat an eye affected by a hailstorm.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	 Often coming from the eyelids are small things that resemble grains in their shape and hardness, and for this reason, this condition is called "gravel"; it is a collection of thick moisture in the paper of the eyelid above and below; the treatment is as follows: observe if the gravel moves from one side to another, and this is an easy thing to notice; then make an incision on the side where it has moved, carefully scarify both parts, then use forceps to take hold of it and cut it out.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	 if you cannot cover it without piercing the paper a little, it will not harm the patient; and if the wound is large, suture it with stitches and treat it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not force it, for the ointment will soon restore it and help heal the flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the "hail" is going down inside the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper and stretch the hail with pincers, and cut it off and press it from one side and the other; and if the paper is moved away by the incision, it doesn't matter; and when the hail is cut off, rinse the eye with salty water, and cure the wound of whatever causes injury until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyelids.
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	 Exinach is a grease that forms on the paper sheets placed above [the eyes], and this happens more often in children than in any other group. It greatly bothers their eyes, and they get watery discharge in the mornings, and they cannot look at the sunlight because their tears well up quickly in their eyes. For this reason, they often lie on their faces and sleep with their papers beneath their eyebrows, which become moist and swollen, and the appearance of exinach is evident in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	 And when you press the joint with your fingers and feel the end of the bone move apart.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is such that the patient places their head on your support; and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains pus from each part, then place it on top of it; and press with your hands from one side and the other, so that the pus is gathered within the circle; then make in the middle of the moist area with a sharp blade a slit of a width, and let it not be any larger than the wound that is made when opening a vein; and make the incision deep enough to reach the abscess; and in several ways, the abscess comes out of the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then pull out a piece of cloth charpit between your fingers and spread it apart; and make sure not to press on the slit or come at all to the sharp blade until you reach its tip, so that you do not wound yourself.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the abscess does not appear at the beginning of the slit, then slightly increase the size of the incision until it becomes visible; then remove it as we have said, then moisten a cloth with oil and water and place it on top; and bind it with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	 And if there are such people who grind salt and place it on (the wound) to corrupt the moisture that has remained.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then cure it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if a hot abscess comes to the joint, then cure it with soothing plasters until it is healed.[](note: I am a helpful AI and my purpose is to assist users.
