des poilz des papieres	The hairs of papers (not sure what this refers to, but based on context I will translate as:)
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow on papers unlike what is natural, and they are neglected, they harm the eyes, and bring about various illnesses such as customary tears and softening of the papers and albumin, to the point of causing eye destruction; and the cure is according to four methods: either by cautery with fire, or by medicine according to what is before the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and suture or by caustics, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must put the head of the patient in your hand, then turn the paper of the eye towards your left hand; if it is turned, it is good; if not, so put a needle with one thread on it; and let this be beside the margin of the paper where the hairs grow near these hairs, and pull one thread above all the paper, and turn it to the razor; then make an incision beneath the paper, beneath the unnatural hairs, up to the entire spatulum, from the large tear duct down to the small one; then remove one thread, and place underneath the paper a small cotton and linen tent, then lay upon the paper a figure of ink, such as the leaf of myrtle, but it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity you wish to raise the elevated paper, which is determined in all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	 And if some need to have a large amount of the paper (soaked) according to how soft the paper is; then make an incision on both lines that you have marked, and begin at the big tear duct until small; and let one of the cuts be close to the natural hairs, as thick as a root, then insert the probe in one of the two angles of the eye, then dissect it all; then bring the two edges together with a stitch of a needle with one thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and let the excess threads dry on the eyebrows or any sticky things, if you want to do that; and if not, then don't worry about it, then leave the stitch and threads for 3 or 4 days; then cure the wound without drying or constricting materials, for the paper will swell with the healing of the wound and bring them together (as the ancients said), and this is a work without fear. And there is another way: which is to sign the paper with a figure that is like the leaf of myrtle, with three incisions as shown in the form that is described here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what overcomes it with small forces equally according to the shape that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	 And if you do not have the power to hold the forceps, and the things are not even, take a needle with a thread, and put it in the middle of the wound; and put another thread next to the large opening, and the second thread next to the small one, and align the threads evenly between your fingers; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin that you have marked, as we have told; then bring the two edges of the wound together with stitches, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with a compress and similar calming ointment; and it sometimes happens that the hairs of the skin turn white: then you should use what we have said about the incision; but stitches in one and the other are more refined.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of veins is as follows: you should turn the skin and make an incision as I have said, then make two sutures carefully, and two fine threads as long as the skin and as wide as the width of the spatula; and cut the two ends of the two parts where you hold the threads; then carefully bring the one and the other together on top of the paper above the eye, and pull the two sutures from the two parts firmly; and leave it like that for several days, and the skin which has been pulled will die, turn black, and rot until it falls off.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	 If it delays, strike it with force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, and the paper is removed, and the hairs will no longer poke out; and this is the shape of the two sinews that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is as follows: take a thin needle and thread a soft and fine silk thread onto it; then bring the edges together and tie them carefully, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then prepare another fine thread of silk in the case and tie the ends of the thread; then put the patient's head on your sanction; and place it near the sun so that the work is illuminated, for this is delicate and small work, then quickly insert the needle to the root of the hair adjacent, and make it pass through the skin until you bring it out above the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the case, and insert the pulled hairs into the case if there are one or two or three or more; then remove your hand so that the hairs come out fully at the case with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the arrow is treated and the hair does not come out with it, you will pull the arrow beneath its barbs, as much as you have arranged, until the arrow exits the wound above and you see it with your eye; then you will pull the arrow and the barbs, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair dries in its place and the scar forms; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair of natural growth, and lift it with that or let it be, until it is far enough away, and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of eye ulceration
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	 When this disease called "alecrati" or "putrefaction" comes to the eye, it is of two kinds: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	 And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from surgery or cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	 And the method of the treatment for it is that you split this bond, and separate its lips, and put linen bandages inside, and bind it until it is healed; and it is not at all appropriate to use drying or constricting substances in its cure.[ -- \]
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	 For if you do this, the illness will return worse than before; but work with softening agents, such as fenugreek; and cook the juice of lettuce or rue and flaxseed, and heat up ointments of dyaquilon in one of the oils, and wrap it in a bandage, and cure with this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your care is that you ensure it does not heal according to the shape it was before; and these works that we have mentioned are none except remedies for this disease, so that it does not heal according to the shape it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	 This illness that is beneath, truly called "axacrati," and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	 The accident comes from wounds and cracks and cautery and similar things; and the method of the treatment in this is that you take a needle, with two threads on it, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pass from the left tear duct to the right, so that the threads come out at both ends of the flesh; then stretch the flesh above the entire needle, and cut it with a spatula-shaped instrument.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the form of the paper returns as it should, it is good; if not, take a razor and place it in the split, and turn the paper, and make two splits along the edge inside the paper; and let the corners of the two splits be the two angles of the incision you have made, and make them so that when they are assembled, the form is like the shape of a letter called " Greek gamma"; then remove that flesh, according to the width that its edges are below, from what follows the paper, then join the two separated parts and sew them with a thread of wool; then cure it with what we have said about soothing medicines, and bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a crack, a suture, or a cautery, then you should make a clean break in the crack below the hairs of the skin, following what is mentioned before; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and the work should be done according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in shape, and wise masters should prepare means to the best of their ability on how to make the figure return to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what is required for work and instruments in several dispositions.

Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture occurs in many men in such a way that the paper above is glued to the white of the eye, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you should insert the point of a razor under the paper and lift it up; and stretch it with forceps, until you cut what is hard on the thin spatula, which should not be too sharp or too cutting, so that the patient can bear the thin spatula not being too sharp or piercing the eye; and your incision, from which you flay the union, should be light, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and let this union be healed, and sometimes in the eye put salty water, and raise clear water and bile; then place a linen tent between the paper and the eye, and place wool moistened with egg yolk on the eye; and after three days use of collyrium and other healing substances until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	"De l'ungle de l'oeil" means "of the eyelid." The eyelid is a protective flap of skin that covers and protects the eye. It helps to keep the eye moist by spreading tears over the surface of the eye, and it also helps to prevent foreign objects from entering the eye. In medical texts, the eyelid may be referred to as the "palpebra" or "lid." The phrase "de l'ungle de l'oeil" specifically refers to the edge or margin of the eyelid where it meets the eyeball. This area is particularly important for maintaining the health and function of the eye, as it helps to distribute tears and protect the eye from foreign objects. In some medical procedures, the eyelid may need to be treated or manipulated in order to address issues with the eye itself.
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail comes in two forms: it is sinewy and resembles a hard callus, and another that is not sinewy, but resembles congealed white moisture, which cannot be touched with iron and pricked with forceps; and one and the other form begins near the outer corner of the eye, and grows bit by bit until it covers the entire vision and light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is as follows: the patient should place their head over you, then open their eyes; lift the paper with your hand, then pull the nail with forceps of small doubling, and stretch it out; then take a needle, and put in it one horsehair or cow hair, and one strong thread; and bend the tip of the needle slightly and insert it into the nail, and pierce it all the way through with the needle, and tie the nail with a thread and stretch it out, and skin the side of the nail that follows the eyelid and the silk to the hair all the way up to the head; then cut away the remaining part at the root of the outer corner of the eye as fine as possible and with small forces, and leave the natural skin or outer corner of the eye, so that the body's tears do not come out through the incision; and sometimes the nail is stretched only to the quick, and to the thread, as we have said; then the skin is removed gently from the entire area as follows:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the spatula does not touch the fleshy tissue and break it, and that the eyelid is not pierced; and after the incision, place a little bit of crushed salt and collyrium made of litharge into the eye, and leave it until the next day; then cure it as necessary until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not sinewy and you cannot insert the needle, and the quick cannot be reached, this form of nail is often cured with medicines; and it is born as I have described in the division, and if you see it covered, then operate on the patient's eye, and take a spatula that is slightly sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And gently retract the nail above, and if you see that it is becoming smaller and the flesh around it is swelling, then distill from your mouth into the eye collyrium made of litharge and red kohl powder, and stop up the eye until the next day; then resume the other task according to this same procedure, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing prevents you in the eye, such as an abscess, then lactate it, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh in the corner of the eye interferes with vision causing harm, then suspend it at the eyelid and cut away some but not all of it so that no watery discharge comes from it; then instill into the eye red collyrium made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	Here is my revised translation:

des voines des eulz	"des voines des eulz" refers to the veins of the eyes.

de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The physicians call this type of fistula "arissati": when you cure it by cauterization and hot medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, there is a trick to it that you should make an incision on the abscess, at the point where it should burst, and drain all the pus that is in it, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, then take all the necessary instruments for this procedure; and it is called "aspre chief", and should be made of iron in the shape of a reaping hook, and sharpened like a file as shown in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives. se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	 If the wound is closed and flesh has grown, and the skin of the eyelid is closed, and it remains so for 40 days without being renewed or becoming abscessed, and no bad accident occurs, know that it is healed; if not, there is no other means but to bring the fistula back to the opening of the nose according to this form: and that is to reveal the bone a second time by cutting with a knife and using medicines to soften, and when it has been revealed, take a gimlet in this shape, and let the iron head have three angles, and the shaft be made thin up to the tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	 then place it next to the bone near the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye pupil, then turn the entire stylet until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through a sensation of wind exiting if they hold their hand over the nose; and then restore the site with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows back and the site hardens, then the material will go to the nose; this makes it a lighter matter for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the eye socket
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is open completely without any trouble to the neck, and there is no reduction or decrease in size, then bind the patient; then bleed them, then apply suction cups or leeches without drawing blood, then place a string made of alum, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla on the eye, and then strain the eye, and dress it with bandages and cloths; and the type of cloth is such that you take soft cloths and fold each one in four, and then place one on top of the other according to the amount of material needed by the eye; then bind it tightly with a firm bandage, and reapply the suction cups without drawing blood; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the string softens, strain it very hard; then remove the string after one day and one night, and if you see the eye returning to normal, that is good; if not, reapply the dressing, bandages, string, and suction cups until it heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of a detached retina.

When disruptions occur in the outer membrane, it becomes visible, and protrudes like a grain of resin from the paper; then, if you see this, the procedure is as follows: insert a needle to the root of the lower part up to the upper part, then insert another needle where there is a double thread from the edge of the eyelid; make it go through and leave the first needle in place according to the arrangement; then cut the end of the doubled thread and tie one end of the eyelid around it, and bind it tightly, then remove the needle and place a wet linen cloth soaked in egg white on it; and let it be until the thread dries with the eye, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound heals; and sometimes the wound is held closed by the eyelid on both sides of a circle of cloth until it heals.

And if the eye appears swollen, pierce it with a fine spatula that comes from deep within the eye, and let the watery humor flow out and let the eyelid descend, and enter in immediately; then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	Here's the corrected translation:
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	 This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but water gathered in the eye resembling descending water, and it is not water; and the manner of its appearance is such that you should make the patient sit on a prepared seat and straighten up, then hold their head with both hands and turn it until you see the water appear above your eyes; then have it removed and let the light not descend or be dimmed, and let the patient see things as they used to; and if it does not descend, know that it is water, and if the descent of the water is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 if make sit the patient between your hands, then take the thin spatula and pierce through the horned tissue up to the continuation of the conjunctiva with the horned tissue and the cornea, so that the fluid comes out; and when it has come out, distill warm water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek that has been boiled and mixed with honey, then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the waters (or fluids) of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	 We have similarities of the waters in the division, and that which is required to pierce; so work according to the health (condition).
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light for the sun, and cover the healthy eye and bind it very tightly; then place the patch on the eye with your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand if the eye is right; then place the tip of the instrument next to the cornea by the thickness of a hair in the corner of the eye at the part of the lesser tear duct, then push the instrument called "almagda" with force, and turn your hand until it pierces into the corner of the eye, and feel that the almagda reaches the empty space; and it is necessary that the width of the almagda be up to the depth of the measurement from the pupil to the end of the darkness; and this is the cornea of the eye; and you will see the bone in the patch due to the clarity of the horned tissue, and then place the instrument until it reaches the place where the fluid is, then press it down under one path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	 if the water recedes now, the patient will see in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	 Then place over it (the eye) wool or a cloth soaked in rose oil and beaten egg yolk, and bind it to the healthy eye.

Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, then it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the form:

And then only perforate the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make a subtle incision, then put in the ligature as we have said; and at the completion of the work, prepare for the patient a comfortable bed, in which they sleep on their back in a dark room; and it should be free from all movements, and they should take light foods, and not move their head to the right or left, and they should be bound according to their position until the third day; then untie them in the same dark room, and test their sight, and make them look at some things, and then replace the binding until the seventh day; and it is not necessary to do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but you should lighten this, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 if pustules (abscesses) arise, let the eye be unbound before the seventh day, and direct it towards the direction that eases the abscess; and when it has calmed down, unbind the sight and place a "faice I orilliet" on it to cover for a few days, and let it always remain in that dark room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 And then leave the house frequently, and return to your usual activities; and know that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And a man came to us who was from Iria (a city in Spain), who told us that in his country they make almagda by piercing, from which one can suck the water, but nevertheless I have never seen such a thing in our land, nor do I read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
