de la char sor le neis	of flesh from the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 Sometimes various kinds of newborn flesh or skin grow attached to each other, some of which resemble scorpions with many feet; and there are such growths that have raised skin of fuscous color, and soft skin of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 Then in the case of this wound that is soft, and not inflamed, you should make the patient sit between your hands with their face towards the sun; clear their nostrils, and apply a probe to those wounds, and pull out any pus; then collect as much as you can support on a delicate, sharp spatula on one side, until you are certain that the wound is completely cleaned.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any part that cannot be cut, open it with a very fine and light instrument so that nothing remains; and if pus forms or an abscess arises, treat it as necessary; and if they are malignant abscesses, cauterize it quickly to stop the bleeding and remove all the flesh; then pour rosewater, vinegar, or wine on (the nose).
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If the nose does not clear and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is healed; but if moisture does not drain as it should, know that there is pus stuck to the bone above, which the instruments cannot cut: then you must insert a slightly thick linen thread, and it should be smooth and have spaces of about a digit or less between each knot; and place the patient's nose at the edge of the thread with as much force as they can bear, and pull gently until it comes through the nasal cavity into the mouth; and children do this often in school, and it is an easy thing for those who want to do it; then hold the head that comes out through the nasal cavity with one hand, and the other head that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and know which one comes out first by feeling the knots on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Perform this procedure so that you know the wound has corrupted the flesh, then pull out the sutures, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and put it back in its place as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all remaining flesh; and then place a plug of wood in the nose for several days until it is healed, and if drying medicines are needed, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And whether it be of silver or bronze, similar to an open lamp, like a funnel, and the spout the same; and if you wish, make a closed funnel, and let the instrument be full to purge the head; and have a handle on the head to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of flesh from the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often a sickness is born in the head of the nose, called "telul", and it grows and becomes large at times, to the point where it is visible; and therefore you must cut it at the beginning and extract it all, then place on it the cautery or a burning medicine; and if you wait until it has grown large before cutting it, see if it is hard, of a dark color, with little sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an inflamed abscess, because when it is cut once, it can cause great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of a dark color, and you see that you can extract all of it, have the patient empty their stomach and cauterize the area without fear, and cure it with drying and constricting agents.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn up.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when solutions of coagulation come to one of these cartilaginous works, it helps little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then when this happens to someone, look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring the two lips together in a stitch, then cure it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, then you must cauterize all the edges of their wound until they heal, then bring the two lips together in a stitch and bind it, and put powder of dragon's blood and ground incense on top of the powders, and place a piece of strong plaster or another adhesive plaster on top, and leave it until it dries out through it, then cure it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of stitching is to approximate the wound: either with needles, as we have said in abdominal stitching; or with thread, as I have informed you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	To some men there come within the lips hard abscesses like grains of pepper, smaller and larger; then one must turn the lips and make an incision on each nodule, and take it with forceps and cut each part; then apply the place after the incision with powdered vitriol until the blood is stopped; and then leave it open to air, and cure the place of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, a swelling of the flesh occurs on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; you should hold it with tongs and cut it at its root, letting the pus or blood run out; then put vitriol powder or other restraining and desiccative powders on the wound; and if this flesh comes back after the incision, which often happens, you should cut it again and cauterize it; it will not come back after cauterization. Here are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of deafness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, calluses appear on the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth become black, green, and yellow, such that the corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth become foul-smelling; you should make the patient sit between your hands, with their chin in your holy palm, and scrape the visible calluses or teeth until nothing remains; and similarly for any black, green, or yellow stains, as well as for any other discolorations, until they are cleaned; and if you remove what is present at the first cleaning, that is good; if not, then start again on the second and third day, continuing to scrape until everything is removed. And know that teeth require various forms of instruments for scraping, according to what the work demands, because the scrapers used to scrape outside the teeth have different shapes than those used between the teeth; these forms and others should be prepared in advance.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you cure a toothache, you must delay pulling the tooth as long as possible, because one should not do it hastily; for it is a very serious matter until there is no excuse to pull (the tooth).
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Then, when the patient is about to be pulled, you should make sure of the tooth loosening.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Often, the pain deceives the patient, and they think it is a tooth that is causing the problem, and they have a good tooth pulled; yet the pain does not go away, for it is due to a bad root, as we have often seen with these surgeons. And when you are certain of the loosened tooth, you should cauterize around the tooth with a strong styptic to protect the gum all around; then pull it with your hands or with delicate pliers, pulling and tugging until it is loose; then securely fasten the pliers, and have the patient's head in your lap, holding it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After extract the tooth without breaking it, and if it does not come out, take any of these instruments and gently insert it on each side, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, you should fill it with cloth where the holes are; and hold it delicately with pincers so as not to break it when tightening; and one must work very carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And take great care not to break it and leave a part of it, for this will cause greater pain for the patient due to the malice of the root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And beware not to act as some ignorant surgeons do, who in their haste and audacity sometimes break the root and do not bring about what we have described; but rather cause great illness due to the remaining roots or the broken chariot, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is extracted, rinse the area with wine or vinegar and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often does, fill the area with powdered vitriol; and if that doesn't work, cauterize the area.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments used to pull teeth first should have long and thick handles that do not bend when pulling the tooth; and these are their shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of sturdy size so that they do not bend when pulled, and let them be made of good quality iron, and let them have teeth to hold onto wounds.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the root remains to be pulled, you should place cotton soaked in butter on it for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 until the place is softened, then apply tongs called "algefri," which resemble a bird's beak; and they should be made inside like a file, and this is its shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots still do not want to come out with all these forceps, then you must cut open all the flesh around the root and apply an instrument called "althali," which is a flat piece of metal with this shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and sturdy so that it does not break easily. If the root comes out with this, it's good; if not, then use all the instruments described in the following forms:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one helps oneself with this instrument that has two branches, of which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other metal instruments that are in front of the teeth, and of this instrument that resembles large pliers, of which this is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these instruments be strong so that they cannot break, and know that there are many dental instruments, and also other instruments that are not mentioned; and the wise master subtlely finds his own instrument according to what his work and the illness demands, for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach any instrument due to their diversity, and one does not break a tooth or other bones, but searches among the instruments that are needed, as I have told you, and helps with gestures, of which this is the shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and sturdy to hold the bone so that it does not slip, but can hold and remove it; and then restore the place with appropriate medicines for this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, let it be all smoothed out with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not in accordance with the body's natural form, and its shape is ugly, and similarly in young women, you should determine if the tooth is new-growing and not in its correct position, and cannot be straightened or filed: then file it; but if it is misaligned with the tooth next to it, take this instrument, which has a small hook-like shape, and made of sharp iron:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And use the file frequently, day by day, because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the other teeth; and if it appears that the tooth can be filed down, file it with a thin file, such as this one shown in the illustration.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is similar to the files used for making needles; and file down the tooth frequently, day by day, gently so that it does not move until it falls out; then use a plain rasp at the end, and if the tooth is too sharp and wounds the tongue, you should file down the roughness until it is even, so that it does not wound the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth loosens/falls out.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the front teeth become loose, either from trauma or falling out, and the patient cannot bite down on what they eat without defecating, and you have treated them with constricting medicines to no avail; then they must be constricted with a gold wire, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the wire be of medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to align the teeth, take the thread and place it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the patient's jaw between the loose teeth, whether there is one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then repeat the process until you reach the starting point, and pull gently but firmly, so that the teeth do not move at all; and secure the wire at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then bind the jaw with a thread using pliers, and align it, and place it between the healthy tooth and the loose one, making sure not to injure the tongue; and keep it tight as long as it can stay, and if it loosens, or the thread breaks, then tie it with another thread; and let it remain and serve in this way all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of aligning two healthy teeth and two loose ones, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is replaced in its place as soon as possible, as we have said; and one should not meddle with it unless they are wise and skilled; and sometimes the shape of a tooth is made from animal bone, and it is placed in the gap where it is needed, and it is constricted as we have said, and it remains in place for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the tie of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 Sometimes there is a ligament beneath the tongue that comes naturally at birth or accidentally due to a healed wound; and the procedure is as follows: you open the mouth of the patient, hold their head in your hand, and lift their tongue; then cut the nervous ligament wide enough so that the tongue is loosened from its anchorage, and if there is hardness or knot, which is due to healed wound, insert the hook and cut the ligament wide; and make sure not to penetrate too deep to avoid damaging the artery that lies beneath; when you have finished, apply a swab of rose-colored water or cold water, then place a linen tent under the tongue; and let the patient change it every night so that the ligament does not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 And if there is a flowing of blood, place vitriolic powder on the wound; and if the blood does not stop, cauterize it with the ligature cautery, which is good for that; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of fussey color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining toward blenchor, and there is moisture, throw onion peel on it, and make an incision with a thin spatula, and release it from one side and the other; and if the blood comes to meet your work, put vitriol powder on it until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you draw everything out; then lift the leu easily and gently, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Sometimes abscesses come inside the throat called "godath", and they are properly called the two almonds. And when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is hard abscesses of little sensitivity and of whitish color, do not touch them at all with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if they are red and the root is large, do not touch them at all with iron, to avoid bleeding; but leave it alone until it is ripe, and then you will remove it, or it will break by itself; and if it has a whitish color that returns, and the root is fine, prepare the instrument to cover it, but first see if the abscesses have calmed down and are appeased.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then make the patient sit down in front of the sun, and his head should be in your lap, and open his mouth and take the surgical instrument in your hands, and press down his tongue with it, covering the entire instrument; it should be made of thin silver or brass, just like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And press the tongue down beneath all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the onion peel and insert it into the almond, and draw it out as much as you can; and draw some of the pus with it, then cover it with the instrument, so that it may be as follows, which resembles forceps; and yet the jaws are close together, and one presses against the other, and it is made of iron, either iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this tool available, take tongs instead, of which this is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side and blunt on the other; and once you have tonged one of the almonds, tong the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with warm water, and vinegar, and strained, and if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with water or the peels of pomegranates cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then heal it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses grow in the throat besides the two almonds, so cut them then as you would the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, which is to say a small abscess; and she had her entire throat closed up so that the woman could not exhale due to the blocked passage, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained in this state for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so swollen that it had pushed out two teeth through both nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 I hastened then and quickly stuck a probe into one of the boils, then pulled it out and extracted a large piece of pus; then I inserted another probe into the other nostril and gave her a drink and pressed her tongue; after that, I stuck the probe into these abscesses and cut out a part of it, and only a little blood came out; and so the woman's windpipe was cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut into this abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept growing and filling up the space that I had emptied, becoming very large; then I drained it and cauterized inside her throat: it stopped growing after that; and I left those parts, not knowing what God did with her afterwards.
de l’uve	of the grape (from Latin "uvam") or eye (from Latin "oculus"), Old French used "ueil" for both, so "de l'uve" is ambiguous in this language and could mean either "of the grape" or "of the eye".
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When pus descends to the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below, large, and round, it is called "eye.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 When it is healed as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help at all, and you see that the main abscess has calmed down and it is fine, then you should cut it; and the one that is round and not long; and it is blood-colored or the color of decay or black, then you should avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Therefore, when you see it, according to its swelling and length as I have said, you should make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned before; then insert the needle into the eye and pull it down, and cut it at the first of the two instruments that I have mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And it is necessary that you do not cover entirely the superfluity that is beyond the natural limit; because if you cover more, it will harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient is afraid of being covered (in bandages), then one must use strategy in performing the cautery while allaying their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 And the method of cauterization is to use a hot iron.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And let the patient place their head into your support, and then press their tongue to the instrument that we mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and moisten it with living hot water, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and apply the tip of this instrument, which has the following shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have the patient place a hair or put the medicine on it, such as the handles of a spoon, and place the instrument full of medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth with the medicine inside, so that it does not go down to the throat and cause choking; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the eye, for half an hour, until you see it turn black and the bites of the medicine are calmed; and if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument with the cotton into the wound, as much as the cotton adheres to the eye; and do this often, until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry and fall off after three or five days. And if you need to start the cauterization of the medicine again, then start it again, and after the cauterization wipe around the eye with cotton wrapped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and cure with gargling until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision or cauterization if it is treated with fumigation in this manner: take chamomile and hyssop and oregano and rue and camomile and elder and similar herbs, and gather them all or some of them in one pot, and put them to boil; and let the pot be well glued with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot there should be an instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 And whether it be of silver or bronze, and one of the eyes be put in the patient's mouth until the vapor rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye becomes mortified; then begin again frequently, until the eye dries up, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the onset of a hot abscess, for many things can happen; and do not do it unless at the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and put inside it an eggshell crumb, so that the patient's mouth is not too hot; for the eggshell crumb does not allow the vapor to weigh down the mouth, and this is a good remedy altogether.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often a bone or fish spine, or some other object gets stuck in the throat; therefore, you must pull out what you can see, and press the patient's tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you may see the object move; and what is not visible and has lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit after the food has been cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out through vomiting; or the patient has swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of napkin, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a string to the sponge and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will swell up, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out as we have said, take an instrument of wood in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it may enter more easily into the throat, and hold the head up high; and take care not to touch the epiglottis, so that he does not choke or push the bone in further; and it is better if the patient puts the instrument in himself, so that he can feel where the object is; then insert it all the way until the object comes out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat sinew
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 Sometimes the veins are treated with medicine, as I mentioned in the division, by means of medical treatment; and when this does not help at all, then look at the patient's throat in the sun, after you press their tongue with the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see the vein, then draw it out with a small hook, or with delicate pliers that are suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and throw it in without swallowing, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the tongue tastes the water, it will fall out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 And if it does not fall out as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida using the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall out without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 The method of fumigation is as follows: take a pot with hot coals in it, and cover it with a perforated cloth, with the opening of the instrument placed in the hole; then pour your fumigation into it, and the patient places the handle of the instrument in their mouth, closing their mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but reaches the tongue; and the tongue will fall out now, and if it does not, repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty and bitter foods, and do not drink water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out by this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which to treat the tonsil is, when it can be seen, similar to curved pliers in order to enter easily into the throat; and it should resemble a bird's beak, and have roughness like sandpaper, so that what it takes, it cannot release; and see here the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter of abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 Many similarities of abscess exist, according to what memory comes after this in this book, and they are different in penetration and size; and it is in two ways, one of which is in its very form, and those that retain moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second manner is for the places where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 For abscesses of the head are different than those of the lower body, and abscesses of the fleshy part are different from those that come in joints, and each one must be judged accordingly in treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is mature according to its development; and there are such kind that must be pierced when they have grown, and do not die according to their development, such as abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 For when abscesses come next to joints, and are left until they rot around, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupt, which causes constriction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 Or if the abscess is next to the main member, and you delay the perforation until it is rotten, it will harm the main member; or if it is next to the fundament, you should pierce it as soon as it is dead; and one must not pierce an abscess that has grown without digestion being completed, except for one that is next to the fundament, lest it rot inside and form a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of the piercing of the abscess when it is dead according to its maturation, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and the softening and swelling of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you must perform the piercing in the lowest part of the abscess, and where it is apparent that it has moved; and let the piercing be long and through the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places where there is no cavity.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those that bend, according to the member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to leave the puncture until it is firm in completed digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you pierce it before that, the body of the pus will be prolonged, and it will be full of much filth; and perhaps the lips and the depths of it will become hardened.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if there is an abscess that is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limb requires.[
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And it is necessary that you make small incisions in small abscesses, small openings; and in large abscesses, large openings, and many cuts according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut out the core and cover it; when it has become as soft as a cloth, and is mortified, then one must do as with buboes: and if there are such that are split into three angles, and if there are such that are cut like the leaf of myrtle, such as abscesses of glands; and if there are such where a round incision is made, and other incisions and similar cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 Those who have no head, such as a soft superficial abscess, it is necessary to fully pierce it; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and has gathered a great deal of pus, and you pierce it, not to draw out all the pus in that hour, but only a part; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then extract some more; do this several times, gradually increasing the amount, until all the pus comes out; do the same even if the patient is of weak constitution, or a woman, or a small child, or an old, frail man.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 For the spirit (gas) sometimes jumps with the release of pus, which may cause the death of the patient, but you do not realize it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Avoid this chapter with great care, and when you have lanced your abscess, clean the wound and look if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a flat incision, then apply thin linen or old cotton bandages; and if it is large abscesses with many holes, then you should put a tent in each one so that they come together; and if you have cut off a piece of skin in the abscess and left it hanging, then you should fill it with old cotton or linen rag without moisture, and bind it for three days; then remove it and dress the wound with ointment until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs during your work, bring cold and fresh water, wet a cloth, and apply it to the bleeding site several times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the bleeding persists, provide treatment and care, and use the powders that I have mentioned in this book with light pressure, and if it is in winter, and the area where the abscess is located is very sensitive, then you should place tents and wet cloths on it, heated with wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer, and the area is fleshy, then you should place damp cloths on it, using water and oil or wine and cold oil until the third day, as we have said; and then unbind the abscess, dry and treat it until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what one must understand universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how to proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and herein follows the chapter on the subject.
des soros	In Old French, "des soros" means "of sores" or "on sores". It may refer to the treatments or cures for various kinds of sores.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 Where small abscesses come on the head, and are shaped like a chicken's wattle, and there are many similar ones.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 There are some that are fleshy and such where there is moisture like pustules; and there are those that are hard and stony when cut, and there is no doubt that the artery does not oppose it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the procedure for cutting is that you should test every instrument called a "trocar", to see what it contains, with the shape as follows.[This translation assumes that "li ovraiges de la taille" refers to a surgical procedure involving the use of a trocar, an instrument used to puncture the body and drain fluid or gas. The text states that one should test the trocar to determine its contents before proceeding with the surgery.]
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 For if it contains moisture, they make an incision above the long [one].
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture has been evacuated, skin it immediately without leaving any of the skin that contains the moisture, for it will come back if anything is left; then soak a cotton swab in Egyptian ointment, if available; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, leaving it until the next day; and those who are on night shift will take care of it.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then replace the cotton, as before, on the second and third day, until you are certain that nothing remains from the night; then clean the wound with appropriate ointment until it is healed.[](https://www.deepl.com/translator#auto/en/Et%20pues%20rencomence%20lou%20coton,%20si%20com%20devant,%20le%20second%20jor,%20et%20lou%20tier,%20tant%20que%20tu%20saches%20bien%20qu%27il%20ne%20demoure%20point%20dou%20nit;%20puis%20cure%20la%20plaie%20d%27oignement%20a%20ceu%20convenauble,%20tant%20qu%27il%20soit%20sanez.)
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 And if the abscess holds in pus, cut it along its length; and throw in your leeches, and skin it from all sides, and apply all your care to draw out the pus where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, do as I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And do the same for the abscess if it is stony, and cut and treat it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 And cutting into a stony and moist abscess is easier, for they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And if some of these abscesses, either in the head or elsewhere, have no moisture, and such abscesses as I cut into on an old woman's head; and found the abscess like a hard, rough and white stone, which could not be broken; and if one had struck it with something, they would have made a wound just as if from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 In other abscesses appearing on the head, except for those that appear on children's heads and at the roots of ears, let the incision be as low as possible so that pus can easily drain; and treat it as appropriate.
des scrophules	"Des scrophules" is a medical term used to refer to a type of abscess or inflammatory swelling, usually found in groups, typically on the neck or behind the ears. These swellings are commonly known as "scrofula" or "the king's evil". The term comes from the Greek word "skirphos," which means "tubercular swelling." In medieval medical texts, scrofula was often associated with tuberculosis and thought to be caused by an imbalance of bodily fluids or humors. It was also believed that the touch of a king could cure this condition, hence the name "the king's evil".
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Often, these abscesses occur on the neck and under the armpits, and in other tight spaces, and sometimes they appear in various parts of the body; they are large and are interconnected with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 And each scrofula is specifically located in its own area, just like a knot or an abscess on the head, as we have said; and there are many varieties of these scrofulas.[`Samah Shah123@gmail.com`](mailto:Samah%20Shah123@gmail.com)
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 There are such [things/cases] that contain moisture, and there are some evil ones that do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 Then in the one that you see in good condition to touch, and it appears similar to the color of the body, and moves from every part and is not swollen in the neck or arteries or veins, and is not deep; you should cut it off at the top, and skin it from both sides, and stretch the two lips of the wound with sutures if necessary, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and press gently and repeatedly, and be careful not to cut the nerve or vein, and let the scalpel not be too sharp or cutting, so that the hands do not slip, and do not penetrate too deeply, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put in the wound vitriol powder, or any powders that stop bleeding, and bind up the wound; and leave it until the abscess has calmed down, and the wound has softened, and begun to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 And when the bleeding has stopped, return to your work until you have completed it; then examine with your skill if any small scrofulous sores remain, and cut them out and clean the wound.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofulous sore, it is not appropriate to cut the sore at its root, but instead bind it with a strong double thread and let it fall off by itself without harm; then apply the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then bandage it.[](https://www.definitions.net/definition/bandage)
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you cut out the entire scrofula, it is necessary to bring together the two edges of the wound and sew it up, since there is no remaining excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 It is necessary that you attend to cutting the root of it, and pulling it out, and sewing it up as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For those scrofulas that have an excess, pierce where it is clearly visible, and do so as was previously said, depending (on the condition), then apply dressings with ointment and similar things to corrupt what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with a healing ointment until it heals completely.
de squinance	The word "de squinance" in Old French can be translated to "of sciatica" in English. Sciatica refers to pain that affects the back, hip, and outer side of the leg, caused by compression or irritation of the sciatic nerve.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and wrote about the "tailleure de la gorge," but I have never seen anyone in our land who performed it, and that is their wording in writing.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have squinting, it is necessary that the slit of the throat called "epiglotte" be cleared; and this is not done with their help, because all the veins and the windpipe of the patient are closed to those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in both almonds.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the windpipe, it is necessary to cover the epiglotte to avoid suffocation which comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 Therefore, when we wish to split the epiglottis, it should be split below three or four circles, making a small slit across, between the two circles or according to the length of the slit in the syphaxis, not in the cartilage; and those places are suitable for splitting the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 And if the master is afraid, he should stretch the skin of the throat to its full extent, then split the windpipe until it reaches the trachea; and avoid cutting any blood vessels, if you see any; then cut the syphaxis as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the trachea when the membrane jumps out through the slit, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed where there is doubt about strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound in the windpipe and sew it all the way up to the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote the growth of flesh until it is healed.[--------------------][---------------------------------------------]
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albuccasis says that this should not be done until the throat is completely choked up, and the patient is judged to be dead and there is absence of breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then place a bandage on the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and they breathe through the wound, and thus are kept from dying; and for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the illness has passed, and it passes in 3 or 4 days. And then they command to sew up the wound and cure it, until it is healed; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 I saw that a damsel took a knife and plunged it into her throat, cutting part of the tendons in the windpipe; and I was called to cure her, and found her as if she were dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that had issued from it, and I knew well that it had not received any treatment or dressing but was open to the throat, and the wind was escaping through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hurried and sewed up the wound, and cured it until it was healed; and nothing happened to the damsel except that she was hoarse of voice, and later returned to her normal state; for this reason, I say that in cutting the epiglottis, one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	of the swollen throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 These abscesses are called "goiter hernias", and are large abscesses in the color of a lump, and are very common in women; and is according to two manners: natural and accidental; where the natural one has no remedy.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And the accidental is according to two manners, one of which resembles fat, and the other manner resembles an abscess coming from an artery; and there is fear, and one should not operate with force except in the one that is small, and test and examine the entire inserted part: if you find it like ordinary fat, and it does not bleed in any way, then cut it as you would cut fat, and pull it out entirely, if there is any; and search thoroughly, and cure it as it should be, until it heals perfectly.
des nous	of the nuts (or: of the swellings)
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 Many ways there are, which I will tell you all the similarities; and now it is necessary that I say all the difference that is between abscess and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that a dislocation is heat and fever-holding, as long as the boiling (of blood or humors) has not passed, and the putrefaction is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 With an abscess there is no heat, fever, or pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a blister and becomes swollen; and there are two similarities, either fatty or moist, and very colored as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the new (dislocation), that you first test and inquire about all the instruments which are called "entromissoire", according to the form that comes in the chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 And the manner of inquiring about abscesses is that you take the moistest place that you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers back and forth, until you know that the instrument has penetrated the core, then according to the size of the abscess; then extract the intruder, and be careful not to let it burst.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If moisture runs and collects, let it have its color, and incise it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the incision, moisture does not come out, know that it is fat, then incise it in a cross shape, and take it with tongs, and gently scrape it from each side and towards the shirt it lies on so that you pull it out whole with the cloth; and if you cannot pull it out whole, tear it apart piece by piece so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 For if anything remains, the inflammation will return many times; and if some remains and the blood bothers you, apply corrosive powders to the wound, bind it up, and place something soothing for abscesses that is warm on it, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and if the swelling is large, then cut the two edges of the wound and treat what festers in the flesh.
