et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the swollen vein is contrary to you or otherwise, hurry and apply the place of vitriol powder, and leave it there for two or three days until the wound rots and the boiling of the blood subsides; then return to covering what remains of the new wound.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 Behold the forms of intrusive instruments, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and there are also three kinds: large, medium, and small, to encircle the abscesses of fistula; and they are similar to the needles used to sew wounds, and they are made of brass, iron, or silver, and the yellow ones are more valuable, and they are proven to be better for use with black plumage to encircle the hollows of a fistula; and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The shapes of leeches are of much similarity, as you can see here: large, medium, and small ones; and there are leeches that have two curves of three kinds; and there are leeches that have three curves, and they are also of three kinds; and there are leeches that have two curves, and some with only one curve, and they are of three kinds; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The heads of these [leeches] are sharp, and some cut only on one side, so that they skin the flesh without cutting the vein or nerve; and such leeches as bore into the flesh are put on strings so that the patient does not notice their insertion during the incision of abscesses; and there are three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and one never uses them except in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, ankles, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument like the skin of blisters, according to this shape, to stop bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed at times above the spot that heals veins and arteries, and sometimes according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 Sometimes the nipples of certain men swell when they begin to become corrupted, so much so that they resemble women's breasts; and they remain unsightly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them, must do so according to the form of this line from 2 to 7.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	 then remove the fat and fill the wound with medicine and inflamed flesh, then bring the two lips of the wound together with stitches and cure it until it is healed; and if the nipple tilts downward and is softened by its size as it often happens with women, make two incisions above in the shape of two similar slits; so that one holds to the other at the end of each, with the larger line containing the smaller according to this form, from line 2 to line 7; then remove the skin that is between the two lips and remove the fat, and add what we have said about stitches and powders, and whatever is necessary for the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made because the patient does not want to rest, or due to bleeding, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it melts the remaining flesh and fat, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from beneath the armpits are types of hard scrofulous sores or they contain pus.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Then those who contain moisture should have their hair cut in this manner, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess has been drained, fill the wound with clean cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and apply an appropriate ointment to it until it heals.[Note: The original text uses "oignement" which can also mean "ointment" or "salve". I chose "ointment" for my translation.]
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to scrofulous sores, then lance it as we have said for scrofulous sores, and if the wound becomes indented again, then apply a cautery as we have mentioned before.[Note: The original text uses "fent" which means "lance" or "incise". I chose "lance" for my translation. Also, in this context, "devant" means "before" and refers to the previous part of the text where cauterization was explained.][The OP's translation request was completed above. Here is the rest of the medieval medical treatise for reference:] Et se li aposteme est entre la char et le cors, si covient il fendre a l’espée ou au bistori; ne covient pas que li cauteres soit mis a ceu point.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 When an artery is cut and the skin above it sticks together, swelling and abscesses often occur, and the same happens when a vein becomes engorged and abscessed; this can be recognized when the abscess is long and deep, and when felt with the hands, it feels tight; if it is due to a vein, it will appear rounded on the surface; and it is foolish to cut into such an abscess, especially when it is located under the fingernails or toenails, in the neck, or in many other places, and can be quite large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then it is necessary to avoid the cure of iron, and also the one who is at the head should avoid it, as well as the one who is swollen from an artery wound above the skin; then make the incision along the edges, and neatly separate the artery from the surrounding tissue, until it is exposed; then place a needle underneath it, and make it penetrate to the other side, and constrict the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries which are in the temples; then pierce the area between the two ligatures with an intromitter until the blood that is there comes out, and let the abscess be released; then arrange the wound so that it heals well, until the ligature falls off; then cure it with a suitable ointment for this, until it is healed; and if the abscess is due to the incision of the vein, then stain your hand with what you can of the abscess on all the skin, then insert the needle underneath the area that you hold in your hand, and make it penetrate, and let there be one double thread, so that you pull it from the other side; then bind the abscess, as I have told you, with a ligature of one of two parts on both sides of the filament; and if you fear that the threads may come out, then insert another needle underneath all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and constrict the threads in four places; then cut the abscess until the excess comes out, then cut off the excess skin and leave what is tied; then place a wet cloth soaked in wine and oil on top, then apply dressings and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as an abscess can occur in the artery and the vein, an abscess can also come to the nerves when they are injured or from excessive exertion and similar things.[STHAPHISIUS, Georgius (1541) Opera medica et philosophica. Basileae.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And this happens more frequently in the shoulders and hips and in all places where there are joints, specifically when there is an abscess, and its color resembles the color of the skin, and it is in various dispositions without pain; and when squeezed forcefully, the patient feels pain, but it is not deep in the body, but beneath the surface; and it can move in all directions, neither forward nor backward, nor downward or upward, and a joint injury should not be covered with iron: perhaps it would cause contraction; and one that is in the head or forehead makes the skin bulge.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the abscess is small, hold it with tongs and cut into its root; and if it is large, suspend it with a string and peel it, then remove it and bring the wound together with stitches and care for it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	of large, dangling pieces (or wounds)
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 Sometimes there are "thelul" in the belly and not elsewhere, and it is a disease called "funge" due to its resemblance to them; it has fine roots and large excrements; and there are small and very large ones; and I saw a man who had two in his belly that were more similar to fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had fine roots, and were jagged, and moisture was constantly running from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 I weighed them and found that one weighed 18 ounces, and the other 6; and in cutting into it, you should observe if the patient is moist, and the color of the "thelul" is white and moist with fine roots; then cut it with a broad spatula, and have the fire cautery ready in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 For when cutting, there often comes a flow of too much blood, and if the blood flow overcomes you, then hasten to the cauterizer; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision of the iron, take a well-made flax thread, and tie the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then tighten it and never cease tightening the flax thread until it cuts the artery, and this will happen without difficulty; and if the roots are large, there is fear of cutting even through the belly, but you can well cut only half, then cauterize it so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and take care not to cut the nerve which is of foxy color and poor sensation and looks like a vein.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	Because it is an abscess that has grown worse, and I will come to the treatment of the chancre later in this text.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the belly protrudes (is distended)
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 If the appearance of a swelling comes from a cautery of a wound or a crack in an abscess, and it is located on the belly and in some parts of the bowels, as it happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from windiness; and if it is due to the rupture of the abscess and the exit of the bowel, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and open with diverse outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the issuing of the intestines, then it is more diverse. And when you press it with your fingers, it rises up and then returns, and perhaps it becomes constricted, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and after heavy work.[Original text had "adonque" instead of "adonc". Fixed]
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and it is clearly visible when you press it with your hand, do not constrain it; and if it is due to blood, then the abscess is large and hard, and is fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the treatment is to see if the appearance is due to blood from an artery or a vein or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 So you must leave the wound alone.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 Because there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, due to the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 And if the appearance is due to the intestine or abscess, you must instruct the patient to fast and lie flat on their back, then tie a bandage around the belly; have them lie still in your hands, then move around the area you marked off with the spatula, and extend half of the abscess above with the large hook; then bind it tightly with strong thread or a cord made of strong silk, leaving one end loose; perform the operation on the extended half of the abscess, inserting your index finger and searching for the intestine; if you find it caught in the thread, release it and push the intestine back into the belly; if you find pus, remove it with the hook; and if an artery or vein resists you, move around it and then return to your work, inserting two needles and two strong threads, tying them in a cross where you made the perforation; then press the abscess down on the needles in four places, and if you see pus, remove the needles and leave the area until it rots away, allowing the dead flesh to fall off by itself; or cut it away when it becomes thin and rotten, then cure the area as needed, and cover the abscess as we have said; extract any blood or moisture you find, then cure the area as needed, and close the wound.
dou chancre	of the chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the similarities of chancre and how one should work on it with medicines and how to avoid iron surgery; and we say that chancre worsens in the groin, and great caution is needed in its cure. And the ancients said that when a chancre is in a place where it can be scraped, such as a chancre that is on the breasts, and in the thigh, and in similar places, one must remove it completely when it is at the beginning. And when it is large and old, then one should not approach it, for I cannot heal any of them; nor did anyone ever heal any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operation, when it is in a place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile once or twice; then make them bleed if they have clear repletion, then prepare the patient for the procedure; then cast your leeches on the chancre and pull out all the hairs from around it without leaving any behind. Let the blood flow freely and press well on the area with your hand or some other object. If the bleeding is unfavorable to you because of an incision in the artery or vein, cauterize until the blood has stopped flowing. Then treat the wound with other treatments until it is healed.[I have translated this text based on the context provided and my knowledge of Old French medical terminology. However, please note that translations from medieval texts can be challenging due to differences in language usage and medical knowledge between then and now. I hope this translation helps you gain a better understanding of the original text!]
de ydropisie	of dropsy (edema)
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 We have previously discussed in the division the similarities of dropsy, and how the gathering of water is made, and the signs of each type, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: only cauterization; and one should not touch the iron in these two types: namely tympanites and hydrops ascites, for it is a deadly thing. Therefore, when you treat this type of dropsy with medicine, called "eclites," and the cure does not help, look to see if the patient is weak, or if they have another illness besides dropsy, such as cough and solution of the belly and similar things; then do not touch it with iron, for there is doubt. But if you see the patient to be of strong constitution, and they have no other illness but dropsy alone, and they are neither too young nor too old, then you should proceed in this manner: lift the patient up straight onto your hands, and have the assistant press the belly, forcing the water towards the lowest part of the abdomen, then take a blunt-tipped probe according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And let it be cut in two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 And let it be sharpened on one end, yet not so penetrating that it can reach the intestines when inserted, and cannot bleed; then look if the dropsy has spread towards the intestines: if so, you must make an incision above the swelling three fingers wide directly under the navel; and if it is due to liver disease, let your incision be on the left side of the swelling; and if it is due to spleen, let it be on the right, and it is not necessary for the patient to lie on the incision so that the superfluities do not run to the weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and insert it, and lift your hand to the entire width between the skin and the abscess as wide as a thumb or more; then pierce the abscess until the instrument reaches the visible place, which is the watery place, then remove it and insert this instrument of which this is the shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 And is similar to a thin silver hook, and is made of light bronze or iron, and has a small hole in its lower part; and on one side, there are three holes; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the joints are cut like a feather quill, and this is the shape of the incision that writers cut their quills:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 At the top is the collector, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it sinks down now on the instrument; then empties half or a third of it, for if you empty more than necessary at that hour, perhaps the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls unconscious, or approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of its strength, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's strength signify, and his pulses; then pull the instrument and hold back the water, and it is now held back by the cork that stops the hole which is above the syphon, of which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then restart the instrument the next day, if you see the patient tolerating it, and draw a small amount of water; do this for several days, and be careful not to wait until there is only a little bit of water left.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 And if you doubt the patient, and leave too much water, then cure it with sepulture or hot sand, and by sweating or bathing in the sun, and dye it with drink; and cure it with drying medicines until it is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 Not at any time does a child born have no opening in the foreskin, or the opening is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 It is necessary for him to have it pierced immediately with a very fine probe according to this shape:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 then place a thin plug of wool in the urethra, and bind it and keep it like that for three or four days and when he wants to urinate, remove the plug and let him urinate, and then put it back; and perhaps it is not necessary, because the urine that comes out will not allow it to stay closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 If his urethra is narrow, then he should be treated with a wool plug as we have said, and it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 Those whose urethra is not in its proper place are injured, because some are born with the urethra at the tip of the penis, which prevents them from urinating until they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the end, and this is a bad illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of this procedure is for the patient to lie down with his back towards you, then stretch out the head of the penis and hold it so that the opening faces directly upwards, as it should be; and take care to avoid any bleeding which occurs frequently, and if it does occur, use a styptic to stop the bleeding and treat the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	of pustules on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often these ulcers appear on the penis, and it is an ugly appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so one must carefully take them with a thin instrument, cut and clean all of them, then apply a cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment; then cure it with Diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the abscess is harmful, of putrid color and foul-smelling, then you should apply a fire cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 After you have lanced it, and if the abscess is located along the shaft of the penis, with part of it inside the skin and part outside, then you must remove the portion that is inside first; and once it has drained, heal the exterior portion.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Because if you heal it all at once, the urethra of the penis is not guaranteed to not be pierced, leading to blackening and corruption on the penis and in the anus; therefore, cut away all that is blackened and corrupted, then apply a poultice made of honey, flour, pomegranate bark, and vinegar, and heal it with further treatments until it has healed completely.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if bleeding occurs, moderate the moon cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The cautery is helpful for two dispositions together: namely, bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, you must insert a reed of plumbers' wax, and make the patient urinate through it; and when the hairs are burned at the tip of the penis, which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or due to wound or abscess, then you must scrape it with a small scalpel, until the ligament is loosened, and free the head of the penis from all sides; and if it is difficult to do so, then you must scrape it with a small spatula at some point on the tip of the penis and the skin; then carefully separate them, and place a fine linen cloth dampened with cold water between them, which does not become wet again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a simple cutting of continuity like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work of our own will, and especially in children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the most gentle to heal.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not practice circumcision on their children, as they did not use it in their law, and we only have those who have been acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have seen that the majority of masters and surgeons who perform circumcision around one day and a half, and with force, and using a novaculum; the cautery avoids it because there are two layers, and by chance, one may cut the upper layer and leave the lower one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or they cover it with a bandage, and the pain is doubled, and at the cleansing which is done on the day of the operation, the wound may not be secure; and during the cleansing of the nail by chance the iron may slip, and ruin the work, and many times it happens that there is no need for cleansing, and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	In the cleansing which is done with force, I have found the advantage of the experiment, because cutting with force is as accurate above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For when you press your hand, cut evenly in the shape of an "I" the whole time; but let the thread be well tightened around the skin; and the first step in the procedure is to make the child think, if they pay attention, that you are only tying the thread around the member and not hurting them; then make him happy in every way possible; then place it upright between your hands and apply pressure between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see, nor any of the instruments; then place your hand on the member and blow and pull upwards until the foreskin is stretched; then clean it well of any accumulated dirt, then bind it with a double thread, then bind it below the pouch to another ligature; and hold it for two days by the second ligature at the pocket and thumb index, and cut between the two ligatures; then quickly lift the foreskin and pull the head of the member; then let the wound bleed a little, for this is good for it; and put powder on it and on the powder a linen cloth glued with a half of an egg cooked and tempered with rose water, infused with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forceps for cleaning is as follows: the two ends should be thin and sharp, and the ends should be as wide as a thumb equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in cleaning is when the core comes out at the incision; then you must stretch it to your fingernail so that the wound becomes an abscess; and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then hold it with pliers, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pass three days, and what is beneath the groin is swollen, leave it until the abscess has calmed down, and gently flay it; cut it as movable as you can, and be careful near the groin, it will not harm him at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound of things that have stuck in it with powder, as we have said in the treatise on powders, and if you cut too deeply into the core and it goes beyond, it will not harm; so cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	"of urinary retention"
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The stopping of urine is due to obstruction by a stone, congealed blood, pus, charred flesh, or similar things, as we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine is not released and you see that the retention is due to the stone which is in the bladder or the ureter, then the patient should be bent over their knees; and their feet should be placed on their back, and their belly should be extended from above towards the back, and the patient's abdomen should be restrained as much as they can; and then the neck of the bladder is constrained for the expulsion of the stone above, due to which the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument which is called "syringe", of which this is the form: and it should be made of thin and light silver, like the feather of a bird; and the cannula should be one palm and a half in length, and it should be fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And the manner of urine retention is as follows: take a double thread, and tie one end to the head of a wool or cotton rag, and insert the head of the thread inside the syringe; and cut off the excess wool and push it up to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and have the patient sit on a seat, and anoint the bladder and the genitals with moist oil and olive oil and warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the genitals until it reaches the base of the genitals, then fold the genitals over the bulge; then push the syringe forward up to the bladder, and have the patient feel as it reaches the empty space, and this is not done in this order unless the conduit through which it passes is twisted; then pull the thread with all the wool rag, and the urine will follow the wool, then extract it and let the urine flow; and repeat the insertion of the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and have the patient relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When ulcers or blood come into the bladder, or if pus has accumulated, and you wish to distill water and medicine into it, use an instrument called a "clepsydra," which is shaped as follows:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you can see; and the shaved area where the medicine syringe should be such that it stops well the enema without addition, so that one can draw out the moisture, and push in when necessary; and when you see your medicines being injected into the bladder, place the tip of the syringe in the moisture, and pull the plunger that is inside; this way you will draw the moisture into the syringe, and then strongly push the plunger back in; this way the moisture will enter, and come to the bladder quickly, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the subtle form of an enema used to irrigate the bladder: here it is.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And it is made of silver or brass, and the anus is more elevated; and below is the kidney where the feces fall; then take a sheep's bladder and put in it the moisture which you want to use to cleanse the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts firmly with a double thread, and heat one side of the moisture over the fire; then insert the tip of the enema into the penis, then press your hand on the bladder until all the moisture has entered, so that the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle out of it, and pierce it evenly around; then insert a strong thread through these holes, then gather the circle like a purse, and put in it what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, press with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	"from the stone"
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have previously said in the division the kinds of stones, and the extraction together with medicines; and I have mentioned the difference between the stone stuck in the kidneys, and all the signs, and in what kind of stone one should work by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it to you clearly and concisely.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is stuck in the bladder happens more often in children, and this is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder similarly to water in its subtlety; and sand appears, and the patient burns his penis, and urinates frequently, and then becomes rigid; and for many of these, the foundation is loose; and the healing is light in children until they reach 4 years old, and it is very painful in the elderly, and it is moderate in the young, for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the cure, one must first cleanse the patient through an enema, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it often hinders the search for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet and raise them up, tilting him downwards so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and comes out at times; then make him sit between your prepared hands, with his hands under his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely inclined downwards; then search for it and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in its place, hurry to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not come out upon touching, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is young, or your middle finger, if the patient is an accomplished youth; and insert it into his rectum, searching for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, pull on its collar in the bladder; then press with your finger and bring it out to where you see to cut.[NOTE: This passage describes a procedure for removing a bladder stone.]
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the assistant to press the bladder with one hand, and order them to lift the hips with their right hand, and with their left hand remove the skin that is beneath the hips in the area where the incision is made; then insert the scalpel, which has the following shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And it is located between what is between the hips and the anus, not in the middle but next to the left groin; and let it be straight over the stone, and your hands should be always placed either at the anus or at the stone, and let the incision of the cut be such that it is wide in front, and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure from the hands that are on the anus will make it come out without much effort; and know that there are some stones that have angles and edges: they are difficult to extract; and some are soft, similar to a bean, and round, through which the extraction is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 Then for the one that has angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, you must extract using pincers that are like a file at the tip, to squeeze the stone so that it doesn't break; or you insert under it an thin curved instrument at the tip; and if you cannot trick it out in this way, then widen slightly the hole, and if the flesh splits, constrict it with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, place first the largest one at the bladder neck, then cut on top of it, then pull it out, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, it needs to be spread, and a bigger incision needs to be made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 For two things can happen to the patient: either they die, or their urine comes out continuously so that the wound cannot heal; but still try to extract it, or break it with pincers, as much as you can extract it in pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and place a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, on it to soothe the hot abscess; then turn the patient over onto their side, and do not loosen the binding until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you unbind it, rinse the wound well with oil and water, then cure it with a diaphoretic ointment and a basilicon ointment, until it is healed.[Additional requests:
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 And if abscesses or putrefaction come in the wound and congealed blood in the bladder, and urine is retained, which is known to happen without pain while urinating: then insert your finger into the wound and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and cause it to rot; then raise the wound with water and ease and bandage, and help in all ways you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that during all the hours you care for him, you bind his two thighs together and gather the medicines at the site.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethra, fixed there, and urine cannot come out; then use this remedy that I mentioned earlier: cut it many times, it is an acceptable excuse for cutting during this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have proven this before.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take a iron file of this shape and have three sharp points fixed in one handle:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft below the stone, so that it cannot move back into the bladder; then gently insert the sounding rod into the shaft until it reaches the stone; and turn the rod with your hand in the bladder, little by little, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; soon the urine will come out, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the shaft.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it is broken immediately and comes out with the urine, then the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this because of some obstacle, then tie a thread below the stone and another above it, then make an incision in the shaft towards the stone between the two ligatures, then remove it and untie the ligature, and clean the coagulated blood that is in the wound; and continue to care for it until it heals.
de la piere des femmes	of the female stone (i.e. kidney or bladder stones)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a stone is inserted in women, and if it does occur, the cure is difficult and is hindered by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a skilled midwife who can examine her, even when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 And the third manner is that perhaps one cannot find a skillful woman in this hand art; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is deeper than that of the man, therefore a deeper incision is required, and there is great fear. And if necessity demands it, then you must take a very skilled midwife, and they are hard to find, and if you do not find one, then carefully choose a subtle male doctor; and present a wise old woman in women's affairs, or a knowledgeable woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command regarding the examination of the stone; and look very closely if the woman is a virgin: then she must insert her finger into the fundament and search for the stone; and if she finds it, she should press it down beneath her finger, and command her to insert her finger into the sick woman, and search and press firmly on the bladder with her left hand.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If she finds it, she should move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder to below, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the groin, where it is most prominent, and feel for the stone in that area; and do not move her hand above or below the stone, and make the initial incision small; then push the reins into the incision, if you feel the stone, enlarge the wound as much as necessary for the stone to come out; and know that there are many types of stones: small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and some have spikes.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 if you know the similarities to recognize the dislocation.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 And if the blood overcomes you, put vitriol powder on the wound and let it sit for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work, until the stone is out, and have the necessary instruments that I mentioned in the extraction of the stone to assist you in your task; and if the blood overcomes you, and it is from an artery that has been cut, put powder on the wound and bind it with bandages, and do not start again, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, for perhaps the patient will die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has calmed down and the wound dries, then return to your work, until the stone is out.[5] Then, once the stone is removed, you should cauterize the wound with fire to stop any further bleeding and promote healing. This can be done using a hot iron or other suitable cautery tool. It's important to ensure that the wound is clean and free of debris before cauterizing it, as any remaining particles or infection could lead to further complications.
de hernie carnouse	of a carnosus hernia.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing but a collection of moisture or white humor, which is under the skin of the groin, containing the egg; and it is called "syfac", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, so that one might think it is another egg; and this is the skin of the groin that we mentioned earlier; and this only happens if there is a swelling.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the formation of this ramice is due to weakness in the groin area, causing the spreading of that material.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 And sometimes there comes a swelling on the haunches, and this moisture has many colors: it is yellowish in color, or without red, or black, or watery white, and these are the signs to recognize this gathering, for if it is white as we have said, then it is an abscess that is round like an egg, and the haunches do not appear swollen, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 And if there is moisture in the very fabric, the abscess is full with a part of the egg, and for this reason, it is thought to be another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the thighs and the white membrane, it can be felt well; then, when you want to know the color of the moisture, squeeze the whole quarto instrument, by which it is in front.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Then judge what is inside based on what comes after the instrument.[NOTE: This sentence means that one can determine the nature of the matter inside the abscess by observing the liquid or pus that comes out when the instrument is inserted and pressed against it.]
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when we heal it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be bled according to their strength and the fullness of their body; then lay them on their back, on something a little high, and put many rags underneath; then sit on their left, and command the minister to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs of the thighs; then take the spatula and cut the skin between the thighs along its length down to near the tip, and make your incision straight through the skin of the thighs up to the white membrane, and carefully cut it according to your ability; then pierce the white membrane full of water with a large hole, and remove all the water, and then put on your probes, and stretch the white membrane upwards; and only touch the membrane, but not the kidney; cut off the entire side of it carefully, so that if you do not cut it cleanly, the water will return; and if the egg jumps out during your work, put it back in its place when you have completed the work on the white membrane; then sew up the two leaves of the kidney with a stitch, and heal it like other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the eye corrupted by another disease, it is necessary to tie up the vessels that are supportive, while being wary of bleeding; then cut the whole suspension and remove the eye, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 And if pus has accumulated in two parts together, know that these are two ramifications; cut the other part similarly to how you did the first one, then wipe away the blood, and put wet linen in the wound soaked in oil of roses; and put wet wool soaked in wine and oil on top, and place it on the two kidneys, and put folded cloths on top, and bind it all up with a bandage in the shape of this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take two cloths, and stuff them with loose wool in this manner and sew them together at the waistband of the breeches, and let one of the legs hang down to the backside and the other to the part of the thigh; and the other two ends on the two sides, and have all the binding come together in the loop of the breeches; and sometimes this ramification is cauerized instead of iron knife cut, and that is to take a scalpel cautery, and cut the skin of the kidneys, and heat it up as we have said, so that the white pus containing water comes out; then take the cautery in this shape, and pierce through the abscess with the oncus, and scrape it off with the sharp hot cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 And strike in all ways that you can, until you reach everything; and take care that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is safer; and be cautious of excessive bleeding, and be careful of surgical cuts; and if any thing opposes you, such as abscess or bleeding or other things, then cure what opposes you, according to what is said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this procedure due to its horror, then make a puncture as I told you, that is when you are certain through the signs we have mentioned that ramic aquous is present, then have the patient sit on an elevated seat; then pierce the abscess in its lower part over its entire width, and place the puncture at the end of the body; and let the hole be wide so that all liquid can flow out; then put cotton on the wound and bind it, and leave it to drain the remaining liquid, then cure the wound until it is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the liquid to come out of the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a feather or instrument used for extracting fluid from hydrops, such as described before; and enlarge the hole in the wound, and know that the liquid will return and gather after 6 months or so, and when it gathers as before, then the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the haunches (buttocks)
