Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 A formica (ant) is a small ulcerous lesion that appears near the body and goes deep inside; sometimes it is found by touch and feels like a dead person's trembling, and it spreads throughout the body, especially in the hands more than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	 And the treatment is that you take a quill from a goose feather or a strong vulture feather and place that quill on the trembling (lesion) until the circle encompasses the trembling all around; then turn your hand around the entire quill so that you scrape all around the trembling, pushing it in deep, and extract the trembling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, make one of iron or steel in this shape, and let it be thin underneath and wide on top.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	but not piercing, in order to hold it on the finger and press it; And if you wish, cauterize the spine with fire, as described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	in the shape of an enema.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes, a enema is made of silver or copper, or molten tin or lead; and sometimes it is made with these instruments, both large and small, depending on who they are prepared for.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Then those that are prepared for the treatment of children and weak, suffering individuals are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of a small or large enema is as follows: the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	 and there is a dislocation where the belly is swollen, as you see, and the anus is pierced; and there are two openings on one side and one on the other; and let the belly be where one puts medicines from an animal bladder or parchment, and let it be pierced all around with small holes, and have one finger's width of space between each hole, then insert a strong thread twisted in the shape of an X or O into these holes, and bind the belly as if it were a sack; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then perform an enema; and this is the form of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	 And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the tip of the enema with oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then insert it gently; then the minister presses it with both hands together until it is completely inserted, then remove the enema, and raise the patient's legs in the air, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it come out as much as it can; and if he sleeps a whole night, it will be a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you give an enema to a patient with a disorder of the belly, and the medicine quickly comes out, then administer it again until it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	 And if there are piles or abscesses on the fundament, let the enema be as fine as for a child; and this is the shape of the fine enema that the leather should be constricted around:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have previously said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments for hands and remedies, according to the completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and by what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 The things by which wounds are made are: striking with a stone, cutting with a sword or knife, or with a lance or staff or arrow, or similar things; or they are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, starting with simple wounds of the head, for the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from a strike of a stone or similar things, and the skin is torn open and the wound is large, and you suspect a hot abscess: then have it immediately purged of the cephalic (relating to the head) itself if there is little bleeding from the wound, and let the incision be contrary to the injured part; and empty the patient of repletion of wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if he does not want to be purged, let his food be diminished, and let him not drink wine, nor eat meat or animal flesh; and place on the wound, if hot abscesses come there, cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in stiptic wine; and if there is no hot abscess, but it is fresh and of whole blood, and has not been exposed to air, then place a powder (which I will mention shortly) on it; and if the wound has been exposed to fire, then place some poultices on it until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like that of a sword cut and similar ones, and the lips cannot come together with sutures, then bring them together with stitches, as I will describe for belly wounds, using stitches.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 If the wound is exposed to the bone, and is gaping and only holds together by a small amount, then cut it; afterwards, cure the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat solid foods, such as heads and roasted barley, as well as similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if you find rotten flesh on the skin, and it is not attached to the bone, then cut away all of the rotten flesh and discard it, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or a vein, that cannot be stopped with medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it dislocated, then tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is easy: it consists of applying this powder which promotes healing once the surgeon has cleaned the wound.[INTRO\_NOTE] Here's a continuation of your medieval French medical treatise. I hope my previous translations were helpful to you! Let me know if there's anything else I can assist you with.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And the manner of the powder is as follows: take one part of incense; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and finely powder them, and apply it to the wound, and bind it firmly, until it dries well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it securely, and leave it unbound if it does not swell; for the medicine is not removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes only quicklime is used, when incense and dragon's blood are not available, but the wound has already been treated by the physician.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the cancer has corrupted the wound, do not put this powder on it; but apply some digestive ointments or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it suppurates; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And if a bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with delicate forceps; and I will tell you later about skull fractures.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck[fn]
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, it has no difference with that of the head, unless the sinews of the neck or the arteries are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 If it is the nerve, there is no other remedy but to leave the wound alone and not apply anything restricting, for that harms nerves and makes them retract; and do not place anything cold on the wound, for the substance of nerves is cold, and their connection is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be mild, such as lime washed in clean water, and mixed with rose oil, and also a similar mild ointment. And use moist dressings.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew it up and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it has healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wounds are deep and swollen and full of pus, pierce it in a lower location; and if an artery is cut and there is a flow of blood, tie it off, and bind it up, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the conduits are preserved, so that food passes, then sew the windpipe to the ridge of the throat, and do not touch the throat but return it to its natural shape; and then bind it appropriately, and leave it for some days, then cure it with discarded salves until it is healed; and if the wound has left an impression on the bone, seek it out; and if there are pieces of bone, pull them all out if you can, and those that you cannot, leave until the wound rots, and becomes loosened and straightened; and if the wound is fresh, powder onto it the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, cure it in this way as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 If it is a spear or knife blow, and the wound is deep, look if from the wound there is an exit of wind (air) while the patient is breathing: then know that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder in it at first, nor bind it so that the blood does not coagulate in depth, and returns to the heart, and quickly kills the patient; but put attractive ointment on it, and bind it two times a day; and if you don't have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for 3 days, or 4, or more; then there will not come spasms, nor bad tremors of heart, nor stranguria (painful urination); and when you see good dispositions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Heal then the abscess and other wounds, until it is healed; and if it cannot heal, recognize that there is a fistula; and heal it as it should be done.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, whether on the belly, side or back, heal the front part of it; if it is large, with sutures; and if it is small, with powder; and if it is close to the bone and there are pieces torn off, then clean the wound and pull out the fragments if they are separated; and if they are not separated, then let the wound rot, which will make the extractions easier. And judgement for wounds on other limbs is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	"the rupture (or tear) of the belly" or "the perforation of the abdominal wall" could also be possible translations for "dou derrompement dou ventre".
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 The ruptures of the belly are great, medium, and small; sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines come out from a large wound, and the suturing is more difficult, and often the small wound is worse than the large one, because the intestines are harder to put back in, if they are not put back in hot against hot; for the intestines swell immediately upon feeling the cold, and therefore they enter back in more easily, and therefore it is better to leave the middle-sized wound open, so that the intestines can be more easily returned to their place. And know that the ruptures of the belly are according to four manners: the two common sutures happen in the suture of the belly, and the suturing of other wounds of the body and the two other common sutures are specific to other wounds; and yet they are more appropriate with the suturing of the belly, and I will describe each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestines is outside, and it is difficult to put back, this can be done in one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And when it is cold, warm it in the following way: moisten a sponge or a piece of cloth in warm water only, or cook it in a decoction of wormwood, cypress, and pepper, and sprinkle the intestines until the swelling is removed; and sometimes use this wine to compress, and it is often effective for reducing swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when you see the swelling separate, soften the intestines with liquids, such as broths of healthy or slimy and bad tasting foods, for this eases the opening for little things; and if it cannot enter, make an incision in the wound with a surgical instrument used to cut piles; and the first remedy is more important than the cutting, that nothing should be cut without great necessity; and this is the instrument to split [it]: cut inside the curve and not through, and see the shape [here].
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines protrude, replace it in its natural shape and place if you have the power to do so, for this is better than cutting.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 When the wound is large, and it is in the lower abdominal area, then you should make the patient lie on their back and place their legs higher than their head. And if it is in the lower abdomen, then you should place the head and chest higher than the injured parts. And similarly, if the rupture of the abdomen is in one of the two parts, then you should ensure that the injured part is higher than the other. And it is necessary to treat large and medium-sized wounds as I have described.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 For small wounds, prepare what you need, then take a piece of linen cloth and hold the entire wound with your hand, bringing the edges together. This is the common method of stitching, which consists of taking a needle or more, depending on the size of the wound, leaving a space at the edge of the wound, and inserting a needle with strong thread. Pierce both sides of the skin with the tips of the siphac, which are beneath the skin, as far as you can penetrate that part, and bring the two ends of the siphac together. Then wrap a double thread around the needle twice, bringing the edges of the wound together, leaving space again, and inserting another needle. Tie the thread as you did with the first needle, repeating this process as needed until the entire wound is stitched. The needles should be of medium size, neither too fine nor too thick, because fine needles cut through all the flesh, and overly thick ones cannot penetrate well. It is important not to insert the needles too far from the skin and flesh, so as not to reopen the wound before it heals. Once the wound is stitched, trim the ends of the needle so they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and place bandages or cloth on the needle ends to keep them in place until the wound heals. This method of stitching with needles is best for small wounds. For the second type of stitching, a single needle or two are sufficient. The common method is to bring the edges of the skin and siphac together with a single needle and strong thread. Once you have pierced all four layers, pull the needle back to where you started, as one does when sewing fabric. Leave space between each stitch equivalent to the width of a finger. This type of stitching is known by people, and I stitched a wound that a man had on his stomach, which was injured by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm’s breadth wide, with two palms’ breadth of intestines protruding, and it was located in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I set the intestines back in place after they had been outside for twenty-four hours, and the wound was healed after fifteen days, and I treated it, and it was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 And the physicians had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine; and I placed clean, old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle and insert it from the outside in; when it has pierced straight through to the other side, place the tip of the siphac or thread where you inserted the needle, and make it pierce from the inside out on the other side; and the technique for this stitch is such that you sew just as a pelterer does with furs, leaving the siphac exposed on one side and picking it up again on the other, until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 The second manner of stitching, which Galen properly calls, is when one brings together two natural parts, and applies one part of the edge to the other part in such a way: insert a needle or head of the thread close by, and make it pierce that place only, and leave the two sides of the wound; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outside to the inside, to the two sides of the wound; then make both pierce from the outside to the inside, in two other holes of the thread which are on the other side; and this is the stronger manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galen says this word, and some testify, that one must stitch the belly with two needles, each having a thread; and one should insert one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew leather; and know that when the wound is in the middle of the belly, the stitches are more difficult than on other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The judgments of the wound are as follows, just like the judgments of other wounds: and that is when you find the wound fresh, with all its blood, so that the flesh has moved aside, then replace the intestines and the cut; then put powder on dried flesh on it, and if the flesh has moved aside, then put any nearby ointment on it, as long as the wound is still open; and clean the threads, and let the sutures and the miraculum be fastened; then cure the wound like the others, until it is healed; and if you don't have medicines, then put on old cotton, as soon as it begins to close, and move it two times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 For you do not need any other medicine in many cases when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound may communicate with the principal members, then you should moisten light linen in moderately warm oil, or in rose oil, and place it around the edges, and beneath the armpits; and if he feels pain or putrefaction in the belly, and this often happens, then you should enema him with warm black wine, and similarly if the putrefaction reaches the intestines; and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine called "jeun" cannot be healed when it is wounded, and this is due to the multiplicity of veins that are there, and the delicacy of its entire body, and its similarity in nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 And if the ear falls out of the wound, put it back in place as you would with the intestines, while it is still fresh; and if it is old and turned black or blue, tie off the blackened area to prevent bleeding, since there are veins and arteries there; then cut away the tissue between the tied-off area and place the two pieces hanging down from the part beneath the wound outside in order to lighten the extraction when the ear falls out, and let the wound heal.
de la routure dou boueil	of the break (opening) of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 When the intestines are prolapsed and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, because I saw that a man was stabbed in the abdomen with a lance; and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and became swollen and developed into a fistula, and there came out excrement and gas; I treated it as best I could, and did not stop working on it until it healed and the wound closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 And when I saw it soldered, I feared that the patient would have pain in his belly; and he had no pain, but rather improved and began to eat and drink; and some experienced ones said that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be bound in such a manner: take large bandages, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the bandage has opened its mouth, place it on the two edges so that it pulls its mouth taut; and then cut off the head of the bandage, and this holds so that it cannot become undone, then put another bandage in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely covered; and stitch the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 The head of this instrument is heated in the interior, and it brings no harm to the patient, and one can suture the interior with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in such a manner: take the head of this intestine thread that is very dehorned, and then tie the head of this thread to a thin twisted linen thread, then put the thread on the needle and sew the intestine, and pull it together in the incision; and this method of suturing is not outside the path of trust and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, even when it is in one of the large intestines, there is no device or cure, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or where it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that every wound or abscess, when it matures, is commonly called "fistula," and similarly when it breaks open and discharges pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 And a fistula is, in truth, a hard and white nodulation that is painless and as hollow as the feather of a bird; sometimes clear and thin, other times thick; sometimes little pus, and other times quite a bit; and I have spoken in the classification of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is not due to anything but one of the Nine causes: namely, due to the small amount of blood or flesh; or due to its badness; or because there is hardened flesh inside and on the edges, which does not allow flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the place is rotten, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine used for treatment is not good; or due to corruption that is similar to a plague; or due to the property of the region being slow in digestion, healing slowly, and swelling by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and cures with medicines in the classification.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary for me to make known to you the treatment of a fistula which is made by handiwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Know that a fistula can occur in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from the great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the syphilis, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to some joint of the hands or feet; and some reach the property of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And all fistulas of this kind are of difficult healing, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not reach the place I mentioned, and you have trust in the cure, and you recognize it, then take a probe of iron or of steel, if the fistula is straight, then seek it; and if the fistula is crooked, then seek it with a subtle probe of lead, for lead bends easily around curvatures; and if the fistula has many holes and you cannot seek it well with probes, then irrigate it through one of the holes, for moisture quickly travels from one hole to another, and cleans it; then seek its opening as much as you can, so that you know if there is bone or nerve in it, and if it is deep, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and where he feels it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or from a nerve, or from an artery or vein, or in any of the places I mentioned to you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the abscess and the corrupted flesh that is inside; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deeply embedded straightly, then you must cut deeply, as much as you can, then put wet bandages medicated with medicine in it, and push them up to the opening of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the remaining superfluidities; and then put on ointments that draw healthy flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If vein or nerve does not trouble you in the main members, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, let the king (cauterize) until all corruption is removed, then cure the injured flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and returns bent as before, know that you have not yet reached the bottom: uncover and seek until you reach the bottom, and remove all corruption, then restore the place; and if it is healed in this way, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If not, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot reach it; and there is no other means but to leave it to nature; and if there is a small bone that is corrupt, and you can pull it with tongs, then pull it out with a suitable instrument for this, and if there are many bones, pull them all out, do not leave even one; and if moisture acts against you, and there is no error or fear, cut and remove the moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place a putrefying substance on the wound and leave it until the flesh around the bones begins to rot, and then the bones will come apart more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh bone, then reduce the corruption only until all the blackness is gone, then restore the wound; and if a large part of it has corrupted and reached the marrow of the bone, then it must be covered and protected until the corruption is healed, and then cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 A young man of around thirty years old had pain in his leg due to an internal cause, such that matter came into the leg and caused a large abscess, and there was no obvious reason to open it; but the physicians, in their foolishness, operated on the abscess too much until it opened, and a great deal of matter drained out, and it became a fistula, and a lot of pus came out that all smelled foul and moist from the body; and many physicians applied treatment to it for two years, and there was no skilled person in the art of medicine among them, until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines they were using to treat him, and the matter that was draining out through the holes, which was very corpulent; and the young man's skin became red, and he had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I set up a tent in one of these openings, and then searched all the openings, and found that one came towards the other from all sides of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 I then hurried and cut into one of the openings until I exposed a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the rot reached as far as the inner bone; I thought that what appeared to me of the rotten bone was all of the corruption, and believed there was no other corruption except for what I removed; and I began to heal the wound with soaking medicines for a long time, but it would not heal; and then I began again, and exposed the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I ignored it, and then removed it, and took care to heal the place; but I was unable to do so, for I cut around one palm's width of the bone, and pulled out all of its flesh, then healed it with medicines; and it quickly healed and became solid, and there was no need to begin the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 For through the evacuation (of blood) he often groaned, but he was completely healed, and there grew in place of the bone a hard flesh, and it was of good disposition and caused no harm or contrary effect at all, neither going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this way: take a bandage and strain it at the end of the visible bone, and command someone to hold it up; and put another larger linen bandage on top of the skin that is above the bone, and stretch the head so as to pull the rotten flesh underneath, and uncover the flesh above the place where you want to operate, so that the knife does not cut the healthy flesh; and put a hot iron or a piece of wood beneath the bone to cover the rotten flesh; and it is necessary to operate until one can see and feel that the corruption has been removed, and to operate again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 And if the bone is corrupt and not visible, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, reveal all the flesh; then put a piece of ember underneath, and then apply silk from one side to the other side of the corruption, and let the silk be one finger's breadth away from the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, cut the corrupt joint and cover the bone or what it contains on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other remedy but to cut; and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand, or in the ankle of the foot, this is a very strong thing, but nonetheless you must examine the corruption, how it appears to you; and clean it in all the ways that you can, except let the vein or nerve not hinder you; and know that there are many incisors and silks for cutting these bones, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of the skin, and their thickness and thinness, and their size; and therefore it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each type of work; and know that the task will show you the instrument that you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the symptoms of diseases; so consider the instrument that you need according to what is required.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The shoulders rot or decay, either inside or outside; and when you have treated this corruption with the cure of medicines, and it does not improve, then you must cover that member up to the place where the corruption comes, so that the patient escapes from death, or from the greater harm, which is the defect of the member; and the sign is that the member becomes black, so that it seems as if it has been burned by fire, and after the blackness, the corruption spreads from member to member, taking hold throughout the body; so you must hasten to cover it, and if it is due to the sting of any venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and the like, if the corruption is in the joint of the finger, you should cover it, and do not give it space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 And if it (the corruption) reaches as far as the hand, cut at the joint, so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, cut with a knife; and if it goes beyond the knife, it is death, and no appeasement or medicine will help except for the amount of its power; and do the same when the corruption comes to the foot: if it reaches the first joint, cut after the other joint; and if it reaches the foot, cut the whole foot; and if it rises in the leg, cut at the joint of the knee; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to let the patient die; and the way of cutting or sewing the member is that you tie it above and below, and extend one minister one of the ties downward, and another minister the other tie upward, and you separate the flesh which is between the two ties by a span wide, so that the bone is exposed; then cut or sew, and put a linen rag on each side, so that the thread does not touch the healthy place, and come to the patient with no other harm or abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 And if bleeding occurs while you are working, then cauterize the area quickly, or apply restrictive powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the wounded limb with a suitable bandage and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in our town: he had a discoloration that looked like a burn from fire, and this corrosion first appeared on his foot toe, until it spread to the entire foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he quickly covered his foot, and it was healed; and long after, the corrosion returned to his hand toe, and he came to me, and I applied reactive substances after the cleansing of the body, but the corrosion could not be stopped; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I did not, because I had hope of pushing out the material; and I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, because his vitality was weak; and he despaired completely, and returned to his land, and covered his hand, and it was healed; and I have only told this story so that one might do likewise, if necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 Sometimes a abscess occurs in a fatty place, and remains so long that it forms a large collection of pus; and then it bursts and pierces, and the pus comes out, and the hole remains visible, like a hollow vessel; and the skin that is on top is as thin as delicate cloth, and does not reach to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a disease is called "tumor", and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so elongated that it reaches to the bone in depth, it is called "fistula"; and the skin is such that you cut all the skin around, and likewise when it is thin, like delicate cloth; and it does not heal easily due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 And if you think that the skin has hardened, and corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, cure it with an enema as follows: see if the breasts are large, and the swelling that is in it has a foul smell, then enema the patient with Egyptian medicine prepared as follows: take alum, oil, and pitch, equal amounts, and place in a vessel over fire, until the medicine becomes red and as thick as honey; and then take as much of this as needed, and mix it with water and honey, and give the enema to the breast, and constrict the anus; and leave the medicine inside for 2 hours, then extract it by straining; do this many times, until the breasts are cleansed, and the pus is gone; and sometimes enema with ashes' water, when this medicine is not present, and this is done by taking vine ash, and pouring water over it, then filter it, and give the enema, until you know that the breasts are well cleaned; and if the patient cannot bear the Egyptian medicine or the ashes' water, then give an enema of water and honey with a little pitch; or give an enema of honey and wine mixed, where the honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine makes the skin harden; and when you have done this, and you think that the breasts are well cleaned, then give an enema of that which produces flesh in it, and this is done by taking diascordium ointment, and mix it with rose oil and wine; or give an enema of some medicines and remedies, whose properties I have mentioned in the treatment of remedies; and if the nipple of the breast is small, and the nozzle of the enema cannot enter, then widen it a little with iron, and insert a piece of the Egyptian or basilicon ointment, until it is widened; and if the wound is too large, then sew it up and leave it in a place where the enema can enter; and if the nipple that emits pus is above, then aim lower where the pus comes out.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 For when the bowel is deeply trapped, it does not allow for evacuation; and if you are unable to cover the wound beneath as you would like, then make sure that the bowel runs to its lowest point, for when the bowel is deeply trapped, it does not allow for evacuation and if you are unable to cover the wound beneath as you would like, then ensure that: the bowel runs easily downwards, and let nothing of the bowel remain; and take consolidative medicines to place on the wound, and extend a linen cloth over it covering the entire wound; then bind tightly at the appropriate place around the wound, making the hole in the wound a little larger than the first time, then apply a gentle ointment on another cloth according to the size of the wound, and place it on the wound to lighten the bowel, but do not remove the large cloth that is outside until after many days, once; and the one who is over the wound, frequently remove it to remove the contents of the bowel, and know whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digested, or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been spread in this way and you see nature rising on the wound, then know that the breast is already healing and approach the bandages; and then unwrap it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unwrap the wound, change to another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast remains swollen and sagging after many days, know that the breast is not healing.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle venoms linger for a long time, do not lose hope for the recovery, because health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 For there are men in whom the healing of flesh in their wounds is slow, and those who do the opposite; and if pus from an indigestible abscess comes from the breast after many days, know that the breast is not healed; and if the breast is slow to heal and is distant, apply drying medicines in substance and dry in virtue, such as diaphoretic ointment, for there is a great deal of vitriol in it, and this is the last medicine; take diaphoretic ointment, and mix it with rose oil, and moisten it with old wine equal in substance; then cook it and use it; and this same is better cooked and swollen when diaphoretic ointment is not present, or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind them, and powder them on the honey when it is over the fire; and then glue a linen cloth to it, and apply it to the breast, and sometimes administer longwort and celestial lily roots, which are also like vetch flour and centaury; and use simple or compound ones: grind them and make powder, and put it on the honey that I mentioned, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged and not cured by this treatment, know that corruption has reached deep within, and pressure is exerted on the bone, or on the hard members, or on the sinews; then heal with a fistula cure, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 Panarix is a abscess that arises under the nail of the hand, or of the foot, or perhaps in other fingers; and when it has matured, and one does not pay attention, it becomes a bad abscess, and runs and spreads so that it corrodes the root of the nail, and perhaps corrodes it all; and the corruption reaches the bone, so that there is painful, smelly damage, and the finger wound is wide, and the color is black.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you cure it as we have said in the division, and the treatment is of no avail, then you should cut away with a knife all the excess flesh that remains from the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is clean; and if the nail presses against the flesh and begins to prick, and puncture it, then you must place a file under the nail to keep it from pressing against the flesh, and lift it up, and carefully and lightly remove the punctured flesh; then cure it with heating ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 And if the corruption is in the bone, then cut it out and remove it, for as long as corrupt bone remains, it cannot be healed; and if you see that the wound is becoming corrupt, then cut it in two at the narrowest point as mentioned earlier, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is punctured and swollen, and hurts greatly, then you must first clean the wound; then cut the nail of the spatula in a diagonal line, taking care not to cut into the flesh that is beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, apply something soothing.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the swelling in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The two types of dislocations that can occur in the hands of some men by chance are: entirely fleshy, and sometimes there are bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and some are born at the root of the joint, or the birth is in one of the knuckles of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 He who is born with a hump in the back does not move, and he who is born at the joint of the back, perhaps moves; the size of the one who is fleshy is small, in such a manner: cut him at his root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	One who is born in the root of the joint is difficult to cure: so hold (your) hope (in God).
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In the one who is born with a hump on the small of the back, you should first cut the flesh roundly until you reach the bone, then cut the bone to a thickness suitable for it, and then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The unions that come to the fingers can happen through birth, or by the healing of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 It is necessary to cut this fusion so that the parts may return to their natural forms; then place between two tents or damp cloths soaked in rose oil, so that they do not fuse again; or you can place between two thin pieces of wood until the place has healed as it should.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to either of these with the palm, then cut that suture as it should be done.
des vils	 of unclean things/filth
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 Veins are large, swollen vessels full of melancholic superfluities, which come to many members of the body; and this happens more often in the legs of those who walk, work, and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer purging of bile to them at times and then purify them with basilicum.[A note on the translation: "Basilicum" is a plant that was used in medieval medicine as a diuretic and to treat skin conditions. The modern equivalent is not clear, but it may refer to basil or tansy.]
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The treatment with iron is of two kinds: one is to cut (the vein) and let out the black blood; and the other kind is that you raise the vein and draw it all out.
