Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 The cutting (procedure) is as follows: first make the leg very warm with hot water, until the thick blood becomes thin, then strain the leg of the patient from above the thigh down to below the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or two or three places, with a wide incision, then raise and let out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the strength of the patient can bear; and then bind it up and tell him to eat foods that provoke black bile; and resume evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and this is harmful to the patient.[Note: this passage describes a type of bloodletting procedure using iron instruments]
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The elevation of it is done in this manner: raise the leg of the patient, if there is a lot of hair, then place them in the bath, and soak the leg in hot water until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it by the fire, and then apply a hot iron to the long vein above the head of the knee, or below at the ankle; then lift the skin with a lancet, and cut the vein from both sides, until it appears when touched; and it looks red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord; then push the stylet under it, until it is raised above the skin, and then gently pull it with the lancet, then apply it in another place three finger-breadths away; then cut the skin above the vein until it appears, then lift it with a thread, as you did before, and pull it with a lancet, as you did first; then cut another incision, or several if necessary, then lift it, and pull it to the toe of the foot, then draw it and lift it up to the second incision; then pull it out incision by incision, until it comes out entirely, then bandage it; and if you cannot pull it out and lift it, insert a needle with strong doubled thread, and bind and pull it, and insert it underneath a stylet, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it comes out; and be careful not to cut it, for if it cuts, it cannot be pulled out or lifted, and this will harm the patient; and when you have pulled it all out, place wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound; and cure it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And if the eye socket is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you should split it crookedly, but do not cut it completely; and pull it open as we have previously mentioned.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 The shape of the iron used to cut into the eye socket is curved and does not cut completely, so as not to cut the vein. It should be of thick curvature, for if it were fine, it would cut the vein. Instead, it should be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	 of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein runs in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in land that has no moisture. And by chance it may appear elsewhere than the legs, which happens due to decay beneath the skin, just as a snake or worm may appear within the body between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there comes a very large inflammation in the leg, then the location changes and the vein begins to come out, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 When the incision is made, you should wrap a piece of linen around it that is 3.5 to 4 fingers wide, and tie it in place, leaving the linen hanging from the leg. And each time it protrudes too much, wrap it again with the linen and tie it; and if it is too long, cut off a portion but leave the remainder wrapped, do not cut it at its root until it has fully come out, for if you do, it will return to the flesh and cause abscess, decay or infection. Therefore, it is necessary that it be treated little by little, without leaving any remnants in the body. And sometimes this vein, when treated, measures 5 or 10 palm-widths long. A man came to me once whose measured 10 palm-widths long. When you cut it, insert a finger or probe and pierce it down to its base so that everything comes out. Empty the contents inside and apply healing medicines for several days, then cure it as you would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 And sometimes at this vein, many runners, and even when it appears in the joint of the foot or in the foot, and there comes a lot of bleeding, and then it jumps runners; cure it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This disease is called "maladie de buef" (ox disease) in our land, because it often occurs in oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and moves throughout the body up and down, and one can feel it moving from member to member, as it causes the skin to burst and jump out; and it comes from the putrefaction of certain humors, such as worms, snakes, lampreys, and ascariasis in the belly; and there is concern about its harmfulness, because when it moves through the body and rises to the head, and it reaches the eye, it may accidentally enter and destroy the eye; and this happens frequently.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 When you see it being cured and pulled, it cannot be done without pain; therefore, you should tie the area above and below with a strong, tight ligature. Then, cut and pull it out, and if the wound runs deep into the flesh and you can't find it, cauterize it with fire until it dies. The most significant harm it can cause is causing the eye to run, as we have said. If you see it coming towards the head near the eye, firmly press down on the eyebrow beneath it, then cut and pull it out. The patient should use purifying medicines for the body to remove harmful humors and be wary of spoiled food that may cause decay.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 of the pain coming from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that appears in certain limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and soon after, I saw it move up to the shoulder, more quickly than any other thing, like quicksilver when it runs from place to place; the pain left that place and settled in the shoulder, and then soon after, it spread throughout her body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it turned around her body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how it moved in this way from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease take hold in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 Nevertheless, I have often seen that they eagerly wanted to move the pain from one place to another, but I did not want it, as I saw in the woman; and I thought it was because women have a dry body, and visible veins, and therefore this constrained windiness is apparent; and it does not appear according to this reason in those who are plump, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And when you see to cure this illness, and the patient feels this pain, if they show it to you as we have said, then bind it above and below quickly, and then press on it until the constrained windiness comes out; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your own eyes, then have it treated by those who heal windiness, such as foul-smelling pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	 of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their shapes and the parts of the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 The varieties of arrows are such that there are some with large points, and small, and barbed, and headed; and some have two wings, and some have tongues, and some are fletched; and an arrow that falls in a member does so in two ways: either it strikes the principal member, such as the head, heart, liver, lung, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 When it falls in any place of these members and the signs of death, which I will tell you later, appear; then one must be cautious in extracting this arrow, for death often follows in many dispositions; and when these bad signs do not appear at all, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then draw it and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And the sign of the brain when an arrow falls and pierces the bone, and the dura mater that is above the brain moves, is when there is a scotoma (partial vision loss) and is numb and vertigo and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps there is discharge from the nose or ears; and perhaps he loses speech and voice; and there is a discharge of white moisture from the wound resembling pus, and also a foamy discharge from flesh; and if these signs appear, then you should abandon the cure, and pull out the arrow if it is not in deep.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 The signs of an arrow wound when it strikes the heart are: it is close to the left breast, and there is a feeling as if it is stuck in something hard, not hollow; and perhaps the arrow moves like a bird's wing, and produces black blood, and comes chills and cold sweats, and fainting: know without doubt that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the signs of an arrow that has damaged the spinal cord are: if there is no foam coming out of the wound, and the throat swells up, and the patient changes color and sighs heavily, seeking cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrows fall on the coverings of the chest, it is near the small ribs; and it causes great suffering and great pain and sighing; and all the limbs of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrows fall on the stomach, perhaps some matter of undigested food will spill from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrows fall on the belly, and there is an exit of feces through a perforated intestine, there is no hope for a cure or in extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrows fall in the bladder, and urine spills out and comes forth, and the patient feels strong pain: know that the wound is deadly.[OT] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the arms and neck and throat and shoulders and hip joint and the spines of the back and the ribcage and the legs, and similar limbs, are healthy according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When an arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you can do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 It happened to a man that an arrow struck him in the temple at the base of the nose: I extracted it and pulled it out from the other side beneath the ear's fat, and it was healed without trouble.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 And extracted an arrow that struck him in the fat of the eye beneath the eyelid, and the arrow was barbed, and it could not be reached except by the tip, and the arrow was large from a Turkish bow, all iron light without ears; the man was healed, and no ill befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 And I pulled an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow with barbs: I sawed off the barbs, and carefully pulled it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 And I pulled an arrow from a man, who had it fall in his belly, and I thought he would die; and after thirty days had passed, his condition had not changed: I cut into the arrow, and extracted it carefully, and there were no complications.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And if you see a man who has an arrow stuck in his back, and the wound has healed over; and the arrow remains inside him, without affecting his natural condition or causing harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	 And see another person, to whom an arrow struck in the face, and the wound was healed; and remained without suffering great pain; and many similar ones.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 And I pulled an arrow from a man of the prince's, which had fallen into his nose, and it was slanted towards the right side; and the arrowhead was completely buried I was called to the care after it had been there for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 I searched it with a thin probe and felt nothing; and he felt pricking and pain under his right ear.[`pulling an arrow from a man of the prince's, which had fallen into his nose, and it was slanted towards the right side; and the arrowhead was completely buried I was called to the care after it had been there for three days. And I found the wound very narrow. I searched it with a thin probe and felt nothing; and he felt pricking and pain under his right ear.`]
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 I thought it was from the tip of the arrow I applied a plaster of attratifet and digestive to the area because it did not swell; and the place of the arrow became apparent.[`pulling an arrow from a man of the prince's, which had fallen into his nose, and it was slanted towards the right side; and the arrowhead was completely buried I was called to the care after it had been there for three days. And I found the wound very narrow. I searched it with a thin probe and felt nothing; and he felt pricking and pain under his right ear. I thought it was from the tip of the arrow I applied a plaster of attratifet and digestive to the area because it did not swell; and the place of the arrow became apparent.`]
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	 I applied the plaster for many days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained in this state for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his nose; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 I placed corrosive medicine on the wound for many days, until it was open, and I probed it and felt the tip of the arrowhead that protruded; then I applied the medicine to the opening of the wound, so that the head of the arrow became visible; and the wound healed in more than four months, and then closed up so much that I inserted tongs, and they could not come out; so I did not stop trying and using various methods of instruments, until one day I took it out with well-made tongs, according to its shape which will come at the end of this chapter, and I pulled it out and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 And the surgeons judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I then restored it, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 I have told you the nature of the extraction of certain arrows, so that you put your efforts towards what I do not mention, for books cannot comprehend everything; but wise masters compare well even a small thing, and with regard to what is present and lacking, they find new methods and nine tools for dealing with strange occurrences in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 I say that arrows do not exit from the members where they are embedded except in two ways: either by the way they entered, or from another part; and the one that exits at the same place it entered is an arrow entering fleshy parts, and exits sometimes.[ translation notes](In this context, "fleshy parts" refers to parts of the body with a lot of muscle or soft tissue.)
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And if it does not jump now, let it be until the flesh is rotted around it, and the abscess is eased; and similarly, if it is embedded in the bone, and it cannot come out, let it be like that for several days, and move it every day; and then it will jump, and if it does not jump, carefully cut around until the whole area is enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 And if the arrow is embedded in the skull and reaches one of the brain's ventricles, and any of the aforementioned symptoms are present in the patient: do not pull it out, but leave it until it is even after several days, for if the arrow reaches the brain, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrow is not stuck only in the bone, and does not reach the marrow, and the patient remains for several days without any bad accident, then extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out, apply a cauterization around it, as I have told you; then cure the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And if the arrow is lodged in the body so that it cannot be seen, search for it along the whole wound; and if you feel it, then extract it with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein in the way, then enlarge the wound until it is large enough; and extract the arrow if you can, and if there are pieces of flesh sticking to it on both sides, remove as much of the flesh as you can, and then break or bend the pieces sticking out from the arrowhead so that you can extract it; and take care not to break the arrow so that you do not leave any part of it in the wound.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, let it be until the place is swollen, then pull it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And if the flow of blood is against you, moderate what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and be cautious of the incision of the nerve and vein, and use a device on how you can safely pull out the arrow, whether soon or late, firmly or gently; and place the patient in the same condition he was in when the arrow fell on him, for this is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot, then place him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	 The arrow that comes from another direction, where something is visible of it, or the skin is swollen in that spot if it can be seen or felt evidently: then cut there, as much as the pliers can reach, and then pull it out; if it jumps out on its own now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is lodged in the bone, then turn your hand around repeatedly until it enters into the bone and widens the bone, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 And if it cannot come out, leave it in, and then resume the extraction until it comes out; and if the arrowhead is stuck there, push the whole shaft in; and if it has fallen out, and you wish to administer a buttress, use an instrument chevet, so that the point of the arrow enters the instrument's hollow; and then push out, and if the arrowhead is stuck, use an instrument with the point entering first, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 And if the arrow is embedded, you must cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And if the arrow falls in the leg or belly or bladder or side and it is close by, and you can cut above it, then do so; and be careful not to cut the vein or nerve, then extract it, then stitch the wound if necessary; and treat it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers used to treat arrows resembles a bird's beak, and see the illustration here:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The shape of the butt of the leg is similar to the feather of a bird, to place at the tip of an arrow, such as this is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers for attaching and removing is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins in the body.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 There are 31 veins that one uses to bleed, of which there are 16 at the head, namely: two veins that are behind the ears, called the "herbech"; and two arteries that are in the temples; and two veins that are in the eyelids of the two eyes, called "aspires"; and the vein that is between the eyebrows; and the vein that is at the tip of the nose; and the two tendons that are in the neck; and the two veins that are on the upper lips of the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich"; and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The veins that are commonly lanced are five in number: one is the cephalic, located on the left side, which common people call "head vein"; the middle one is called "faste", and it is made up of the cephalic and basilic veins, and common people call it "heart vein"; and the basilic is on the right side, and common people call it "belly vein", and it is above the fascia, and it is the one that is lanced, which is clearly visible on the bump.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 And the "salvatelle" is the vein that is between the ring finger and little finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is under the cavity of the bump on the left side, and the second saphena is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called "nesse", which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins under those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The bleeding of veins that are located behind the ears helps against old catarrh and headaches; and the quality of the bloodletting, as I tell you, is to raise the patient's head and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a string, until two veins appear behind the ears in two hanging places: then seek them with your finger, and where you feel the pulse beneath your finger, stop; then take the lancet, and insert it below the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand along the entire length of the vein, and cut the skin and the vein well two fingers' breadth across, and let the blood flow until you see; then bind and tighten, until it is healed; and I have already mentioned incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is worthwhile for old and solid headache, and customary ophthalmia, and for the body of watery tears to the eyes; and the qualities of the bleeding are as follows: and it is that the patient pulls his neck, so that the two veins appear openly; and feel the pulse beneath your finger, and then bind above with a bandage; then lift the kidney on the vein up to your index finger, and insert the lancet underneath, and lift the vein up, and the cup, as you have done in the two other veins, and make the blood flow according to your necessity; then undo the patient, and put your hand on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on; and then bind it tightly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have previously spoken of their binding and extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 The bleeding of the frontal vein is worth as much as the bleeding of the temporal vein for ancient facial diseases, and for migraines, and for redness (inflammation); and its quality is such that the patient strains their neck by twisting it until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "trepan", whose form is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 And place the tip on the vein, and strike it with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see; then loosen the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is healed and sometimes the work is done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not appropriate for the flame to be too sharp and oblique, for the bone is close, and there is a risk that the flame will break if it is fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 The bleeding of the two veins that are in the inner corners (of the eyes) helps the eyes, and for lice, and for inflammation, and for stye in the eye, and for diseases of the face; and the quality of their bleeding is such that the patient strains their neck by twisting it with some ligature, as before; then bleed, and let the incision be long and wide a little, because there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is too fine, it may break; then apply scarification of blood, as much as you need, and then bind it with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 The sap of the vein in the nose is worthwhile for headache, and for sudden madness, and for diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, and similarly when it is old; and the quality of the sap is such that the patient constricts his neck, then constricts his nose with your left hand, and take a thin, long flame, and stick it between the upper lip in the space that is between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open widely, and the blood will begin to flow; and do not go too deep, and make the blood flow according to your need, then bind it up for one night, for it is quickly restored; and this is the method of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 The dripping of the two waterskins aids in the constriction of the sinew, and the beginning of paralysis, and many diseases, and impetigo, and corrosion, and herpes, and ulcers; and the quality of the dripping is such that the patient pulls their neck from under one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing over the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a seat, then carefully open the vein widely, then draw blood moderately, or as much as needed; then do the same thing in the other vein, then untie the bandage, and moderately tighten both veins so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, so that the wound dries.
de la sainie des leivres	 of the flow of blood/wound drainage from the books (not sure what "books" refers to in this context)
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood-letting from veins in the upper lip aids in the formation of an abscess in the mouth, and in the corruption of gums, cracks in the lips, and around the nose.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 And the qualities of the flow (of blood/wound drainage) are as follows: make the patient sit in front of you and constrict their neck as I have said; then turn the lip and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left, and they can be recognized by the fact that they are black, and also because there are small black veins around them: therefore stop the flow from both of them, and if you do not recognize them and are in doubt, then stop the largest one on each side; and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, as it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 of sweat under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 The sweating from veins that are under the tongue helps after the sweating of the head, and this is at the narrowing of the throat, and for illnesses of the eye, and for illnesses of the mouth; and the quality of sweating is such that the patient lies down in your hands before the sun, and raises the tongue, and looks beneath on either side a black vein: then heal one and the other, but do not go too deep, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 The veins of the arm that are commonly bled are bled in two ways: either by pricking with a large flat needle or a thin, sharp needle like a scalpel, and it is called "anesil"; and they are large and thin according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the mercurial flame is very famous, and is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 And it is necessary, for opening veins full of thick blood that is visible, and that contain thick and clottered blood; and this is the form of the olive-colored flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more finely pointed, and is used to heal delicate veins that contain subtle yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 The bleeding of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that are located below the throat, neck, chest, and stomach; and it is necessary for the surgeon to bleed carefully and be cautious of the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And if the artery is cut and blood flows out, it must be stopped as I have said; and the flame should not be pricking but cutting like a needle.[](note: The translation of 'anesil' as a needle is an educated guess based on context, as the exact word for needle in Old French is uncertain.)
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the vein does not open manifestly, you should constrict it, and apply another one; or seek a ramification of it, or heal the wound in its place on the arm: it opens manifestly; and cover it with a dry sponge, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	 And if you wish to recognize the location of the bleeding, you should proceed as follows: grasp the arm and press on it until you feel the pulse; then mark the spot with ink, and bind the arm, and cover the vein with a dry sponge; and be careful not to strike the artery when you see the swelling, for this is from the artery - avoid it therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you see it protrude upwards like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is from an artery: hasten then, and place your hand on it for a long time, then remove your hand if the bleeding stops, which often happens; bind the arm, and leave it so, and let the patient not move it; and be afraid, and let the patient not move until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped and it overpowers you, and the medicine is not present, cut the artery if it is visible, for its source retreats; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 Take a piece of fennel bark, and split it, and take one half of it and bind it on well until the next day; if the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, cure it, as we have said, with powders that stop blood; and stopping the bleeding is not difficult in many dispositions for the small size of the wound, and the strength of the arm's binding.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 The incision of the vein in the middle helps so that it draws blood from the top of the head and from the body beneath, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it is appropriate for the surgeon to be cautious about the nerve that is underneath, and if it pricks too deep, and he finds the nerve, and it swells and the wound becomes infected, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve often appears, and if it does not appear in some men due to its subtlety, then you must cure it with a blunt instrument; and avoid the nerve as much as you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then make an incision through its length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 The incision of the cephalic vein helps in drawing blood from the head and benefits the eyes; and it is appropriate to incise by pricking with the olive-colored flame or the myrtle-colored flame, because it is the safest of all veins, for there are no nerve or artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 Nevertheless, one should try to find the easiest approach, and not worry if it fails the first time, and try again; and perhaps the area swells for some men when it fails the first time, but they should not worry.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the discharge corresponds to your expectation.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 The first thing you should know about bloodletting is that it is not performed unless it is to maintain health and avoid future illnesses; and the bloodletting should be done in one of the three veins which are: cephalic, basilic, or saphenous; and it should be done at the beginning of spring, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear; and it should be done on the first or third day, after two or three hours into the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 The dripping of medicine for illnesses has no determined time, but rather when needed by day or night, at all hours and in every moment; and one should not bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor women carrying a fetus until the third month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Old French Text: Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 And when one wishes to be bled, in whatever manner, they must first cleanse the intestines with a light enema if they have retained much feces, so that the veins do not draw out impurities from the intestines that can harm the principal members; nor should one bleed those who are overly full of food, or intoxicated, until they are sober, nor those who are edematous; and if one wishes to be bled after a colic attack, vomiting, stomach upset, frequent urination from women, physical exertion, staying up late, fasting, or any other cause that weakens the body; then refine the humors if the blood is thick with foods, drinks, and medicines if you have the means; then enter the bath, if nothing prohibits it, to further refine the blood, and bleed from the vein on the side of the weaker arm, as we have said; and be cautious that day with labor, strain, lust, and similar things; and be happy and joyful, and let the one performing the bleeding raise their sleeve higher than the arm of the person being bled, and they should rub the limb two or three times, then loosen the ligature in the middle, for when it is too tight or loose, the blood cannot flow; and then rub the area around the vein with your hands until the veins swell and can be felt; then moisten the bandage with a little oil, then place your left hand on the vein below where you wish to bleed, so that the vein does not move and is struck by the lancet.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 For there are veins that run like strings in the leg, and some of them are filled with airiness, so that when one applies fire, they contract and cannot be opened; it is the same for such; and if one incises the vein, the wound is too narrow, therefore the surgeon must be cautious in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it's good; if not, try again a little below or above that spot quickly, unless the area is swollen.[ST] Si ceu ne vaut, si est visibles que li voinne va mal, et si faut chaufer le flaime e les mains du sainier.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 And if the wound is swollen and the patient is frightened, let it be for a day or two and do not bind the arm: perhaps abscesses will form; do not enter the bath, then resume bleeding if it pleases; and if the opening is small, carefully cut the skin and if you doubt that not enough blood will flow, place the flame directly into that same hole; and perform the operation quickly, so that the wound remains swollen; for it often happens, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 If you see the place swollen, do not begin the bleeding again, and put a little bit of oil residue on it, for it lightens the body of blood, and the oil residue is beneficial in that location; and thus administer the oil residue in every bleeding that you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and do the same with triacle and bowe, when applied to the place; spreading the blood subtly if it becomes too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 And if a large abscess comes, which often happens, even when it is only bled at that time or the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and put a damp sponge heated a little on the place, and bind it for an hour; and you should do this after the bleeding from the vein, and if some darkness or greenness remains at the place after several days, it does not harm; and if you wish, put something of aloes or myrrh dissolved in chamomile juice on it.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is an abscess and discharge at the base of the belly; place your hand there then, and if you find it soft upon compression of the hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore be cautious not to apply any of the things that we have mentioned, because perhaps it may pierce the artery; but make an application of a dry plaster to harden the place, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.["Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit" can also be translated as "So be careful not to apply any of the things that we have mentioned".]
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each side according to the strength of its virtue, and the color of the blood.[In this context, "virtue" may refer to the healing properties or power associated with a particular part of the body, as understood in medieval medicine. The different sides of the body likely refer to veins on opposite sides of the body, and the quantity, color, and other characteristics of the blood are important for diagnosis and treatment.]

des sainies de ventouse	 ventouse cupping glasses (or "sain" cups)
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cups are made of horns, or of tin, or of glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 And this evacuation, which is to strike without wounding, is of two kinds: either it is entirely with heat, or without heat; and the evacuation that is made by striking and by the extraction of blood is made in fourteen parts of the body, one of which is right at the head; and another is in the middle of the neck; and two others are on the two sides of the neck; and a ventouse below the chin; and the ventouse on the two shoulders; and the ventouse on the haunches; and the ventouses between the two arms; and the ventouses on the two legs; and the ventouses on the two ankles; and this evacuation does not draw blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it weakens one not at all, as one does with venesection; and it should not be administered, neither with nor without heat, in any disease that comes from plethora, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if by necessity of illness it is necessary to bloodlet, or by habit, we administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at any time; for there are some who, when they need to be bloodletted, have a heavy head; and there are some who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes; and there are such ones who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and secrete blood; and there are those who dream, and see through a fog blood and wounds and death and similar things.

The way to apply the cupping glass is as follows: place it empty first, and then attach it quickly with gentle heat, moving it evenly, not stopping until you see the area turn red and swell, and observe the color of the blood that comes out; then pierce (the skin) and replace the cups, taking care of the condition of the body, for there are those who have dry and clear pores: so you should pierce only once, making large but not too deep wounds, and suck gently.

Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 Cupping glasses that are placed without causing harm are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, gout, stomach, abscess, and legs, because these members cannot tolerate being struck. And one does not do this except to draw blood from member to member, as we place on the breasts when the milk is flowing; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place cups on the stomach and on the abscess to reduce swelling; and to remove pain when there is blockage or a stone. Thus, by its attractive virtue, it may perhaps draw out the blockage or move the stone from its place. And similarly, it does this when placed on the liver and spleen when there is retained wind. These cups are administered empty to simply suck, and sometimes they are administered with heat, and sometimes full of warm water, as in cases of pleurisy. And in such a way that one fills the cup with hot water, or water in which herbs suitable for this purpose have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of applying the cup with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And it should be two fingers in width and half a palm in depth, and have on the side near the middle a small hole, as big as to put a needle through, and be made of brass, smooth before so that it does not prick the patient when putting it on the member; and have in the middle a bar of brass or iron, to hold a candle in place, and there should be both large and small [blisters/suction cups], according to the illnesses and age of those who use them; for the blisters/suction cups of children are different than those of the elderly, and of the thin than of the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And one should apply this cup thus to the member: take either oil of wax or linen, and put it inside the cup through the stem that is in the middle of the cup, so that the light is at the bottom of the cup and does not burn the patient; and then place it on the member, with your hand over the opening that we mentioned, so that when you wish, the vapor may exit and the cup can be removed; and reapply the linen as before, and repeat frequently, if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	 In the cup used for the disease of pleurisy, there is no stem or opening, and it is only filled with water when it is full, and placed on the member; this is its form.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 Sweat nodes are not matured unless in members where one can't apply cups due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in bare places of the skin, such as fingers or nose, and other similar ones. And the quality of the node is such that when you find sweat nodes that are in clear, clean wetness without corruption, then take them; and place one cup on them in clear water, until they become familiar (mature), and have nothing in their belly; and then let it be bled and cupped, then rub the member until it becomes red, and place the sweat nodes (cupping glasses) on it; and when they are full and fall, if it is a place where one can apply a cup, then put one on, for it is very valuable.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If not, lift the leg of the bed, and then of earthenware, very well, and then cover it; and if the limb remains swollen for too long after the body of the veins, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and place it on until the swelling subsides; and if the swelling is multiplied, put crushed vitriol, or aloes, and similar things on it, until it subsides; or you put half of peeled beans on the affected area, and leave them until they dry out at the place, and this will stop the bleeding now; and if you need more, take other veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And if the veins will not form, rub the place with fresh blood, or insert a needle until blood comes out, and then apply it, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will dry out; and when you see that they have stopped, sprinkle some crushed aloe and salt, or ash, on them, and they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and deals with the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Know, dear son, that foolish doctors throw away this chapter, as they never saw any of the ancient books, nor did they read letters; and for this reason, the knowledge is estranged in our land, for I never found any good one; and I know nothing, except from the science of ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have extracted the knowledge, and by experience, and by the custom of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what it contains, and summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are prepared, as I did in the two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is appropriate that we mention in the prologue of this book the summary of the teachings and the chapters in which the wise person concentrates their understanding and dwells on the truth, so that those who are tested may know and learn this noble art, and then teach it to others.
