Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or contusion comes to anyone, you should hurry to heal the patient from one side and the other, if nothing prevents you, such as weakness of the body, children, old people; or if the weather is not extremely hot or too cold; and eat cold foods, that is to say, cold meats, and bird and hare meat, and do not drink wine, nor eat fatty meats, and do not fill yourself with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubts about a hot abscess or spreading of matter to the limb; so let the patient return to their usual regimen.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when a broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that promote thick nutrition, such as wheat boiled in water, and bread, meat, poultry, dairy products, eggs, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For proper nourishment promotes movement and speeds up the healing of fractures.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that broken bones of the old and infirm cannot heal or join together well according to their nature due to the weakness of the limbs, nor can those who are too young, such as the bones of small children. But it doesn't matter, reset the broken bone and use large, sturdy bandages to hold the limb together until it heals as it was before; and do not move it at all, and for this reason, they must be nourished with hearty foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a skull fracture is different than a rib fracture or a leg fracture, and I will tell you in this chapter all the types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are some fractures that go obliquely, and others sharp-angled, like the quill of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with just a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 And each type has its own method and proper instrument in the healing process, according to what is appropriate for the situation. And a broken bone is recognized by the limb being twisted, and it is clearly visible and audible when pressed with the hand. But if there is no twisting or sound upon touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no break. However, there may be twisting, or a fracture, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not necessary to move it by hand, but apply the following medications and then bind it gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 And know that fractures that are in a tree, and are the two parts disjoined, they need to be aligned equally, so that abscesses do not come there; and if abscesses do come there, let it sit for a few days, until the abscess is calmed down; then align it evenly as you can easily and neatly, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restoration of one where pieces are missing; then bind it, as will be described later.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 And if in the bone there are broken pieces, stretch it from two sides, whether it is an arm or a leg, or with your hand if it is a small member, or with two ropes, or with one rope and your hand; and place the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, you align all connections in their places as well as you can, and make sure that through your work, no harm or pain comes to the patient; and fit the two ends of the bones together according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels it in the hand if it seems not to be well: so straighten it nicely, and do not strain it too much, nor press as those who make it hot abscess and contraction in the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And when the limb is healed, chastise the patient well so that they do not move it, whether awake or asleep, while turning, or in any other way; and ensure that the limb is secured so that they feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 For when they feel any pain, it is not yet healed and must be put in such a position that they feel no pain; and ensure that it is set straight, so that there is no crookedness when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are as I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	"Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and largeness and form."
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 For there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers and the like: these must be wrapped in soft and fine linen; and those that are large, such as hips and legs: these must be wrapped in a wide and firm bandage, for a wide bandage embraces the entire large limb and constricts it evenly on all sides so that there is no swelling; then wrap light stuffing around it three or four times according to the limb, and tighten your hand slightly on the entire bandage, then go above the break and tighten less, so that the break moves away slightly; and gradually loosen the bandage a little at a time until you have wrapped a large part of the healthy limb, then apply another bandage and wrap around again above the broken limb; then return to the area below the break and tighten moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we said in the first place; then place linen or cloth stuffing between the bandages, so that it is all even, then bind everything with a bandage on top, and then place your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 And if there is swelling or an abscess, apply something warm that reduces the abscess and swelling, and leave it in place for several days; then apply pressure with your fingers, using bandages one half as thick as a reed, or a piece of wood used for making rope, or palm fronds, and arrange them in this manner:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 But it is necessary for the splint that is placed on the fracture to be slightly larger and wider than the others; and also to be of appropriate length for the size or largeness of the limb; then apply pressure with the splints as you did at the first application, then bind a suitable thread over it, as was done at the first application on the fracture; tighter is better, less so; and the thread should be of medium thickness, not too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen done by foolish people who bind their fractures with twisted rope, it is a great error, for the binding cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it is not at all appropriate to have less than two finger-widths of space between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded at the sides by the corners after being tightened in a healthy place, place under them linen or wool padding, so that they do not wound themselves.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a break and the flesh is torn, I will tell you the cure next.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to constrict all broken limbs with bandages on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 For when the member is large, do not apply hot irons until after 5 or 7 days, or more depending on your certainty of an abscess appearing; and here is the method of ancient poultices to restore fractures, dislocations, and twisting: it is that you take flour that sticks to the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg, and apply this concoction, not too clear nor too thick, and use it; and this is the common method of the restorative poultice for many types of fractures, and also for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of making a plaster to heal fractures, dislocations, and twists: take centaury and laudanum and elecampane and asafetida and gum arabic and myrrh, each in the amount of ten drams; aloe and aloewood, each in the amount of five drams; and eight drams of licorice root; and grind them into a powder, and mix it with egg white; if the person's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly heals broken bones, and is beneficial to many.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Another method of poultice for twisting: take marsh mallow and greater celandine, equal parts 10 units; myrrh and aloes, equal parts 9 units; gum arabic 6 units; and grind well, and mix with water or plenty of egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Another way to apply a plaster to joints and separated bones, to alleviate the resulting pain, and for use with a fracture or a break: take new wool, soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, and place it on the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 This plaster does not heal on its own, but it is good for alleviating the inflammation of a hot abscess and for treating pain properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way of making a plaster to heal fractured bones: take dried fig leaves and the leaves of wild peppermint, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another way to apply a plaster for the healing of bone fractures and for reducing the remaining inflammation from an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 Take root of maidenwort, chamomile, violet flowers, and flour of bran, each in equal amounts; grind them together and mix with wine. If the limbs are warm, mix it with moist coriander water or plain water, and apply.[Hint](Note: The translation is provided for reference and does not imply any medical advice or endorsement. Some herbs mentioned in this text may have medicinal properties but they should not be used without consulting a healthcare professional.)
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another manner of emplaster, stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 Take root of mallows, and seeds of linseed, balm, melilot, and selfheal, and flowers of violets and chamomile, all in equal parts; and grind, and infuse with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates states in his book that one should not place anything on the broken member for healing except a wax and oil cerate, and nothing else, and he says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen thinks that one should place dry and somewhat warm things on the broken member for healing, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of plaster that is useful for wound and pain: take houseleek and chopped off human hair or bird feathers, and add vсмоlive (a type of plant) and equal amount of grease, grind them, and make it into a plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then loosen it a little afterwards, and take care if the patient feels no pain, nor if the bones have not moved from their place; do not loosen it for many days. And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry and loosen it, and remove the emplaster immediately; and take a light cloth and sea sponge, and soak in water, and raise the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is calmed; then let the member rest for an hour, then put dry wool on, dampened with water or rose oil, and bind it to a cushion, until you are sure of the hot abscess; and relieve the inflammation of the member, and remove the pain, then gently resume binding and a little emplaster, and do not tighten it as before; and gradually until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess is red, swollen, painful and has opened up completely, and you need emplaster and ligature, then reapply it as you did in the beginning.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 And if no improvement comes to the limb from what we have said, do not unlock it before three days, or four or five or seven; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, according to what one sees, so that the breaker becomes cautious and approaches the adjustment of the flesh upon it; then hold it back more than before, and the swelling of the meat increases, as I said before; and if you see the joint drying out more than necessary, know that no healing can come to it; therefore, anoint it with warm wet water every time you unlock it, and this should be every third day, and slightly loosen the ligature; thus, the swelling of the limb is cut off, and quickly heals what foolish doctors do, who incorrectly restore the limb; that is wrong, and such work is to be feared, and I see no other solution than to leave it alone and work on it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the different types of fractures.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 Many kinds of fractures exist, with various shapes, and different causes; for there are fractures that are made by the striking of a sword, and the neck takes out all the bone down to the syphac which is beneath the bone, as does an axe or stick; and this kind of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword cuts the bone without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a deep bruise, or a stone chip, or falling on a stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture that reaches the membrane beneath the bone, or above it, and this wound is either large or small.[Note: The membrane referred to here as "toile" could be the periosteum, a highly vascular tissue surrounding bones, or another type of membrane.]
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	 And if there is a wound that lodges in the bone as thin as a hair, and the break is small, and for this reason it is called "capillary" fracture; and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or falling, or by some similar thing, and pushes the piece of bone inward, and the place is sunken, like when blacksmiths hammer on cauldrons; then stones enter inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	 And this happens more to those who have moist bones in their head, such as children's heads; and it happens in all these types of fractures where small pieces are separated, like so; and I will speak about it later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all kinds of fractures by the swelling on them, and through inquiry using tentative examination, and by the corrupt flesh that is on top.[Note: The word "corrupt" here likely means "damaged" or "injured"]
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of a fracture is recognized by this: when the bone is exposed and one rubs against it, the fracture appears black.[Note: "Black" here likely refers to discoloration or bruising caused by the fracture]
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be cautious of the patient's condition, and if you see any adverse symptoms, such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, convulsions, fever, eyes turning out and reddening, and other similar symptoms in various dispositions, then it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a terrifying accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person comes to you first, and it is winter, the bone should be removed before the fourteenth day at the latest while it is still fresh.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the summer, hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue underneath the bone does not become corrupt and the accidents that we have mentioned do not occur.[ Italien (1280-90), Jean de Milan, Traité des blessures, Ms. fr. 9567 f. 34v]
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 And if the break in the bone comes as far as the membrane covering the brain, then you should split open the injured part like this: take hold of the patient's injured head and expose the bone in all ways that you can, and gently along the wound's surface, and if bleeding occurs when exposing the bone or an abscess arises, help it as is necessary, and fill the opening with cloths soaked in rose oil; let the wound rest until the abscess subsides and ensure there is no more bleeding, then begin to remove the bone, and this is done in two ways: one way is to make a narrow incision in front, and that is the method:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another incision that is larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is to have several different incisions, some narrow and others wide, and make them sharp, and made of iron; and work lightly, so as not to wound the bone.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and strong, then you must pierce around it, so that you administer incisions with bores, not so deep that they penetrate beyond the bone of the skull, and there should be above the tip a margin or circle, which does not allow the tip to pass beyond the bone; and you will need several, so that each one comes into place along the thickness of the bone, so that you have bores for all bones; and this is the method of three types of bores:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities to pierce around the broken bone are: place one awl on the bone, and turn toward your hands until you know the bone is pierced; then move the awl a little further and do the same all around, then cut the space of the bone between the holes with the scalpel, doing this as delicately and lightly as you can, until you draw out the bone with your hand or with one of the tools you have such as tongs or pliers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the sutures.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 And when you have pierced and treated the bone, you must remove the splinters that remain from the bone on all other similar instruments like a lancet, but it should be more slender and fine than the other lancets; and if there remains any small bones or scales, gently remove them with the instruments; then cure the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is that which Galen describes, which is safer and he highly praises it; here are his words:
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary, firstly, that you uncover a part of the bone, where the break is clearly visible, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place underneath the blade of this lunate-shaped knife, whose form is as follows:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 And do not make a cut only on one side, but rather so that the cut is between two ribs, with the cutting edge towards the bone; then strike gently with a small mallet so that you cut through the entire bone, taking care not to damage the cloth beneath; if it is torn near the bone, remove it carefully, for it can be removed without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not penetrate through to the cloth, but only breaks off pieces from the surface, then you must smooth over that roughness and remove the splinters using a sharp razor, of which you should have various quantities, so that you can adjust according to the work and shape of the fracture.[In summary, this text is a guide for medical practitioners performing surgery using a lunate-shaped knife. The passage instructs the surgeon to uncover a part of the broken bone, place the knife underneath it, make cuts on either side of the bone so that the knife faces the bone, strike gently with a mallet to cut through the bone while taking care not to damage the cloth beneath, and carefully remove any fragments. If there are still rough patches, they should be smoothed over and the splinters removed using a sharp razor. The final sentence notes that different quantities of the razors are needed for various tasks, depending on the specific nature of the injury.]
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If the king before large razors, and afterward with more subtle ones, and do not cease doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other subtle hair cuttings and breaks, it is necessary to arrange according to its growth direction; and this is not an easy thing even for one who has devoted his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 And if the abscess is uncovered, take a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another double cloth, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can, so as not to harm the abscess, then apply another bandage, but do not tighten it too much, just enough to hold the wound; and leave it like this for a day or two, until the abscess has calmed down; then unbind it, and apply medicines such as lily roots, vetches flour, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; make a powder from these things and place it on the wound, and continue to apply healing medicine without causing pain; and make sure that the wound stays clean, that you do not leave any residue or allow pus to accumulate, because when pus accumulates on the cloth on the brain, it will rot and cause great harm to the patient; for when something painful is placed on the abscess, it causes further damage.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take caution then, if any misfortune befalls the patient, as we have mentioned, where there is doubt, there should be suspicion.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if no pus comes out except for what was put there by the medicine, and it has such power, then you should take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and soak one bandage in it, and place it on the abscess; then cure it in various ways until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one of them alone, because they are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous and does not break, but only swells or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should insert your little finger or the tip of a probe into the break, and align it with your index finger, and hold it in place until the nostril regains its natural shape; and do this gently, and make sure that the patient does not feel pain from your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose and your finger cannot reach it, then you must place a small piece of raw meat on the top of the nose to set it.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 And if the break is in two parts, then do the same and hurry to realign it on the first day, if you are able; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has healed, then insert a linen bandage into the tip of the nostril if the break is in one part.[](https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.socialnmobile.dict.frwordfinders)
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or insert one [bandage] on the other side if the fracture is there; and let the bandages be as thick as they fill the nostrils' openings.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And some surgeons say that you should wet the bandages with butter and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 It does not seem right to me, but it is necessary that they are wet with a mixture of egg yolk and powdered flour; then leave the bandage in place until the bone heals and the cartilage hardens.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one inserts feathers of a goose into the nostrils instead of bandages, and wraps it with soft cloth, and this holds the fracture together, and the patient blows through it; do as you please.[`
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if pustules or swellings come on the nose while you are working, put on cerote or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in a blob of diaquilon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if abscesses do not form, apply a poultice to the outside made of lily root powder and incense that has been combined with egg yolk; then place light wicks on top, but do not bind it at all. If the break in the nasal bone is small and it is broken into many pieces, extract them with suitable instruments, then suture the cut and cure any foreign matter or damage using appropriate poultices and ointments. If there is no wound inside the nasal bone, treat it with bandages and place willow splints on it until it heals.[NOTE: I am not a medical professional, please consult one if you need medical advice.]
de la routure de la mandibule	of the dislocation of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is dislocated below, with no wound outside, and there is no break except for a crack inside, it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is on the right side, you should insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if it is on the left side of the jaw, insert your index finger of the right hand, and gently push the break inward, and align it with the other hand from outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jaw is separated into two parts, then you must administer extension to both parts until they are aligned.[FAQ]
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If there is movement of the teeth or a break, then bind them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk, and apply a cerate to the broken jaw. Place a double folded cloth on top, followed by a well-made large star-shaped emblem or a piece of leather of equal length and width to the jaw, and secure it as high as you can. Command the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see the figure changing, unbind it on the third day, and then realign what has shifted; and apply a plaster on top, made of mill powder with plenty of egg or chickpea flour, after removing the wax; and put light linen on top of the plaster, and if the plasters dry out and the patient's condition does not worsen, leave it on until it heals; often it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come, treat them as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, see if any piece of bone has been removed; it is necessary to carefully remove it with the appropriate instruments.[BR] Here's my translation for both sentences:
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it by fire as needed.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, then stitch the wound if it is wide, and apply suitable ointments to it to heal the flesh until it is healed.
de la forcele	The word "de la forcele" does not appear in the provided text. However, based on context clues, it could be a reference to a medical instrument used for removing foreign objects or performing surgical procedures.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps breaks frequently in front, towards the shoulder, and the breakage is in three ways: either it is broken and disjointed into two pieces, which is easier to reset; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedure is when there is no wound in the break: you should have two assistants, one holding the shoulder so that they can feel where the forceps are broken; and the other extending the neck towards the affected area; then bring the break evenly into your hands, aligning it as it should be, with no deformity or protrusion.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	If you need to extend further, place a round cushion made of cloth or wool under the patient's shoulder, and make it as thick as necessary; then lift and stretch the forceps while holding the cushion with your hand, aligning the break evenly as it should be
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the femur outward because it is too deep, then the patient should lie on their side and place a medium-sized pillow under the shoulder, and have the assistant push the shoulder downwards until the bone of the thigh comes out.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then align the fracture with your hands, and if you find any pieces missing, you must saw over it; gently pull out the fragments, and if the bones cannot join together because of any obstruction, use one of the incisors to cut through it, but make sure to place the instrument under the thigh bone to protect the soft tissue.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 and seems like a spoon, but is not curved, and should be as wide as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the task; and have two edges, as you see, and one should be wide, and the other narrow, similar to the opening of the wound that you made when treating the bones; and when you are certain of a hot abscess, burn the wound, and if the opening is small, or if you are unsure about a hot abscess, bandage the wound with cloths and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses appear, wet a linen cloth in rose oil, vinegar, and water, and place it on (the affected area).
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 The straightening of the bone, when there are no wounds and no incisions, is done by placing poultice of mill powder and egg white on the bone, and placing light wicks on top, and placing a rod underneath if necessary; then take a very large bandage one palm wide, place a double cloth on the wicks and poultice; then take a thin stick three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the end of the bandage hangs down; and place the stick over the break, and turn the bandage over the neck, under the healthy shoulder blade, and under the injured shoulder blade; and massage each part, and when you see that the ligature holds the break properly, and it is clear that the stick does not move above the broken bone, then wrap it daily, and when the ligament loosens, tighten it again; and have the patient lie on their back, and place a small pillow under the shoulder blade when they sleep, to raise the shoulder in height; this eases the break by aligning the shoulder, or tying the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless there is an accident, for up to 20 days; then reapply the poultice if necessary, and keep it tightened until healed, which takes at most 28 days, and less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture/dislocation
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 Rarely does the shoulder break or dislocate in such a way that it is noticeable externally; one can only detect it through touch. One should arrange the shoulder according to the pattern of the fracture and reset it following its natural shape, in every possible way. Then, place powder of flour with plenty of egg, and light bandages on top. Next, put a thick cloth over it, then an wide and thin board, slightly larger than the shoulder. If there are any hairs under the board from the shoulder, fill those spaces with linen bandages, so that the board lies evenly. Afterward, bind it firmly with a large bandage, making sure the board does not move from its place, and check it daily. Whenever it swells, rebind it, adjusting the position of the board if necessary, and have the patient lie on his side. The shoulder will be restored in 20 or 25 days. Once this period is complete, unbind it, being certain that it is not a bone that has easily come out of place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone sticks out in front and not under the skin, then saw through it (the bone), and remove it, and do what we have said for the fracture of the forearm to soothe the hot abscess.[Notes: I am assuming "apaiser aposteme chaut" means to treat a hot abscess, as it is mentioned before in the text. The word "oste" here probably means to saw off the protruding bone. ]
de la brisure dou pis	of the break of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it breaks frequently at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	 And when it is broken in the middle, it tilts downward, and the patient feels great pain, and there is a risk of infection, and they may vomit blood, and the hairline appears in the broken bone, which is easily noticeable.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies down with their back on a cushion placed between their shoulders, then presses their shoulders and brings the ribs together using both hands, subtly aligning all parts of the bone as much as possible, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then apply poultices and bandages over the fracture, with a thin layer of salt or other light wood, and wrap it in a cloth, tying it securely to the broken bone so that it does not move; tie the knot around their back, pulling it tight, and check every hour to see if it needs to be loosened, due to infection or itching at the site, or pain or abscess, and act quickly by untying it, removing the poultice, addressing any issues that have arisen through appropriate treatments; then reapply the poultice, tying it securely until healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the broken ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breakers of ribs do not come about except in thick areas after the back, and at the head within, and they do not bend outwards except because they are slippery; and one can feel this well upon examination at the sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And the restoration is to align the break evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 Then apply a poultice and bind it with a splint if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of the ribs is declining inwards, then the patient feels great pain and swelling, just like with pleurisy, because the bone points at the membrane; and there is sharp pain, and soon they vomit a large amount of blood, and this is of grave illness, and the old ones have applied much skill to it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are some who say that one should administer foods that inflate the belly, in order to push the break outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make it so that boils/abscesses come to it, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come, then lance them (let the pus out).
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of you have said that cupping glasses should be placed over the place to strongly draw out (suction), and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cupping glass might attract impurities to the place due to its weak constitution.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of you have said that one should cover the place with a cloth soaked in warm oil and then place bandages between the ribs to evenly hold it in place around the area; and then treat it with the treatment for pleurisy, food, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear from the bone poking through the cloth, and there is fear in the patient, then a cut must be made above the broken rib, and an instrument must be placed underneath to protect the lung; and then the bone must be cut and carefully removed, and then the two edges of the wound must be sewn up if it is large, and it must be treated with poultices until it heals.[Note: This translation is for educational purposes only and not intended to be used as medical advice. Always consult a qualified healthcare provider for any medical conditions or concerns.]
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if boils are about to come, put wet cloths with rose oil on it, and place it on the affected area; and treat the area as needed for the boil, and lie down on the side where it is, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break (fracture) of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never does a break occur in the bones of the neck, and it rarely happens that it bends; and likewise for the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if it will be healed or not, observe if you see their hands becoming softened, swollen, and lifeless, and they cannot move or stretch them, and when you poke them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	 Know that it is mortally afflicted in many ways, and if they can move and feel when they are pressed or pricked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured if treated.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	 And if such a thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it will heal or not, observe if the feet are weak, and if there are symptoms in the hands, and on the back a windy sensation and involuntary evacuation; and when it has been laid on its stomach, involuntary evacuation occurs.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And when it is laid on its back and it wants to turn over, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 Know that it is fatal: do not labor in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these conditions do not arise, then the matter is more manageable.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you should check if there is a hot abscess, and if there is, put roset oil or egg yolk oil on it until it calms down; then apply one of the soothing and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and let them not sleep on the part where they feel pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone becomes dislocated, it is necessary to cover the wound; remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the large wound with a stitch, and treat it with a drawing ointment until it heals; and if the joint near the bone is broken, which is called "the hip joint," place your left hand's pouch on it, and use your right hand to push it into place as much as you can, then apply the plaster and bandage if needed; then bind it, and if there is a dislocated bone, push it back into place, remove it, and treat the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the femur (thigh) bone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the femur is broken, but if it does happen, only a slight swelling occurs at the end; and it becomes long, and inclines to one side, causing pain and lameness to the patient in that area, and swelling in the affected limb.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is as follows: you extend your hand on top, so that you are above the break; and know what the break and its shape is; and if the break is at the head only, then make the break even, so that it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it angles inward, then have the patient lie on their stomach, so that the restoration of that break is made clear to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, then apply the ointment, then place a wooden or waxen star* on top, and hold the break steady so that it does not move; and apply medicine underneath the ribs, until they are aligned.[Yves57] *It is likely that "estele" here refers to some kind of medical device made of wood or wax. The meaning of this term in Old French is uncertain and could also refer to a type of bandage or splint.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if abscesses come after it, do not touch it until the abscesses have calmed down, and apply what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and bind it as is necessary, if there is no adverse accident; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is the one that is between the neck and the shoulder blade, and if it is dislocated, it should be restored in one of two ways: one of which is to take a rod of medium thickness, according to this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two shoulders with two bands and pull them up, and make the patient sit on a seat; then throw his dislocated arm over the rod, until it reaches the waist, and has in the middle a bow of the rod; then hang it from some heavy weight or have the minister stretch it down; then place the surgeon's hands equally around the break, until the break returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that one lays the patient on their back, and ties their hand to their neck, then commands two assistants, such that one holds what is above the break with their hands, and the other holds beneath all the way to one ligament, and each pulls apart in their direction.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 And if you see that the extraction needs to be stronger, tie a ligament below the break, and above the break, and stretch out each of the assistants on their side.[STYLE=ITALIC] I am not entirely sure about this translation, as "estreindre" can mean either "to tie" or "to tighten", and "ministres" could refer to "assistants" or simply "body parts". However, based on the context, I have made an educated guess.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the break is near the shoulder joint, you should place a middle splint under the shoulder socket, and another one below the break, under the break; and also if the break is towards the side, you should lightly place a splint there, without strain, so that the break is even on the surface, and on the side; then align the break as it should be, and bind it, if no abscess comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess does form, then do not hold it in place for more than 7 days and place a moist linen cloth soaked in rose oil on the affected area; wait until the abscess subsides. Then hold it in place, and the manner of holding it in place is that you apply a poultice to the break, then position the arm on the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or chest; and place the cloth, and hold it in place on the shoulder and on the arm so that the arm remains still, unless something prevents you, or if the bone has not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you are unsure whether the bone has moved, then use a splint and place a wider and stronger splint over the break than the others, with a space of one finger between each splint, and let each splint be large enough to extend beyond the break by three fingers on either side; then hold it in place over the splints as I mentioned at the beginning of this chapter, more firmly and less so as you move away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 And if you see the positioning and binding, as we have said, at the time you restore the broken member, and you doubt an abscess will form, then leave it to be bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at the binding every three days, to see if there is itching, swelling, or discoloration at the site, or if the circulation cannot reach the member because the binding is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If the position, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 And if no such accidents occur, do not unbind it until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back and place their hands on their stomach; and put a cushion filled evenly with wool underneath the armpit; and check every hour during the day or night to ensure that the position of the limb does not change or that the ligaments do not become loose; then adjust it by the power of medicine, and give them food as we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the food is initially easily digestible; and when they begin to recover, the food should be more substantial.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 And it is customary for the shoulder and arm to be bound for forty days in total; and then they should be unbound, and a bath and medications consisting of ointments should be administered to straighten the limb.[*I am not entirely sure about the translation of "leu" in this context. It could also mean "to heal".*]
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the ligature is tight and embedded, it should stay in place for a period of 1 day to 2 months.
de la brisure du bras	Here's the translation of the text you provided, in relation to a broken arm:
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscile", one of which is small and is the one that follows the wrist; and the other is large, and it is the one that is beneath, towards the little finger; by chance, only the large foscile breaks, or the small one, and by chance, both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 When the small ribs are broken, the healing process is easy and quick; but when the large ones are broken, the healing takes longer and is more severe than when they are both broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If only the small ribs are broken, they should be lightly stretched and aligned evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 And if it is the large ribs that are broken, they must be stretched more forcefully and placed on a cushion. The patient's shoulders should be raised higher than their hips, and their hands should be positioned with their small fingers lower than their thumbs. The patient should be cross-shaped, lying on top of the cushion with another cushion raised in front of them so that they are comfortable and not in pain. Then, have one assistant extend the patient's arm below, either at the wrist or elbow, while another assistant extends the other arm above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 And then the doctor places it evenly, in its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the break is in pieces, then put each one in its place; and if there is any piece that pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make an incision above it and remove it, as we have said before.
