Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is a wound with the break, I have spoken of this in a separate chapter; so take care of it (referring to the treatment described in the previous chapter).
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 And if during the beginning of the treatment boils occur, apply a compress of rosin oil and white wax, making sure it is not too hard or soft; and gently bind the compress over it until the boils have subsided.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 And then remove the compress, and apply the plaster of flour mill powder with plenty of egg; place splints (esteles), and make the one at the break stronger and a little larger than the others; and know that it should have six splints or arms in multiple arrangements: whether the break is in one of the bones or two; and bind more above the break than anywhere else, and less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the bandages over the break be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the thread used for binding be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And reward the member and the ligament after several days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 And if any bad accidents happen to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then you should moisten the member with warm water until the itching is calmed down; and do not let the member rest tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 And then begin the tightening again, and if the ligament is weakened and the bones disjointed, and similar things, address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you notice that the circulation cannot reach the member because it is too tight, then you must soften it a little and leave it like that for several days, until the circulation has returned, and then bind it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 or when around, then lay hands on its neck, and let its necks be even, and beware of movement and loosening, and sleep on its back; and know that this breakage is healed in 30 or 35 days, and perhaps in 20 days, depending on the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the broken hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that breaks in the back of the hand and at the knuckles often occur, but these are usually not true breaks, rather they result in frequent swelling.

And when the palm of the hand is broken or dislocated, it is necessary that the patient sits cross-legged and faces directly ahead evenly; then they place their hand on a spread out cloth, and the assistant straightens the broken bones and aligns them properly until they are joined; and then an ointment and bandages are applied, unless abscesses appear; then an iron bar is placed according to the size of the injury; and it should be wrapped in a linen cloth.[EnglishGlossary.com](https://www.englishglossary.com) provides English definitions for many Old French words found in this text, including: * au (at, to), croisiet (cross-legged), devant (in front of, before), igalement (evenly), met (put, place), ministres (assistant, servant), os (bones), brisiez (broken), igalz (equal, even), joint (joined), envoloupee (wrapped), drapeil (cloth).* saiches (know), dos (back), poc (there is/are, have), avient (occur), maintes (many), ploieure (swelling), n’i (there not), mais (but, except), quant (when), estendue (spread out), puis (then), sovant (often), apres (afterwards), mal (badly, ill), briseures (breaks).* saiettes (arrows), ovrer (work), incision (incision), sus (on), aposteme (abscess), cure (healing), plaies (wounds), estraction (extraction), piere (stone), semblans (similar, like), doutance (doubt), paor (fear), mors (deaths), en vient (come), plusors (many).* quant (when), desaloiez (dislocated), cause (because), moistor (moisture), remet (set back), leu (place), ne peut demorer (cannot stay in place), revient (returns, dislocates), petit movement (slight movement), ades (repeatedly), avient (happen), ramoinnes (reset).* issue (occurs), jointe (joint), de son leu (from its place), por coi (because of which), ne se puet muevre (cannot move), mal figurez (misaligned), grant dolor (great pain), grant lesion (great injury).
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is on the outside around the stomach of the palm, make a sphere from a cloth and instruct the patient to squeeze it with their broken hand; then bind it with a long cloth, and let the iron bar be as wide as the palm of the hand, and bind it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois. And if the fracture is in any of the fingers, if it's a simple one, place it evenly as it should be; and hold it with the palm, and if necessary, put a small straight stick to raise the fracture and keep it from moving; and if the fracture is in other fingers, such as the index or another one, place it evenly and bind it with the healthy finger that follows; or tie them all together, whichever works best, or put a stick on top, like a splint; and be cautious during the restoration and placement of hot abscess, and treat accordingly, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Here's the translation of "de la cuixe brisie" from Old French to English:
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The thigh bone is often broken, and it's easily noticeable when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration consists of tying one bandage above the fracture, and another below it.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his back, then each assistant stretches out their rope evenly on their side; and that is when the fracture is between the bones.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the break is near the root of the thigh, then let one of the ligatures be towards the wrist, and the other ligature below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 And likewise if it is near the knee, then let the ligature be near the knee, and let there be extension downwards; then place the bones even with your two hands, until it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the poultice, and bind it, if abscesses do not come.[ Louis XVIII of France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_XVIII_of_France)
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside first and then return to your work and care; the bandage is done in such a way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 You should wrap it (the dislocation) with a bandage on the break, doubled in 2 or 3 layers, and let the excess hang; then bend the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg, beside the knee below, and have the ends of the thread come to the top; then bend back on the leg and the thigh the bandage, then put a stake on the break, and put a stake on the bone of the leg; then fill the gap between the leg and the thigh with soft fabric to make the tension even, then begin to tie firmly 3 or 4 knots above the break; and as you go higher above the break, tie it less tightly; then attend to the two ends of the thread that you put between the leg and the thigh, and tie three stakes that are above, then go down to the end of the thread, so that you come next to the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, as long as there is neither abscess nor swelling nor any other similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, loosen it, and realign what is coming out, as we have said many times; and if there are fragments of the bone that prick, they must be gouged out if possible; and if not, the place must be broken open and pulled out; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides. de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin of the knee

de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 Know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called by its right name "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and it breaks just as easily as the arm does, and thus the restoration is similar to that of the arm, and the work is the same. And if the two bones break together, the leg will be twisted in all directions.[NOTE: I am not 100% sure about the translation of "mustelz" and "foscile", as they are not standard anatomical terms in Old French or modern French. However, based on context, I have translated them as two bones in the leg, possibly tibia and fibula.]

Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	 And if the large bone is broken, great pain is felt, and it is clearly visible; and it turns blue. (based on the context, "turns blue" might refer to bruising or discoloration caused by the injury)
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu. de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the leg bones
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is never a break, but sometimes a break occurs in the bones of the foot and toes, and it only results in a fracture in multiple positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If there is a break in the bones of the foot and you see the bones sticking out, place the patient's foot on the ground as if they were going to walk, then place your foot on top of theirs where the bones are protruding, and press down until they return to their place. Then apply a poultice and bandages, and place a small board with two flat chips under the belly of the foot, and bind it to the foot with wraps and other necessary items.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, loosen the binding because you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.[*Note: I translated "desaluez" as dislocated, but it can also mean displaced or out of alignment.*]
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if some of the toes are broken, then set them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; and for the broken toe, place a splint the length of the toe, and make it slightly wider, then place the board that I mentioned under the foot and bind it in place. If there are two or three, or more, broken toes, then place a splint on each one according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the board under the foot; and let it be placed above the belly of the foot so that it touches it well.[*Note: I translated "defuer" as above, but it can also mean over or outside.*]
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, just as we have mentioned; and treat each accident as it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the arm bone (radius/ulna)
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the bone of a woman's nature (vagina) is broken, make her sit spread-eagle, then tilt her hips towards the back and have her held from behind; then fill the vagina with cotton, as thick as one's finger; then stand the woman up, lift her buttocks, and let the cotton come out until it reaches the entrance of the vagina, and the bone will return to its place with the finger; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she is done, replace it, doing this for 7 days; the fracture will be healed. And if you wish, take a bladder of brambles, attach a cane to the opening, insert the entire bladder into the vagina, then blow forcefully into the cane until the bladder is inflated inside; the vagina will return to its place and the fracture will be healed; then fill it with cotton and leave it like that for several days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bones of the wrist in a man or woman are broken, they should be restored as we have said for the bone of the thigh; and such fractures are not hidden from one who applies close attention and skill, and pays heed to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 For the fracture indicates in several ways the correct path of restoration: understand then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose gullet and insert the penis in it; then wrap bandages around it, and leave it for three days or until it heals quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that it be healed now, so that the bleeding which we have mentioned testifies to this.[NOTE: I made an assumption that "sainies" refers to bleeding. If there are any other possible meanings for this word in the context of medieval medical texts, please let me know.]
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, then stain it with vitriol (sulfuric acid), if you have nothing else; then begin to treat the fracture in that same hour or on that day, unless abscesses come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses come, then leave the treatment for nine days until the abscess subsides, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, because you would bring about an evil outcome there.[NOTE: I made an assumption that "li apostemes" refers to abscesses or pus-filled swellings. If there are any other possible meanings for this word in the context of medieval medical texts, please let me know.]
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone appears under the skin, it is necessary to put it back in place gently with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not suitable for you to put it equal with your hands, then use this iron instrument that is 7 or 8 fingers long, and its width corresponds to the size of the wound; and it is necessary for the surgeon to prepare 3 or 4 (fingers), according to what is needed in each bone-breaking treatment; and let it be round and a little thick, so that it does not bend during compression on the limb during your work, and let it be sharp in front, and thick from the middle forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And it is called "palainche," which means that the curved head should be placed on the visible end of the bone; and push it once until it aligns, and make sure they are even with each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot grasp the bone well, then you must cut the end of the bone so that the instrument has enough power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot realign the bone as we have said, then cut it with an appropriate instrument, such as a chisel or knife, to your best ability; and then remove any roughness and small fragments from the bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 Do whatever it takes to put it in its place, then wet a cloth in black stiptic wine, and apply it properly if it is summer; and do not put any plaster or anything with oil on the wound, as it may cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer painkillers when you have reset the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, cutting the bandage to fit around it according to the size of the wound, and take great care that the wound is not constricted by the break; and many times have foolish surgeons caused either death or injury to the patient; and let the constriction be softer and more gentle than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is large or severe, and you suspect that harm may come, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then you should not put it on splints; but wrap hard cloths around it, instead of splints, and bind it.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when you see after one or two days that pus is gathering near the wound, remove what you have put on it, and apply a healing ointment, such as tetrapharmacon ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to unbind the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it has healed and become clean.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be equipped in such a way that the pus drains easily.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if for many days they are exceedingly weak, and it can no longer heal but keeps breaking open, know that there are small pieces of bone, therefore you should stitch the wound with sutures, and remove all the separated pieces that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula comes to the place, or any other form of corruption, then you should treat it according to what is described in its chapter earlier on.[note]: The text seems to refer to a previous chapter on treating fistulas or other forms of wound corruption.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And when the bone is broken and visible on the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder, do not pull it out, for often death results; rather leave it until it rots away; perhaps it will come out by itself after twenty or thirty days; then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	swellings that come upon sutures
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often see after the healing of a fracture, even when it is close to the joint, and it results in an unsightly appearance of the limb; and perhaps the member cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take great care then if it is fresh to us: administer styptic medicines to him, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, so that you take some of these things, or all together, and cook them with astringent wine or with egg yolk or with vinegar; and put it on the wound in lint, and bind it well, and do not loosen it for several days; and then loosen, and begin another, until the knot is removed; or you strain on a piece of wood well made; for the property of wood is that it removes all swellings above the members; and if the knot has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut it off, and let the excess appear; or you have it scraped by a skilled barber, until it is removed, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the weak limb after healing.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone has healed, but the limb remains weak and fine afterwards, it happens for many reasons: one of which is that it was tied too tight, and not tied as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and the nourishment could not reach the member; or due to an excess of moisture; or due to excessive movements, not at the right time; or because there is little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is to make the patient eat, and make the body supple, so that the blood is multiplied in him; and administer baths for him, and give him joy and pleasure; then apply a poultice to the limb, so that the poultice draws great nourishment to it, and often moisten it with warm water, until the nourishment reaches the member; and it regains its natural appearance.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the crooked member after the healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is crooked after restoration, and the broken bone is clearly visible, and the shape of the member is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function; do not believe the foolish ones who say that the member must be broken again, and many foolish surgeons have done this in our land; and these works are blamed, and great harm comes from them, and perhaps death; however, if the nodes and swelling are fresh, they should be soaked in hot water or softening herbs should be cooked, such as leaves of mallow, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make a softening plaster, such as well-made cerate, and take the marshmallow root, and cook it with goose fat or oil of St. John's wort, and make a plaster with it; or take fat figs, and crush them with cow dung, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes nodes are removed by rubbing continuously and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 And move the limb every hour to keep it loose.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the crookedness is old and hardened, like stone, and it needs to be removed with iron, then it should be covered up to the bone with a subtle incision, lightly and skillfully; and cotton and bandages should be used in the care of the wound.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation arises from a joint being out of its place, causing the limb to be misaligned and the patient to feel great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation occurs, it must be corrected immediately.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 For if one waits, the place swells, and perhaps it cannot be moved back into place; therefore, it is not advisable to move it when it is swollen, for often this brings on spasms and other pains; however, when this occurs, let the patient take a laxative, then leave him alone until the abscess has subsided; then soak the limb in warm water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each limb as it comes into place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations of the joints from head to foot.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It is rare for both jaws to be dislocated, and there are two ways in which this dislocation can occur: either they are slightly pulled out of their place and somewhat relaxed; or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the back, causing saliva to flow from the mouth that the person cannot hold in, nor can they close their mouth, and their tongue is enveloped by their speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it will return to its place through several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 And if it is intact and complete, you must quickly reset it and not delay; and in such a way that the assistant holds the head of the patient, and places his folded hand into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is in two parts; and let the other hand be free to ensure alignment; and command the patient to relax and move their jaws from side to side.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the physician adjusts it evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the returning (of the jaw) is difficult, even if it's both mandibles together, soak them with warm water and oil, until you can gently adjust them; do not delay the adjustment, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they are aligned evenly, and the patient's mouth closes well without difficulty, place dampened bandages soaked in a cerote made of rose oil and wax on it, then bind it lightly with soft ligaments; and let the patient sleep on their back, with their head resting between two pillows, so that it is not moved to the right or left, nor do they make any effort to chew, but eat light food until the pain subsides and the jaws are healed; and then eat whatever they want lightly, and do not struggle to open their mouth to eat and drink, until the jaw is well healed and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaw bones cannot be put back in place at once and are not returned to their proper position, fever and swelling may occur, and perhaps stomach upset, and possibly vomiting of bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, know that it is a critical situation; and many times the person dies, within nine days.
de la forcelle	of the fork/fracture
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fracture cannot come out of alignment along the ribcage and the hip, and when it is dislocated, it can be felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And the restoration is as follows: let the patient lie flat on their back, and stretch out their arms; then press firmly with the palm of your hand, and it will return; then apply the emplaster and bandage, and bind it; and the joint that is dislocated towards the ribs cannot come out; unless it does, in which case reset it to its place, as we have said; then apply the emplaster and bandage, and bind it, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed; and similarly, the shoulder blade is brought back when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 Know that the shoulder does not dislocate in any other way but according to three methods: one of which is when it dislocates at the lower part of the shoulder blade; and the second is at the side of the chest; and perhaps it dislocates above, but this rarely happens; and it never dislocates backwards towards the shoulder blades, nor inwards towards the nerves; and often it dislocates downward towards the shoulder blade, especially for those who have little flesh, for it easily dislocates for them; for those who have enough flesh, it seldom dislocates, and it rarely returns back into place.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And perhaps it happens to some men that they receive a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they believe that it is dislocated because of this.[INT](Note: I will provide you with more lines from the medieval medical treatise as soon as you are ready.)
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you should examine it until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And it is known as a dislocation when it is lowered towards the shoulder blade, and creates a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a clear distinction between them; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a pit, and below the shoulder blade where you touch the top of the shoulder, just like a hole; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his neck, nor move at all; and likewise, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you will find it clearly when you touch it; and this type of dislocation is not difficult to set back in place, when it is recent, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The method is as follows: the assistant raises the patient's hand up high, then places their fingers under the shoulder blade and lifts the joint with force upwards to its proper place. The assistant should then raise the hand, stretch it upwards, and then place it back down. It will quickly return to its normal position.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if it does not come back as we have said before, then the patient should be bathed in warm water; and they should be given a soothing and relaxing ointment, such as a decoction of clary sage, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and applied to them; then the patient should be propped up on their back, and a soft woolen pad placed under the shoulder blade, neither too hard nor too soft, then the physician puts his heel beneath the pad, and raises the top of the shoulder forcefully, and pulls the hand of the sick person; and one assistant holds the head of the patient so that it does not move downward; this shoulder will return immediately, and if you see that they set it back in place in this manner: and it is that you make sure there is a man present who is stronger than the patient; and stand at their side, and push his shoulder blade under the patient's shoulder blade, and raise the shoulder blade upward so that the patient hangs in the air; and another assistant pulls the hand of the patient downward toward the stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too lightweight, have them hold onto something heavy, and the dislocation will return to its place now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 And another way to set it is: insert a long stake into the ground so that the patient's head rests on it like a pillow, not too thick or too thin; then place the patient beneath it with soft blankets underneath and have them lie down with their back against the stake; next, stretch out their arm away from their body and the joint will quickly return to its proper position; and if it still does not want to go back into place despite all that we have mentioned, perform this procedure: take a stake about two arms' lengths long and four fingers wide, with a pointed end that can be inserted deeply beneath the dislocated bone according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then place the soft folded cloth on the patient's head, so that the stick does not harm or poke the patient, then place it under the assle of the patient; and stretch his arm on the long part of the stick, and tie the shoulder to the stick, and the arm to the head of the hand, then place the arm on a rung of a ladder that is wide, and let the hands hang down, and leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint will go back in place now.

And when it is back in place, no matter how, you should then place a roll of wool under the assle, then apply the plaster, prepared with powder from the mill, with incense and egg yolk, all over the shoulder and around, then bind it appropriately under the assle, and turn the bandage over the plaster, and embrace the hand to the neck, and let the hands remain like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he eats little, until the limb feels better, as it will heal faster; and then eat more after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it feels firm and not softened, then it is healed.

And if you do all these things, and it becomes dislocated again after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and the patient cannot lift their arm up, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder have been cut or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.

Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the hip is dislocated by points, and returns by points; it has become dislocated all around, both in front and back, and the dislocation has not been corrected, for it is clearly visible and can be felt; and it becomes dislocated according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the knife to the patient with the (boiling) lard, you can see it clearly.

And it is necessary that you reduce it in such a way that abscesses do not come there, for if abscesses do come there, the reduction will be difficult; and perhaps it cannot be completely reduced at all, especially when it is in the back; this is worse than other dislocations and causes greater pain, and perhaps death comes as a result.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is as follows, when it is in such a state that it can be reduced: stretch out his hand with your two hands; and let his arms be spread apart, and the doctor's hands should be placed around the joint on top of and below, and bring the joint back into place at its grooves or at the base of the palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he bends his hand to his hand, and strikes with the root of the palm the dislocated joint.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 For if it does not want to return to its place, apply strong stretching; and have two people stretch the arm and hold it with two hands so that it does not move during the extension; then bend the arm in each direction after wrapping a long and wide cloth around it; and when the surgeon has aligned the joint with his hand, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then press firmly until it returns to its place; and once it is in its place, apply dry poultice with egg white, and hold it firmly, and bind the arm to the patient's neck, leaving it for several days before releasing it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then loosen the binding and let it be. But if you see that the joint is not fitting well, then reapply the ointment and binding, and leave it like this for several days, until it is firmly set; then loosen it.[Notes: "si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien" means to reapply the ointment and binding. "ensi" means in this way.][Read More: Medieval medical treatments often involved a combination of herbs, oils, and other substances, applied as poultices or plasters to the affected area. These treatments could be left on for several days, or even weeks, depending on the severity of the injury or illness being treated. Here's more information on medieval medical treatments: <https://www.britannica.com/topic/Western-medicine/Medieval-Western-medicine>]
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition. li dislocation de la main	hand dislocation
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut. And the resetting is as follows: place the affected hand on a table, extend your hand, and the surgeon aligns it so that he places his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes until it returns to its place; however, you must make sure that it is in the correct position; then, have the patient place the back of his hand on a table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it returns now, that is good. If not, bind it with soothing plasters for abscesses, and leave it like that without reopening it.

Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.
