de la dislocation des dois de la main	of finger dislocation
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 Sometimes the fingers of the hand dislocate on each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or the belly; then stretch out the finger, and push the dislocation towards its knuckles until it returns, then hold the finger's head and bend it towards the side where it is disjoined; and leave it for 2 days, and then straighten it that day; and bind it at night, as we have said, and unbind it during the day, and make it move, and rebind it at night; and do this frequently, until it becomes tight, and similarly do if it is dislocated on the palm side of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and similarly do when it is dislocated from the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Here is a possible translation:
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the back or neck is dislocated in multiple places, there is no cure, for death quickly seizes the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 And the signs are that stools leave suddenly without voluntary control, and cannot be held back, and often certain limbs become weak, or both thighs or both arms or one, and often the hips move in four ways; the one that moves at the back is called "gilbositez": the cure is to check if "gilbositez" has come from childhood: if it has, there is no cure or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And the one that comes from falling or being struck or similar things, the ancient methods of cures say with grand words that it is not beneficial in all cases; but I have shortened it according to my intention and have made instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 I say that in the swelling that comes to the front of the breast, there is no engine or health; and also that which comes directly in two sides, and cannot be cured unless it is properly the one that comes to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient is stretched out on his face evenly, and has support beneath him, so that he does not hurt himself; then stick one stake firmly in the ground at the head, and another at the feet, and tie a rope underneath the patient's heels, and another around his calves, and knees, and ankles; and two assistants know the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two stakes; and they are well tightened, the stakes as we have said, and the assistant places his palms on the spine very firmly, until it recovers.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if it does not return to its place with this treatment, take a board of three arms length, and prop it up under the patient, and have the patient lie on their side, and put the head of the board under the opening, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and have the nurse place her feet on the other end of the board and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you wish, do it with a device that turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And have two pegs driven into the patient's head, one arm's length long, and two others towards the feet, and have between each peg, underneath, a palm's space in length; and have in each peg one hole, where the device turns, and have the pegs firmly planted in the ground so that they do not move; and between each pair of pegs have one turning peg, on which the ropes turn, and have two small pegs, one palm's length long, to turn the device; and then tie the rope that is between the ashes to the device towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet at the other device, and each of the assistants turns his device at the entire rope, and the master adjusts the spine evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 And when it is aligned, place a desiccating emplaster with plenty of egg yolk on it, then the wadding, then an elongated stylet of three finger-widths long, which reaches the area of the gelatinous tissue and the healthy part of the shoulder blade, then bind it with a bandage as we have said, and have the patient use gentle exercise until it is healed; and if any issue arises at the end of the healing process, laxative and soothing medicines should be administered, along with the stylet mentioned before; and sometimes a piece of wood is administered, and sometimes an abscess appears in the back spine of the back, and it is thought to be a dislocation; but it is the bone that protrudes, for which one should not make assumptions: perhaps it could bring about death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and shoulder do not come out of place except for dislocations only, and they do not come out as other joints do; and the joint of the hip is dislocated in four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and more on the inside than elsewhere, and little displaced in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the recognition of its dislocation inside is that when you join the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the sick knee appears higher than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot bend their knee by the fire; and the place which is beside swollen due to an abscess is warm, because the hip comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that which comes to the defective one, is that these accidents are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of one for whom it happens in front, is that he stretches his leg according to its fullness; yet, he does not bend the knee without pain, and if one wants him to walk, he cannot move forward, and he holds his urine, and his ankle swells, and when he walks, he steps on his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of one for whom it happens behind, is that he cannot stretch or bend his knee, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and his ankle is softened, and the head of his thigh is near his side by his ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The reduction of this type of dislocation is that you should examine if the dislocation is old and remains in its position, then there is no cure for it; and one should not be hasty to act.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for the one for whom the dislocation is fresh, and it is of the four types of dislocation, you should act quickly to return the joint and stretch it inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return to its place and not require any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And if it does not return in this manner, then you should prepare and strongly support, holding the leg with two hands, or with a ligament tied above the knee; and another assistant extends his hand above in such a way that he pushes his hands beneath its haunches, then tightly binds him with a gentle ligament on the thigh; and another holds the end of the ligament; and they all stretch up and down at once, so that the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of stretching is common to four similar cases, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, that is good.[Translate request repeated 3 times]
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 Or if not, care must be taken with its likeness when the dislocation is on the outside, you should turn the patient onto his healthy side, then place the ligament on the root of the thigh, and the loin that is beneath the groin, then stretch the ligament up towards the groin, and towards the loin; then another assistant takes his arms, and strongly embraces the large loin of the affected thigh, and stretches it far outwards: now it will return to its place; and this method of dislocation is easier than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 And if you cannot fasten it in this manner as we have said, then you should tie the patient's two feet together with a strong but soft ligament at the heels and knees, and let the affected leg be extended two fingers more than the other; then let him hang from a beam above his head, and let there be two arms length from the ground; then command a minister to embrace the hip's head, and let there be another minister hanging with the patient, who firmly embraces the thigh, for the joints return quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 And when the dislocation is outside, let the patient lie down as we have said in the one with gout, and tighten the ligament on the affected leg properly, and on the belly as well; then place two sticks, one at the head and one at the feet, then insert one stick between the patient's thighs in a straight manner; and have plenty of moist towels around it so that it does not wound the patient, then let each minister stretch out towards him, and let the surgeon put his hand evenly on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, place it on top (i.e., table) and press it as we have said in gilbosité, and let the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, one should quickly stretch out the affected leg as I have said, and the surgeon should make an effort to be over the affected ankle, then press with his other hand and pull downwards towards the knee.[The text seems to be describing a specific maneuver for reducing a dislocated joint, possibly of the lower extremity. The surgeon is instructed to position themselves strategically and apply pressure and traction to help guide the joint back into its proper alignment.]
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And if the dislocation is outward, it should not be stretched downwards or lifted up from the ground. Instead, the patient should be in the same position as if the hip was dislocated outwardly, just like we have said about lying on both hips; and let him lie on his back, and stretch the limbs as we have said before, and press on the joint against the table. It will be enough when the patient stretches his legs and they are even. Then adjust the thighs, apply the plaster, and bind it with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and let him rest for three or four days, then loosen it and apply the plaster again. If you see that they are even, bind it as before, and let it rest for three days; then loosen it and make him walk gently until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee.
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee can become dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inward and outward, and backward; but it does not become dislocated in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg to his thigh, and if it does not reach his thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such [dislocations] is that you make the patient sit upright, extend his leg if he can, and place your back against his abdomen, and place his foot on your feet; then take his knee with your palms, and pull between your hands, then strongly bend the two sides of the knee; and another servant extends his foot, so that the knee comes back to its place, and the sign is that it easily reaches his thigh; and apply the poultice, and bind the leg to the thigh, and keep them together firmly for three or four days, then loosen [the binding]; and the patient should not at all move or go anywhere, until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not healthy, apply strong and extensive stretching, as we have said in the treatment of inflammation, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes dislocated and sometimes completely misaligned, both internally and externally.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 And the sign is that the ankle is swollen and protrudes at the part where it is dislocated: the reduction is easy, and one should gently stretch it with their hands when it is moved slightly.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is dislocated completely, you should make the patient sit upright, and hold them by the leg above the ankle with both hands; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards and place the foot in its proper position; do this twice as we have said, pulling and stretching the foot; if it returns, that's good; if not, start the process again, for it will return; and if it cannot return like this, make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and firmly plant a stake in the ground between their thighs and tie a cloth around so as not to injure the patient; then hold the thigh with one hand and another minister stretches the healthy foot with hands or a ligature tied around the shin bone; then each minister pulls evenly, and the stake should be firmly placed between the patient's thighs to keep them in place when stretched; then the physician places the dislocation with their hands, and another minister holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And when it is ready, put the poultice and wadding on, and bind it firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are above the heel, so that the bandage is not too tight; then leave it for 2 or 3 days, and if the binding loosens, bind it again; then untie it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient to walk for 4 days; and if he goes before this term, it is not certain that he will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come from it, you should soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of the hands
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the hand is dislocated, you should stretch it out nicely without force, and this is an easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the dislocation is in any joint of the foot, you should have the patient sit upright on a level surface or on a table, and place your foot on the visible part of the joints, then press firmly on your foot until it returns to normal; and when it is aligned and there is nothing apparent, place a two-chambered board under the sole of the foot, then bind it firmly and leave it for 3 days, then untie it; and let it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When there is a wound with a dislocation, and one wants to reset it, it often happens that the patient dies; therefore, do not be presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and slow, not hasty; and use soothing hot poultices at the beginning for an abscess, and leave the patient in God's hand if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, so that the abscess comes to a head; and when the limb is in place, then administer soothing hot poultices, and treat the wound as it should be, with drying ointments; and if there is a fracture with the dislocation, and small bones are separated, then remove them, and do what we have said in simple maladies; and beware of entering the path of fear, as I have said, for this will harm you according to your Creator, and for the safety of your art and body.
Amen	 Amen
